# **WOKE UP FALLING DOWN**

---

## **INT. BACKSTAGE GREEN ROOM – GIANTS STADIUM – NIGHT ONE – SEPTEMBER 2000**

The band is mid-prep. The room buzzes with the tension of *80,000 ravenous fans* pounding their feet outside. A muted roar bleeds through the concrete.  [[4.5 KATHY ESPICH character bible|Kathy]] is warming up her voice. [[4.6 JEREMY EVANS character bible|Jeremy]] is running scales. [[4.1 BILL DAVENPORT character bible|Bill]] is deep in the gear rack, fiddling with an effects board. Jeff is tuning—again. Always tuning.

And JIM?  [[4.4 JIM BROWN character bible|Jim]] fucking *bursts* through the side door like he just snorted lightning.

**JIM** (gleeful, bouncing on his heels)  
Okay okay okay okay listen up! I’ve had a vision. A *revelation*. Like a drumstick straight from God’s own kit. We’re blowing up the setlist. *Tonight*.

**[[4.3 JEFF EVANS character bible|JEFF]]** (pausing mid-pluck)  
Blowing up how, exactly?

**JIM**  (grinning like he robbed a meth lab)  
Track three becomes track TWO tonight. “*[[11.1.3 Not Taken Kindly|Not Taken Kindly]]*” kicks it off. No intro tape, no lights down. Kathy just *howls* that first line cold and we *blast* them.

**KATHY** (stares)  
You want me to open a stadium show with a blowjob lyric?

**JIM** (arms wide like Moses parting the Red Sea)  
EXACTLY. It’s raw. It’s primal. It’s anti-spectacle as *spectacle*. We hit them before they even know the lights are down. No intro, no fanfare, no polite warm-up. Just—*boom*—you’re in hell now, motherfuckers!

**BILL** (sipping Gatorade)  
You *do* remember the mayor of New York is in the audience, right?

**JIM** (grinning even wider)  
Perfect. Let him hear Kathy say “licking up his shaft” at 140 decibels. That’s culture, baby.

**JEFF**  
You’re out of your mind.

**JIM**  
Correct. And that’s *why* this is going to work. We don’t give them a *show* tonight. We give them a *hostage situation* with rhythm and bass.

**KATHY**  (sighs, then smirks)  
If we’re doing this, I want flames. Literal pyro. Let me spit fire before the first verse.

**JIM**  
FUCK YES. I knew you’d get it. I already talked to Pyro Mike.

**BILL** (stares, blinking)  
When did you talk to Pyro Mike?

**JIM**  
About fifteen minutes ago while you were tuning the subharmonics on that arpeggiator thingy.

**JEFF**  
It's a modular polysynth.

**JIM**  
Whatever. We're starting this set like a riot in a strip club. And by the third song? We drop *“[[11.1.6 The Left Hand|The Left Hand]].”* No intro. No speech. Just Kathy and a blood-red spotlight.

**KATHY**  (still smirking)  
You son of a bitch. That might actually work.

**JEFF**  
If we crash and burn, it’s on your ass, Jim.

**JIM**  
Deal. But if we *kill*? If we blow the stadium’s *soul* out through its own eyes? Then we *never* play it safe again.

*Beat.*

They all glance at each other. Even Jeff’s jaw clenches with something between anxiety and adrenaline.

**BILL** (sotto, to Jeff)  
I swear to God, if he’s right again, I’m gonna start a religion around him.

**JEFF**  
He’s right about once a decade. It’s… about that time.

**KATHY** (grabbing her mic)  
Let’s open a tesseract. Fuck it.

---

## **INT. BACKSTAGE – GIANTS STADIUM – NIGHT ONE – SEPTEMBER 2000**

The walls *vibrate* from the sound of 80,000 lunatics screaming “COMMUTED” in waves. The band is huddled around a scuffed folding table stacked with half-eaten catering and empty Red Bull cans.

**JIM** (like a kid who just broke into the fireworks shed)  
Alright. Opening the set with “Not Taken Kindly”—but. BUT. We don’t start cold. We don’t just kick it off.

**KATHY** (skeptical)  
Okay…?

**JIM**  
We start with *Woke Up This Morning*. Like, full-on Alabama 3-style intro. A two-minute groove. Smoke machines. Slow-burn. I want that bassline to feel like sin crawling up your spine.

**KATHY**  
The theme song to *The Sopranos*?

**JEFF** (deadpan, livid)  
Jim. Do you realize we got 80,000 people out there screaming our names and you want to wing it on a *TV show theme song*?

**JIM** (arms raised like he’s conjuring demons)  
It’s not a theme song. It’s a *ritual*. It’s Jersey. It’s *now*. They will eat it up.

**[[4.2 JEREMY GILLEY character bible|GILLEY]]** (barging in, eyes lit with unholy confidence)  
Jeff, shut the fuck up. Jim’s *exactly* right.

Everyone turns to look at Gilley. He’s amped, practically vibrating.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
It’s not a theme song. *It’s New Jersey*. These people don’t give a shit if we butcher a gospel hymn—as long as we *nod to the state*, they’ll jump out of the second deck before we’re halfway through the first chorus.

**JEFF**  
And what, you’re just gonna *sing* it? You know the words?

**GILLEY**  
No, I *don’t* know the words. I need the lyrics.

(he turns, yelling like the world is on fire)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
I will need the lyrics. I NEED THE LYRICS *RIGHT THE GODDAMN NOW*. SOMEBODY GET ME THE FUCKING LYRICS!!

*Chaos erupts.*

A tech scrambles. A roadie shouts into a walkie. Kathy’s doubled over laughing. Bill’s already flipping switches on his sampler.

**JIM** (to Gilley, handing him a mic)  
You got two minutes. We loop the riff. You channel Tony Soprano like he’s your spiritual advisor.

**GILLEY** (smiling like a man about to rob a casino)  
Nah, I *am* Tony Soprano.

**KATHY**  
Great. And I’m Carmela with a Glock in her garter. Let’s burn this place down.

---

## **INT. BACKSTAGE – GIANTS STADIUM – SECONDS LATER**

**JEREMY** (leans against a stack of amps, deadpan)  
I’ve never pegged Kathy as Carmela. Maybe Adriana. Maybe Gloria. *Not* Carmela.

**JEFF** (snorts, laughing)  
Carmela with a Glock, man. What kind of fan fiction are we writing back here?

**KATHY** (staring daggers at both of them)  
Say *one* more word and I’ll make you both Carmela’s next goddamn alimony payments.

**CREMEANS** (clapping his hands, sharp)  
Keep it together, people! Maybe we can stretch this intro another two, maybe *three* minutes, but the crowd outside is going *feral*. They haven't resorted to human sacrifice yet, but it’s *imminent*\!

**JIM**  (grinning)  
If they start burning effigies, I want a front row seat.

**KATHY**(whirling around)  
We need *Wardrobe*. Someone find *Wardrobe*\! We need Gilley to look like a mobster *right the hell now*. Where’s a leather trench coat and a pinky ring when you *actually fucking need them?\!*

**GILLEY** (spins around dramatically)  
Do I look like a man who *keeps track of his own wardrobe?* This is linen from 1996. It smells like Marlboro Reds and expired cooch.

**CREMEANS** (yelling toward the corridor)  
CONNIE?! WHERE IS WARDROBE?! THIS IS NOT A DRILL, WOMAN!

A frazzled WARDROBE ASSISTANT skids around the corner with a rack of half-sorted outfits.

**WARDROBE ASSISTANT**  
What?! Who died?!

**KATHY** (nodding at Gilley)  
Nobody yet. But if he walks out there looking like a barefoot yacht bartender, we *all* will.

**WARDROBE ASSISTANT** (pulling jackets like a DJ scratching vinyl)  
Alright, alright—black suit, gold chain, sunglasses, no shirt. Trust me.

**GILLEY** (grabbing the chain and popping his collar)  
*Bada bing*, motherfuckers.

**JEFF** (still laughing)  
If this works, I’m writing a book about it. If it doesn’t, I’m testifying at the trial.

**CREMEANS** (urgent, now pacing)  
T-minus 60 seconds. Crowd's chanting like it’s a cult ceremony. I just saw a guy eat a *foam finger* whole.

**JIM** (strapping in behind the drums)  
Then let’s go full pagan. Hit the riff.

**BILL** (flipping on the synth)  
Smoke’s cued. Light rig’s red and gold. We're Jersey now.

**KATHY** (into the mic, smirking)  
This one’s for Tony. And Carmela. And the bodies buried in the Meadowlands.

*They lock eyes. Showtime.*

---

## **EXT. GIANTS STADIUM – NIGHT ONE – SECONDS BEFORE SHOWTIME**

The lights don’t drop.  The house music doesn’t fade.  There’s no warning. Just a *rumble*.  The kind of sub-bass that makes your sternum beg for red-hot chili peppers.  Then smoke starts billowing across the stage—red and gold, lit like the backroom of a Newark steakhouse on fire.  

A *familiar* guitar riff slithers out of the speakers.  But… it’s not Commuted.  Not exactly.  The [*Alabama 3* groove](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mJpNmYeooQE) slinks through the air like it doesn’t need permission to be there.

---

## **INT. GIANTS STADIUM – STAGE LEVEL – CONTINUOUS**

The *crowd* is instantly confused. The energy shifts—*just slightly*—from pure euphoria to… curiosity. And then suspicion.  They know this.  They know this beat.  They know those chords.  And when GILLEY steps out? They lose their *fucking minds*.  Not because he’s here.  Because he looks *wrong*.  Gilley, normally draped in 1980s pastel swagger, is now rocking a tailored black jacket, silk burgundy shirt (unbuttoned to somewhere near the Vatican), sunglasses despite the night, and a *gold chain so thick it could tow a truck*. He’s slicked back like he’s about to whack somebody or close on a car dealership in Bayonne.

### **CROWD REACTION – VARIOUS CUTS**

**FAN #1** (yelling over the noise)  
Why does he look like he’s gonna sell me insurance and threaten my family?

**FAN #2** (screaming)  
IS THIS SOPRANOS?! WHAT THE FUCK IS GOING ON?! I LOVE IT!!

**FAN #3** (eyes wide)  
They’re *starting* with this?! We’re not surviving this show.

### **STAGE – MOMENTS LATER**

**GILLEY** (grabs the mic, smooth as sin)  
*Woke up this mornin’…*  
*Got yourself a gun…*

*The crowd erupts*.  The second deck starts shaking. *Literally*. Jersey hears itself in this moment.

**JEFF** (stepping to his monitor, turning to Jim)  
Do it, Jim. *Kick it.*

**JIM** (grinning like he invented crime)  
*Oh, I’m gonna fucking kick it.*

He *slams* into the transition beat. The whole band drops into the “*Woke Up This Morning*” groove for a full 90 seconds—then the tempo shifts, *lurches*, and *snaps* into the opening notes of **"Not Taken Kindly."**

The moment Kathy’s voice comes in?

***“Licking up his shaft…”***

Eighty thousand people collectively scream, laugh, lose control, and realize:  This isn’t just a concert.  It’s a *heist*.

---

## **INT. GIANTS STADIUM – DRESSING ROOM – NIGHT ONE – POST-SHOW**

It’s been three hours.

Three unhinged, hypnotic, *hallucinatory* hours.  The crowd got everything and then five more songs they weren’t supposed to.  No one’s sure how it ended.  They just know **“[[11.1.21 Come Inside Me|Come Inside Me]]”** *didn’t* close it.  Which means the *universe might actually be broken now.*  The band collapses into the dressing room like fallen gods.

**JEFF** (half-laughing, half-dead)  
Did anybody check the seismic data?  Can we confirm if that registered in Edison?  On the *Richter scale*?

**JIM** (slumped on the floor, shirt gone, eyes wild)  
If it didn’t, we go back out there and *fix it*.

**BILL** (muttering from the couch, eyes closed)  
No. No more notes. No more sound. I’m a puddle of synth and regret.

**KATHY** (pacing, drenched in sweat, eyeliner halfway to her neck)  
We just fed 80,000 people pure chaos with a side of bloodlust and didn’t even give them the safe word!  They’re gonna need therapy.

**GILLEY** (leans against the wall, chain still swinging, shirt fully unbuttoned)  
Therapy?  We gave them *faith*.  That wasn’t a concert. That was *church with felonies*.

**JEFF** (grabbing a Gatorade, collapses into a chair)  
I can’t feel my legs.  Or my brain.  God it hurts. What the *fuck* did we just do?

**[[5.2. JEFF CREMEANS MODERN REVIEW|CREMEANS]]** (pokes head in, clipboard in hand, pale and rattled)  
You *improvised* an encore. You *skipped* the closer. You made *eye contact* with a security guard who pissed himself during “*Sin and Death*.”  Congratulations.  The fire marshal may want to speak to you about the *second deck*.

**JIM** (grins, still sprawled on the floor)  
Tell him to bring a drink and a lawyer.

**KATHY** (flopping down beside Jeff)  
Can we never open with a Sopranos cover again?

**GILLEY** (smiling through the sweat)  
Are you kidding?  That’s how we *open every Jersey show* from now on.  We’re a *fucking religion* now.

**BILL** (eyes still shut)  
Yeah? Then I’m declaring myself the Pope of feedback and holy distortion.

**JEFF** (grinning through the exhaustion)  
Then write that into the Book of Setlists, chapter one:  *And lo, the bass did quake, and the people did shake, and the second deck did sway like a drunken prophet…*

*Beat.*

The room is quiet, but alive. The kind of stillness that only comes *after a storm*.  They’re drained.  But *charged*.  Wrecked.  But more *them* than they’ve ever been.

**CREMEANS** (deadpan, flipping through notes)  
Night two’s in 21 hours.  I suggest hydration.  And possibly an exorcism.

*Laughter. Real. Rough. Earned.*

---

## **INT. GIANTS STADIUM – DRESSING ROOM – LATER THAT NIGHT**

They’re still buzzing—sweaty, ruined, high on the aftermath.

**GILLEY** (sipping whiskey from a plastic cup, pacing like he’s onstage again)  
Alright, so here’s the deal: if we ever do a show in Jersey again—and *you know* we will—we open *that way*.  *Woke Up This Morning*. Blood-red lights. Total surprise.  Because *that*… is *us*.  Uniquely *Jersey*, uniquely *Commuted*.

(he turns, eyes locking on Jim)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
*This*, my friend… Mr. Jim Brown… is why I like you.  And why I’ve *always* liked you.

(beat)
You got any more bright ideas, or did you spend it all on HBO homage and stage terrorism?

**JIM** (leans up slowly, voice low and smug as hell)  
Well, we *are* in Jersey…right?

**GILLEY** (mock suspense)  
I’m listening…

**JIM**  
Who owns Jersey?

**ALL** (in unison, already knowing)  
*The Boss.*

**JIM**  
Exactly.  So why don’t we do it right?  Tomorrow night…we *don’t* roll into our opener.  We *explode* into it.

(he stands now, grinning, daring)
We come out swinging with *Born to Run*, fuckers.

**JEFF** (choking on his drink)  
What—*WHAT*?!

**KATHY** (laughing so hard she wheezes)  
Jim. Jimmy. That’s sacrilege.

**JIM**  
No. That’s *paying tribute*.  We’re not stealing from Bruce.  We’re *borrowing money* from the E Street Band.  With interest.

**BILL** (genuinely intrigued)  
We cover it straight or tear it apart?

**JIM**  
We rip it to shreds. Rebuild it with synths and rage and *whatever the hell that thing is* you play during “Sin and Death,” Bill.

**GILLEY** (grinning wide, pacing again)  
You mean the demon church organ?  Perfect.

**JEFF**  
I’m not saying yes. I’m saying if we do this, we better do it *right*.

**KATHY** (serious now, eyes narrowing)  
Then we better rehearse.  Because if we screw up *The Boss* in his own backyard…we’ll need *witness protection*.

**CREMEANS** (from the doorway, exasperated)  
If you dorks try to out-Bruce Bruce, I want hazard pay.  And backup choir insurance.

**GILLEY** (grinning like a man who just robbed a cathedral)  
Oh, it’s happening.  We’re *Commuted*.  We don’t just play shows.  We *commit felonies in four-four time.*

*Beat.*

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
Now someone go find Clarence Clemons’ ghost and ask him for his blessing.

---

## **INT. HOTEL LOBBY – EARLY MORNING – NEXT DAY**

**CREMEANS** is hunched over his laptop at a hotel business center kiosk, muttering to himself like a man negotiating with the devil.  He’s got Real Media Player playing, a crumpled hotel napkin with names of rehearsal studios scrawled in Sharpie, and a *burning sense of dread*.

**CREMEANS** (to himself, gritted teeth)  
You want to cover *Born to Run*… in *New Jersey*… without *practice*…?  Are you *trying* to get us whacked?

(he dials a number, holding the phone with his shoulder while pounding keys)

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)** (into phone)  
Hi—yes—do you have a rehearsal space available today? No?  Okay. Thank you.  

(sotto)  
Rot in hell.

(he hangs up. Dials another.)

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**  (into phone)  
Staten Island? That’s practically the countryside. I’ll pay double—triple.  No, we don’t need catering.  We need *soundproofing* and legal deniability.  

(beat)  
You got a room? YES. Book it. Name's Cremeans. Don't ask who for.

### **INT. ELEVATOR – SECONDS LATER**

**CREMEANS** slams the call button like he’s about to defuse a bomb.  He’s on the phone again, walking fast, headset jammed in one ear.

**CREMEANS** (into phone)  
Okay, here’s the deal—Staten Island. Studio’s called **Castle Tone**. Hour and a half from here if traffic doesn’t try to assassinate us.  I already wired the guy an amount of money that technically qualifies as hush money.

**JEFF (O.S.)** (from behind, approaching with a coffee and zero shame)  
Are you scheduling our criminal trial or a rehearsal?

**CREMEANS** (glancing back, exasperated)  
*Both.*

**KATHY (O.S.)** (pulling on sunglasses, clearly hungover)  
Staten Island? Jesus. What is this, a *banishment*?

**CREMEANS** (dead serious)  
It’s the closest rehearsal space in the tri-state area where  Springsteen doesn’t *own a cousin*.

(he turns, deadly calm)

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**  
Do you want to rehearse this in Jersey, have it leak, and get *concrete shoes* in the Raritan River?  No?  Then shut up and pack your gear.

### **INT. HOTEL ROOM – CUTAWAY – MOMENTS LATER**

JIM is stuffing sticks into his case, humming “Born to Run” off-key like a man invoking the name of a saint with sacrilegious joy.

**JIM**  (to himself)  
This is either going to make us legends… or get us sued into the *afterlife.*

---

## **INT. RENTED VAN – LATE MORNING – EN ROUTE TO STATEN ISLAND**

The van rattles down the Jersey Turnpike, stuffed with gear, coffee cups, and regret. Kathy’s passed out against the window in dark sunglasses. Bill’s trying to fix the EQ on a Bluetooth speaker. Jim’s tapping his thighs like a human click track. Cremeans is driving like a man who’s had three stress-induced heart attacks since breakfast.

**JEFF** (from the back seat, staring out the window)  
You know, the more we drive into Staten Island…the more it just feels like *North Jersey with yellow and blue license plates.*

**JIM**  (grinning)  
Don’t say that too loud. They’ll revoke your right to a bacon egg and cheese.

**BILL**  (flatly)  
It’s like if Jersey and Long Island had a kid and raised it on diesel fumes and zoning violations.

**KATHY** (mumbling without opening her eyes)  
That kid plays lacrosse, owns four knives, and says “bro” as a comma.

**CREMEANS** (white-knuckling the steering wheel)  
Do you all want to *live* long enough to *rehearse this song*, or should I just drive us off the Bayonne Bridge now?

**JEFF** (sips his coffee)  
Not gonna lie. Dying before we butcher *Born to Run* on Bruce’s turf might actually be the dignified way out.

**JIM** (gleeful)  
No dignity left, brother. We cashed that in the second Gilley screamed “GET ME THE FUCKING LYRICS.”

**KATHY** (sitting up slowly)  
I swear to god, if we run into an actual Springsteen while we’re rehearsing this, I’m faking my own death.

**CREMEANS** (sighs)  
You’ll be lucky if we don’t run into one of his *drummers*.

---

## **INT. CASTLE TONE REHEARSAL STUDIO – STATEN ISLAND – EARLY AFTERNOON**

The room smells like warm amp tubes and three decades of spilled Red Bull. The band is surrounded by mismatched gear, foam paneling, and a whiteboard with “NO SWEARING IN THE LOBBY” hastily scribbled on it.

Jeremy is staring down the *arrangement chart* for “Born to Run” like it’s a map of a minefield.

**JEREMY** (pointing with a marker)  
Okay. Look. We’ve got a *very sticky* problem here.  We don’t have a horn player.  And you know what part *isn’t optional* in this song?

**KATHY** (half-serious)  
The sax solo that sounds like America crying while getting a speeding ticket?

**BILL** (nods solemnly)  
Clarence Clemons is not a vibe. He’s a *pillar*.

**JIM** (grabbing his sticks)  
Unless one of you suddenly learned to play tenor sax in the last five hours, we’re going into this *half-dressed at a wedding*.

*Silence. Heavy. Awkward. And then—*

**GILLEY** (perking up, raising a finger like he just solved world hunger)  
What if…instead of horns…I play the solo on *harmonica*?

*Beat. All heads slowly swivel toward him.*

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  (grinning like a man with zero business offering this)  
I can play a note on harmonica.  Probably *two*, if I practice.

(he pulls a *beat-up Hohner* from his pocket like it’s a sidearm)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
C’mon. What do you think, guys?

**JEFF** (blinking)  
Gilley, the last time you played that harmonica was at a Waffle House in Mobile after six shots of Wild Turkey and a dare.

**GILLEY** (grinning wider)  
Yeah, and I *crushed it*. That waitress *wept*, Jeff.

**KATHY**  (sighs, rubbing her eyes)  
Gilley. That’s like saying you can fly a 747 because you once won a game of Flight Simulator drunk.

**JIM** (stretching)  
Actually…a distorted, blown-out harmonica in the right key? That might sound kind of badass. Dirty. Raw. Jersey *garage gospel*.

**BILL** (skeptical)  
It could also sound like a car alarm with a head cold.

**GILLEY** (pacing now, possessed)  
Guys. *Listen to me.*  Springsteen sings about working-class grit, blue-collar pain, escape velocity from heartbreak and gas stations.  Nothing says that better than a harmonica that sounds like it’s been through *divorce court*.

**JEFF** (staring off into space)  
I cannot believe we’re about to deface “Born to Run” with *DIY Bruce cosplay and a $14 harmonica* from Guitar Center.

**KATHY** (sits on an amp, shrugs)  
It’s either the worst idea we’ve ever had…or the most honest tribute Jersey’s ever seen.

**GILLEY** (clapping his hands)  
Let’s find out which it is, baby!

---

## **INT. CASTLE TONE STUDIO – REHEARSAL ROOM – MINUTES LATER**

Gilley’s standing there with the harmonica like it’s Excalibur and he’s *just barely qualified* to wield it. The rest of the band stares, somewhere between disbelief and curiosity.

**JIM** (slowly nodding, tapping a beat on his thigh)  
You know what?

(beat)
That’s actually a *great* idea.

**JEFF** (stares like he’s watching a man admit to liking *room temperature sushi*)  
Jim.

**JIM**  
Hear me out.

(he stands, gesturing with one drumstick like a philosophy professor in a biker bar)

**JIM (CONT’D)**  
We’re from the *Midwest*, right?  That’s our foundation. That’s our blood. But we’ve got *East Coast bones*—New York noise, Jersey soul.  We’ve got *Southern muscle*—a little Nashville, a lotta Memphis. Hell, Kathy’s vocals sound like Kentucky bourbon on fire. So why not take *Born to Run*—which is already American as hell—and *dip it in the blues*?

**KATHY** (half-laughing, half-intrigued)  
So what, we’re doing Bruce by way of *Chicago and Clarksdale*?

**JIM**  
Exactly. Give it a little dirt. A little growl.  Let the harmonica sound like it just crawled out of a Mississippi ditch and hitchhiked to a Jersey diner.

**BILL** (musing aloud)  
So we’re rebuilding it like a Delta blues anthem hijacked by an 80s synth band…inside a garage…next to a barbecue.

**GILLEY** (grinning ear to ear)  
Now *that’s* a fucking concept.

**JEFF** (grudgingly, nodding)  
If this works…it’ll work *because* we didn’t try to be Bruce.  We just tried to be *us*.

**JIM** (tapping out a slow, swampy rhythm on the snare)  
Right. Not a copy. Not a cover.  A *tribute*. Midwest boys, channeling the Boss through *grit and gospel*.  Chicago. Memphis. Jersey. All in one.

*Beat.*

**KATHY** (grinning and sinning)  
Alright, Boss Babies. Let’s see if we can make this thing *walk like a sinner and howl like a saint.*

**GILLEY** (raising the harmonica to his lips like it’s a weapon)  
Stand back. I’m about to blow some *Bruce Mississippian Delta heat*.

---

## **INT. CASTLE TONE STUDIO – CONTINUOUS**

The band is still buzzing off Jim’s “Memphis-meets-Jersey” sermon. Gilley’s holding the harmonica like he’s about to baptize it in whiskey. Jeff is tuning. Bill’s already lost in synth patch menus. **KATHY** folds her arms. Not pissed—just *firm*. She steps toward Jim with that look she uses when she wants answers and not *theoretical vibes*.

**KATHY**  
Alright, preacher man.  What’s your vision *for me* in this mess?

*Everything stops. Even the harmonica holds its breath.*

**KATHY (CONT’D)**  
Piano and vocals. That’s my lane.  I’m not dragging a tambourine across the floor. I’m not moaning into a harmonica mic.  If we’re doing this, I need to know where I *fit*.  Because I’m *not* stepping outside the framework. Period.

**JIM** (nods, no ego, all respect)  
Fair.

(he walks a slow half-circle around the keyboard rig, hands tucked under his arms like he’s thinking through a chess move)

**JIM (CONT’D)**  
You *open* it.

**KATHY** (eyebrow raised)  
With what?

**JIM**  
Just you.  Just that worn-in upright tone you love—dusty, a little dissonant.  You hit those chords like you mean to *confess* something.

(beat)
You hold the song by the throat, and *then* Gilley slides in with the harmonica.  He doesn’t lead. You *lead*.  Vocals come in slow—low. Like smoke under a locked door.  No roar. No Broadway belting.  You haunt the room.

**KATHY** (crosses arms tighter, skeptical but intrigued)  
You want me to start *Born to Run* like it’s a funeral dirge?

**JIM** (smiles faintly)  
Like it’s a *resurrection*.

*Beat. Kathy tilts her head. Still guarded, but the gears are turning.*

**KATHY**  
No crescendos unless I say so.

**JIM**  
Only when you say so.

**KATHY**  
I want my mic dry. No reverb until the bridge.

**JIM**  
Done.

**KATHY**  
And if anyone talks over my piano intro, I will *break their fucking fingers*.

**JEFF** (sipping coffee, not even looking up)  
Fair warning, guys!

**GILLEY** (quietly, sincere)  
No one’s talking. We’re *listening*.

*Kathy finally exhales. Just a hair. That’s a yes.*

---

## **INT. CASTLE TONE STUDIO – MINUTES LATER**

The room is silent now. No jokes. No quips. Just *tension*. The kind that smells like sweat and legacy.

**KATHY** slides onto the piano bench like a gunfighter settling into her holster.

**JEFF** adjusts his strap with the calm of a surgeon. BILL dials in a synth pad that sounds like distant thunder. JIM is locked in behind the kit, mallets ready. GILLEY stands still, harmonica in one hand, mic in the other, for once not running his mouth.

**KATHY** places her fingers on the keys—no flourish, no warm-up.  And then—*she plays*.  Slow. Hollow. Beautiful.  The opening chords of “*Born to Run*,” not as anthem but as *eulogy*.  Like Springsteen crawled out of a gospel tent during a blackout.

Three measures in, **JIM** lays in a heartbeat—just the kick, muted.  *Thump. Thump.*  
Like a body dragging itself off the mat.

**GILLEY** raises the harmonica. Waits. Breathes.  Then: a long, trembling note. Raw. Crooked. *Perfectly broken.*

**JEFF** joins—low, pulsing bass.  **BILL** swells in, whispering atmosphere beneath it all like a storm coming in sideways.

And KATHY sings.  Low. Controlled.  Like she’s daring the song to defy her.

*In the day we sweat it out in the streets of a runaway American dream…*

Not triumphant. Not defiant.  *Reckoning.* And in that moment? There’s no Springsteen. No Clarence. No Jersey bar band myth.  Just *them*.

**Commuted.**

Rebuilding one of the greatest songs in American history like it’s a transmission from the edge of the country.  Let them try?  They *are* trying.

And they’re not the best band in the world for nothing.

---

## **INT. CASTLE TONE STUDIO – “BORN TO RUN” REHEARSAL – FINAL BRIDGE**

KATHY’S voice is trembling now—not from weakness, but from *tension held too long*. The band’s been walking a tightrope of restraint for three full minutes. The crowd of ghosts in this room can barely breathe.

And *Jim*?

Jim’s been watching the whole thing. Timing it. Measuring the silence like a fuse burning down.  Every tap of his mallets has been *foreplay*.  Every eye twitch: calibration.

Then—

**JIM**  (quiet, to himself)  
Now.

*BOOM.*

He slams the snare with both sticks, *hard*, and in one motion the band *erupts*.

**JEFF** drops into a relentless run of bass eighths that hit like a freight train.  **BILL** floods the room with synth choirs and arpeggios that sound like angels mid-nervous breakdown.  **GILLEY** screams into the harmonica mic—raw, untrained, but *honest*—and it *soars*. **KATHY** hammers the piano like it owes her rent and belts the chorus, no longer restrained:

*‘Cause tramps like us—*  
*Baby, we were born to ruuuuuuun\!*

*The whole room shakes.*

Not with feedback. Not with volume.  With *conviction*.  A band on the brink.  A song reimagined by *the only people on Earth reckless enough to try it*.  And when the last note rings out— no one speaks.  Even the air is holding its breath.

**JIM** (quietly, setting his sticks down)  
That’ll play in Peoria.

**KATHY** (turns slowly, sweat-slicked and smiling)  
That’ll *kill*.

**GILLEY** (grinning like he just robbed a goddamn train)  
New Jersey is *not* ready for what’s coming.

**JEFF** (grinning, finally)  
Let’s show ’em who owns the *other* turnpike.

---

## **INT. CASTLE TONE STUDIO – REHEARSAL ROOM – LATER THAT AFTERNOON**

The band is catching their breath. Gilley’s lying flat on the studio floor like he just gave birth to rock and roll. Jeff’s rehydrating like a camel who saw God. Kathy is sitting at the piano, quietly proud.

Suddenly—*the door slams open.*

**SARAH MALCOLM** (enters like a tactical nuke in a pantsuit)  
*Found you.*

Everyone freezes. A moment of pure, primal silence. Even Jim drops a stick.

**SARAH (CONT’D)**  
***Fucking Staten Island?***  This is where you disappeared to?

**CREMEANS** (literally flinching)  
Sarah. Hey. Wow.  Didn’t expect—

**SARAH** (interrupting)  
You didn’t *expect* me?  You ghosted *Island Records*, *Island Security*, and *your own tour manager*.  I had to call *cops* in three boroughs to confirm you weren’t dead in a ditch. Why have you been off the grid, Jeff?

**JEFF (CREMEANS)**  (stammering)  
We were…rehearsing.

**SARAH**  
Rehearsing?  In a defunct carpet warehouse with bad lighting and no ventilation?

**KATHY**  
Technically this used to be a martial arts studio.

**SARAH**  
*Even better.* So you’re combining *sweat*, *delusion*, and *injury risk*.  Lovely.

(beat)
And by the way—*have you read the New York Post* this morning?

(she slams a crumpled paper down on the amp case)

**FRONT PAGE HEADLINE:**  ***SAX OFFENDERS!***  
*Commuted Opens Giants Stadium Show with Sopranos Theme, Ends with Jazz-Free Orgy of Chaos*

**GILLEY** (grinning, leaning over to look)  
Hey, they used a great shot of me!

**SARAH** (reading with venom)  
“Gilley resembled a cross between Tony Soprano, Don Johnson, and a man who’d wandered out of a tanning booth straight into a crime scene.”  That *great shot*?

**JEFF** (deadpan)  
That’s kind of fair, actually.

**BILL** (quietly)  
They called the encore “criminally oversexed.”

**SARAH**  
Good. So you’ve read it.  So you know that Bruce Springsteen’s publicist called *Island* this morning.  To ask if you plan on *defiling his legacy again tonight*.

*Beat.*

**JIM** (very casual)  
We are.

**SARAH** (turns slowly, voice ice cold)  
Excuse me?

**JIM** (grinning)  
We’re playing “Born to Run.”

**SARAH** (staring at him like she’s trying to burn a hole in his soul)  
Do you have *permission*?

**KATHY**  
He’s dead serious. And it’s actually… good.

**SARAH**  
You *illegally* blew through the Sopranos theme and now you’re going *Boss mode* in the Boss’s house?  And you didn't tell *anyone*?

**CREMEANS** (quietly, pleading)  
It was a *time-sensitive idea*.

**SARAH**  
*Time-sensitive*? You people are one rehearsal away from being a RICO case with guitars!

*Beat.*

**JEFF (EVANS)**  
Look. It’s gonna work. It’s not theft. It’s tribute.  We’re not trying to *be* Springsteen.

**GILLEY**  
We’re just… *borrowing lunch money from the E Street Band*.

*Silence. Sarah stares at them. Gilley gives her the smallest wink imaginable.*

**SARAH**  
If you pull this off…If this *doesn’t* start a web ring war, get us sued, or have Clarence Clemons’ ghost show up with a baseball bat…

(beat)
Then I’m sending champagne and NDAs.  If you screw it up?  *I’ll bury you in Long Island and tell Rupert Murdoch's dick it was creative differences.*

*She storms out, heels echoing like gunfire on linoleum.*

---

## **INT. CASTLE TONE STUDIO – STATEN ISLAND – SEPTEMBER 2000 – MOMENTS AFTER SARAH MALCOLM STORMS OUT**

The room is thick with silence and secondhand rage. The *New York Post* headline still sits on the amp like a declaration of war. Gilley’s grinning. Kathy’s stretching her back like she just carried the entire female sex for the last twenty years.

Jeremy stands near the door, eyes on the empty hallway where Sarah disappeared.

**JEREMY** (quiet, genuine)  
I thought she’d want to, like… *listen to the song*.

Everyone turns. He’s not being sarcastic. He *means it*.

**KATHY** (smiling just a little)  
Oh, honey.

**BILL** (dryly)  
Jeremy, Sarah doesn’t listen to music. She listens to *liability exposure*.

**JEFF (EVANS)**  
She doesn’t hear chords. She hears lawsuits.

**JIM** (sits back, thoughtful)  
Yeah… but he’s right. We built something today.  She could’ve just *heard it*.

**GILLEY** (tilting his head, still smirking)  
She’s not paid to hear us.  She’s paid to *find us* when we vanish into the wrong borough with stolen harmonicas and bad ideas.

**KATHY** (walking back to the piano, already setting her fingers on the keys)  
Still. Would’ve been nice.

*She plays the opening “Born to Run” chord—slow, funereal, flawless.*

**KATHY (CONT’D)**  
Let’s give her something to read about tomorrow too.

**JIM** (snaps the beat in slow, steady time)  
Let’s go again.

---

## **INT. CASTLE TONE STUDIO – STATEN ISLAND – LATER THAT AFTERNOON**

The band’s catching their breath after another run-through. The harmonica solo didn’t suck this time. Sarah Malcolm is long gone, the Post headline still fluttering in the A/C breeze.

KATHY stands near the piano, staring at the *Born to Run* vinyl sleeve Jeff's holding. She’s tapping her boot like a bomb waiting to go off. Then—*snap*.

**KATHY**  
Okay.  If we’re doing this?  We’re doing it *hardcore*.

(beat)
We go full mob.

**JEFF (EVANS)**  
Wait—what?

**KATHY** (stalking toward the center of the room like a general planning the final battle)  
Mobsters. All of us. Head-to-toe.

Pinstripes. Suspenders. Fedoras. Cheap cigars if you’ve got ’em. We walk onstage like we’re about to bust up the Copa, not headline Giants Stadium.

**BILL** (stretching)  
And you?

**KATHY** (grinning like the Godfather's favorite niece)  
I’m dressing like a *mob doll*.  Red dress. Heels. Fur stole if I can find one in time.  Hair up. Lipstick *violently red*.  Think *Gena Rowlands meets Lorraine Bracco meets full-blown Catholic guilt fever dream*.

**JIM** (nodding, impressed)  
I’m already in.

**KATHY**  
But Gilley—*you*.

(turns to him with theatrical precision)
You, sweetheart, are dressing *exactly* like the Born to Run album cover.

**GILLEY** (still panting from harmonica practice)  
The white t-shirt and blue jeans?

**KATHY** (points)  
Yes. That. Right down to the rolled sleeves and the cocky lean.  No accessories. No chains. No linen. No sunglasses.  You go out there like a *saint of Springsteen*.

**JEFF (CREMEANS)**  
We’re gonna look like a band that got *dressed by Scorsese and canonized by Columbia Records*.

**JIM** (grinning)  
And we’ll sound like Jersey went to hell and came back through *Memphis in handcuffs*.

**KATHY** (grabs her mic like it owes her an orgasm)  
Let’s make it look like a hit.  Let’s make it *feel* like a crime.  Let’s go out there and *rob a stadium*.

*Everyone stares. Beat. Then—unanimous, inevitable—*

**GILLEY**  
Born to run, baby.

---

## **INT. GIANTS STADIUM – BACKSTAGE DRESSING ROOMS – NIGHT TWO – 6:57PM**

The clock is *ticking*. Curtain in *thirty*. The crew is hustling, but the vibe is pure *fever dream*.

WARDROBE is in *full panic mode*—piles of jackets, suspenders, heels, lipstick, and three separate people yelling *"Do we have a violin case that looks like it might have a gun in it?"*

**WARDROBE LEAD (CONNIE)** (hands full of pinstripes and despair)  
Why does everyone suddenly need *fedoras*, *red lipstick*, and *a white t-shirt with zero branding*?\!  
This is a *rock show*, not a dinner theater production of *The Sopranos: The Musical*\!

**CREMEANS** (pacing like a father outside a delivery room)  
Look, Connie, it’s *conceptual*. It’s a visual *statement*. It’s *Kathy’s plan*.

(leans in, whisper-hissing)  
We’re doing *Born to Run* as if it were *scored by a crime family*.

**CONNIE** (flat)  
That’s not an answer. That’s a felony and a fever dream.

**KATHY** (striding in, already in her dress, cigarette behind one ear, holding court like a mob wife on Easter Sunday)  
It's *branding*, sweetheart.

(beat)  
You want a show people remember twenty years from now?  You make it *look like a myth*.

**CONNIE** (still holding a garment bag)  
You're wearing heels on a stadium stage?

**KATHY**  
If I break my ankle, it'll be on beat.

**BILL** (appears in suspenders, deeply uncomfortable)  
These pants are from the 1940s. They have no give. I'm going to rupture something during the bridge.

**JIM** (grinning, in a too-tight vest, twirling drumsticks like a switchblade)  
That’s the point. *Authenticity through suffering*.

**GILLEY** (walks in last, white t-shirt, blue jeans, boots, hair slicked back, zero irony)  
How do I look?

*Everyone turns. The room goes quiet.*

**KATHY** (softly, sincerely)  
Like the ghost of every jukebox in America.

**CREMEANS** (eyes him, nods once)  
Springsteen would probably punch you.  And then offer you a cigarette.

**CONNIE** (surrendering)  
Okay. Whatever this is, just—don't rip the costumes, don’t bleed on the fabric, and please, for the love of God, no *real* guns.

**JEFF (EVANS)** (off to the side, in full Frank Sinatra noir drag)  
No promises.

---

## **INT. GIANTS STADIUM – BACKSTAGE TUNNEL – NIGHT TWO – 60 SECONDS TO SHOWTIME**

The roar of the crowd *bleeds* through the concrete.  80,000 people. *Waiting.*  The band stands in a tight circle in the dark, barely lit by red floor lights. Dressed like gangsters, ghosts, legends.  Sweaty palms. Twitching fingers. *Adrenaline like sacrament.*

**JIM** (low and steady)  
Alright. Here’s the show.

(beat)
We go in just like last night.  *Woke Up This Morning.*  Straight. Slow burn. We don’t wink. We don’t smirk. We don’t flinch.  *We play it exactly straight.*

(looks around, dead serious)
We look *weird*. And we *do* look weird.  There’s no escaping that.  Mobsters. A harmonica. Gilley dressed like a myth that can’t read music.  That’s baked in.

*Beat. Breathless pause.*

**JIM (CONT’D)**  
And then…

**GILLEY** (grinning, eyes wild)  
And then *what*, brother?

**JIM**  
And *then*… *we hook them.*

(voice rising)
We *kill* 80,000 people at *once*.  Not with volume.  With *shift*.  With *shock*.  With the most beautiful, brutal *pivot* in rock history.  *We detonate “Born to Run.” Our way.*

**JEFF** (quietly, firmly)  
Like a gospel funeral in a stolen car.

**KATHY**  
Let’s make ‘em beg for the keys.

**BILL**  
Let’s *make ‘em forget Springsteen wrote it first.*

*The huddle tightens. Eyes lock. Breaths sync.*

**JIM**  
1…  
2…  
3…  
4—

**ALL (IN UNISON, SHOUTING):**  
*COMMITTED\!*

*The lights blow out. The intro music rolls. And the band charges the stage like they just broke out of prison with a song in their balls.*

---

## **EXT. GIANTS STADIUM – STAGE – NIGHT TWO – MOMENTS BEFORE DOWNBEAT**

Smoke rolls low across the stage. Lights are low, gold and blood-red. The crowd is already on their feet, *80,000 strong*, pulsing, waiting, *primed*. The hum isn’t sound anymore—it’s a *temperature*.

From stage left, **JEREMY EVANS** walks out to his mark.  Slow. Measured. Grinning just enough.

He slings the guitar across his back like it *belongs* there. His boots click once, then settle. The smoke licks around his ankles like a welcome. The spotlight hasn’t hit yet. He’s just a silhouette.

And it hits him—This is the *most fun* he’s ever had *before* a show.  Before the heat. Before the blood rush. Before the first note scorches the crowd.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**  
*It’s electric.*  *No, it’s more than that.*  *It’s like standing on the lip of a volcano while someone counts backward from ten.*

He looks out. Thousands of faces. Rows and rows of people leaning forward—not shouting, not screaming—just *waiting*.

**JEREMY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**  
*You can see it in them. That tension. That fire. It’s coming off them like static. They don’t know what’s about to happen, but they know it’s not what they’re expecting.*

He adjusts his strap. Breathes. His fingers twitch once over the strings, not playing, just *checking the gravity of the moment*.

Somewhere behind him, Kathy's shadow takes her seat at the piano. Jim is crouched low behind the kit. Bill's synths blink in readiness. Gilley's harmonica is warm in his pocket.  And Jeremy?  Jeremy smiles.  Because he *knows*—once this thing starts, there’s no putting it back in the bottle.

And he’s *ready*.

---

## **EXT. GIANTS STADIUM – STAGE – NIGHT TWO – THE OPENING NOTE**

The lights dim.  The roar builds.  80,000 voices, rising like a *storm surge*.  And then—

**One note.**

**KATHY.**  She hits the first piano chord like it’s a *summoning*.  Slow. Haunting.  A *dirge*, not a celebration.

*You woke up this mornin’…*

Her voice is low, smoky. Not belted—*worn*. Lived in. Like the lyrics came from a barstool confession and a rolled-up twenty.

**The crowd?**  
Confused.  Delighted.  *Electrified*.

**GILLEY** steps into the light, harmonica already at his lips. White t-shirt. Blue jeans. The ghost of Bruce Springsteen *and* a Jersey devil.

He blows a note—sharp, cracked, *alive*.  The audience *screams*.  They *get it*.

This is *last night*, but not.  This is *theater and fire and betrayal and resurrection*.

**JEFF**, **JEREMY**, **BILL**, **JIM**—they fall into formation.

The Sopranos groove rolls on, *perfectly straight*.  It’s reverent. It’s real.  And then—

**JIM’S STICK GOES UP.**

**JIM** (whispers)  
Now.

*SNAP.*

**The band turns. HARD.**

**BOOM.**  
Born to Run.  
*Their* version.

**KATHY’S** hands SLAM the keys.  **BILL’S** synths SCREAM.  **JEFF** and **JEREMY** lock into a war march rhythm that sounds like a Cadillac doing 100 through a thunderstorm.

**GILLEY**:
*In the day we sweat it out on the streets…*

His voice *isn't Bruce*.  It’s *gravel and gasoline and gospel*.  It *shouldn’t* work.  But it *does*.  *God help us, it does*.

The *stadium loses its fucking mind.*

People *scream*, *cry*, *collapse into each other*.  This isn’t a concert.  It’s a *riot in a chapel*.  The horns are *gone*.  The harmonica *howls* in their place.  The chorus HITS like a damn *freight train*.

*Tramps like us—*
*BABY, WE WERE BORN TO RUNNNNNN\!\!*

**Pyro lights. Spotlights swing.**  **Second deck starts swaying.**  The sound crew’s radios are *screaming*.  Security is *waving their arms*.  And **Commuted**?

They just *became myth*.

---

## **EXT. GIANTS STADIUM – STAGE – MIDWAY THROUGH “BORN TO RUN”**

The *bridge* is rolling.  Gilley leans into the mic like it owes him rent.  Kathy’s vocals are molten.  
Jeremy and Jeff are locked in like they’ve known each other since *before time*.

And **Jim**—Jim sits behind the kit, *soaked in sweat*, *grinning like a lunatic*.  Every hit lands like he’s punching a hole in the sky.

He glances out over the crowd—*the entire state of New Jersey* having a *spiritual collapse*.

People are screaming.  Crying.  Holding each other.  Climbing the rails.  *Confessing sins to roadies.*

And Jim?  Jim just lets the next *snare crack* fall like a lightning strike.

**JIM (V.O.)**  
*Jesus Christ.*  *This is real.*  *We’re doing it.*  *They’re not just listening—they’re losing their fucking minds*.*

*He hits the ride cymbal like a bell tower announcing the end of the world.*

**JIM (V.O.) (CONT’D)**  
*I’ve got the best gig in the world.*  *No question. No debate. This? Right here? This is it.*  *I make the earth move. Literally.*  *With sticks and sweat and a rhythm that crawled out of Memphis, stole Bruce’s car, and torched the map.*

He looks left. Gilley turns, wild-eyed and *feral*.  Right—Kathy is howling into the bridge with lipstick smeared like warpaint.

Jim raises both sticks above his head—*final chorus incoming*.

**JIM (V.O.) (CONT’D)**  
*One more time, Jersey. Let’s see if the second deck can take it.*

He *slams* the beat in—

*TRAMPS LIKE US—*
*BABY, WE WERE BORN TO RUNNNNNNNN\!\!\!*

**Explosion. Of. Sound.**  Stadium on *fire*.  People on shoulders.  Security frozen.  *History made.*

And Jim?  Jim’s just smiling.  Because this?  This is the dream.  *This is what forever feels like when it’s loud enough to shake the stars.*

---

## **EXT. GIANTS STADIUM – NIGHT TWO – THREE HOURS LATER**

The show is *over*.  But it didn’t *end*—not really.  It *collapsed*.  Into an *improvised encore*, a *saxless gospel*, a *hurricane finale*.  Three hours of sweat, screaming, and soul surgery.

Now?  The *lights are down*.  The *crowd is gone*.  But the *echo* is still vibrating through the steel bones of Giants Stadium.

---

## **INT. BACKSTAGE – STADIUM DRESSING ROOM – 1:45 A.M.**

The band is *wrecked*.  Not tired. *Wrecked.*

**Kathy** is flat on her back on a couch, heels kicked off, red dress bunched around her knees, eye makeup *somewhere near her collarbone*.

**Gilley** is sprawled in a folding chair with a half-eaten hoagie in one hand and the harmonica still in his pocket like a spent weapon.

**Jeff and Jeremy** sit shoulder to shoulder on a bench, not speaking, just breathing, chests rising like they survived *combat*.

**Bill** is hunched over a Gatorade like it’s the Holy Grail.  One sock on.  One sock… *missing forever.*

**Jim**?  He’s the last one in.  Still holding one stick.  Eyes wide. Grinning like a man who just stole fire from the gods.

**JIM** (hoarse, reverent)  
That was a *fucking orgy*.

**GILLEY** (hollow laugh)  
Of *sound*. Of *sin*. Of *pure New Jersey ecstasy*.

**KATHY** (half-conscious)  
Someone call Sarah. Tell her we broke music.  She’ll want to fax a statement to *Jesus*.

**JEFF** (slowly)  
Did we really do it?

**JIM** (grinning)  
We *did it*.  And they’ll be *digging notes out of their teeth for a week.*

**CREMEANS** (enters, pale, shaken, soaked in logistical horror)  
The fire marshal called. He wants to know why section 223 *levitated*.  And also… who authorized *pyro during a harmonica solo*?

*No one answers. They just start laughing. Uncontrollably. Loud. Ugly. Honest.*

**JEREMY** (through the laughter)  
We’re gonna be banned from Jersey forever.

**KATHY** (eyes closed)  
Good.  Let 'em try.  We *own* it now.

**GILLEY** (to the ceiling)  
Goodnight, Boss. We hope you were listening.

**JIM** (sinking into a chair)  
Show’s over.  *That’s how you land a fucking plane.*

*Beat.*

The dressing room goes quiet.  Not from exhaustion.  From *completion*.

**FADE OUT**

Just the sound of breathing.  Dripping sweat.  And the ghost of 80,000 people still screaming in the rafters.

**End of Night Two.**

---

## **INT. BACKSTAGE – STADIUM DRESSING ROOM – 2:00 A.M.**

The *orgy has ended*, but the *human residue* remains.

Empty bottles. Towels. Gear cases flung open like war relics.  The *scent* of adrenaline and afterglow clings to every wall.

**KATHY** pulls on a hoodie over her ruined dress, hair still pinned up like a mob doll who just survived *Judgment Day*.

**KATHY** (grabs a water bottle, heading for the door)  
Alright, boys. I’m gonna go screw.  Tell security not to knock unless the building’s literally on fire.

**JIM** (smiling)  
Want us to lie about who with?

**KATHY** (winks)  
Always.

She’s gone.

**JEREMY** leans against the wall, finally cracking a smile that’s pure, dumb contentment.

**JEREMY** 
All I want…is a cold beer and a chair that doesn’t smell like panic.

**JEFF (EVANS)** (rubbing his temples)  
I want silence.  Darkness.  And a cab that doesn’t have a radio.  I got a migraine creeping in like a rat with steel-toed boots.

**CREMEANS** (pulling out his ancient Nokia like a battlefield medic)  
I’ll get you a ride. Don’t talk to the driver. Don’t tip in quarters. Just get horizontal.

(points toward the hallway)
Cab’s waiting out back. Don’t let the interns follow you.

**JEFF**  
Bless you. If anyone asks, I’ve joined a monastery.

He’s gone too, fading down the corridor like a ghost with receipts.

**BILL** stretches, shirt half-unbuttoned, still flushed with victory.  **JIM** grabs a towel, wipes the sweat, then throws it right back over his shoulder.

They exchange a glance.

**BILL**  
You thinking what I’m thinking?

**JIM**  
Autographs.

**BILL**  
Chaos.

**JIM**  
Loose women and the burning need to be seen by *witnesses*.

**BILL**  
Let’s go work that crowd.

**CREMEANS** (stepping in their path, clipboard in hand like a holy symbol)  
Hold up.

(pointing toward the loading dock)
There’s a *chain-link fence* back there separating you from the fans. It’s meant to *restrict access*, not *invite heroics*.

**JIM** (grinning)  
So don’t climb it?

**CREMEANS**  
Or mount it. Or lean into it with a Sharpie in your teeth.  And for Christ’s sake, if someone throws a bra over the fence, *do not autograph it while it's still warm.*

**BILL** (no hesitation)  
Too late.

**CREMEANS** (shaking his head, walking off)  
One day. One doggone day without a tabloid quote.

**JIM** (throwing an arm around Bill)  
Come on. Let’s go soak in the *cult we accidentally founded*.

They disappear down the tunnel, headed for the dock, the fence, the waiting crowd *that isn’t ready to let go yet*.

---

## **EXT. STADIUM BACK DOCK – MOMENTS LATER**

A wall of *fans*.  A fence covered in Sharpie ink, torn paper, thrown roses, and at least three bras.  Hands reaching. Voices yelling. Cameras flashing.

**Bill and Jim step out into the night like rock stars returning from *Olympus*.**

The people scream.  The city howls.  And history, apparently, still wants *just one more encore*.

---

## **INT. STADIUM – PRIVATE DRESSING ROOM – MOMENTS LATER**

The hallway is chaos—autographs, gear, yelling. But through one discreet door with a laminated “PRIVATE – K.E.” sign, *silence reigns*. The room is dim. Soft light. A couch. A rack of costumes. An empty champagne bottle on its side.

**KATHY** stands in front of the mirror, peeling off her lashes, hair a storm cloud of spent glam. Her face is smeared, her dress half unzipped.

Behind her, **a man sits on the couch**.

Tan. Tank top. Hair like it’s been gelled since birth. Eyes vacant, like no thoughts have ever dared to linger long.  *Jersey Shore incarnate*. No clue who he’s with. Doesn’t ask. He watches her in awe, sipping something sugary from a plastic cup.

**JERSEY GUY**  
So… like, are you famous or somethin’?

**KATHY**  (turning slowly)  
Only tonight.

*Beat.*

She tosses the lashes on the table, walks to him, and climbs right into his lap like it’s her throne.

**JERSEY GUY** (utterly overwhelmed, trying to keep up)  
You, uh—you want me to eat you out sometime or—?

**KATHY** (silences him with one finger)  
No.

**JERSEY GUY** (nods slowly)  
Cool.

She kisses him. Hard.  Pulls him down onto the couch with her.  No tenderness. No conversation. Just heat. The crowd is still screaming somewhere down the hallway. But in here?  **Kathy Espich is done giving everything away for art.**  Tonight, she just wants something *stupid and satisfying*.  And this Jersey guy?  He is *perfect*.

### **CROSSCUT SEQUENCE – NIGHT TWO AFTERMATH**

### **INT. PRIVATE DRESSING ROOM – BACKSTAGE – NIGHT**

**KATHY** straddles **JERSEY GUY**, tangled in red satin and gold chain, half-laughing into his neck.

He moans something like “You’re incredible,” but she’s not listening.  She’s chasing sensation like it owes her rent.

### **INT. YELLOW CAB – MANHATTAN-BOUND – NIGHT**

**JEFF** sits alone in the back seat, pale, jaw clenched, head *throbbing*.  The cab’s dome light flickers like God is mocking him.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
*Three hours under stadium lights.*  *That spotlight was more accurate than a laser-guided missile. Right into my fucking eyes.*

The cab STOPS.  STARTS.  STOPS.  Red light. Honk. *Another* red light.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
*New Jersey traffic is proof there is no God. Or if there is, He’s extremely petty.* 

The brake lights ahead glow with biblical intensity.  Jeff presses his head against the cool window.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
*Someone is having an orgasm backstage right now, and I am actively dying in this backseat.*

### **EXT. STADIUM BACK DOCK – CHAIN-LINK FENCE – NIGHT**

**JIM and BILL** are *kings* in the parking-lot court.

Fans scream.  Bras fly. Security guards pretend not to see anything. A woman hands **JIM** her *thigh* for an autograph.  **BILL** signs a *baby’s onesie* and gets kissed on the cheek for it.

**JIM** (to Bill, ecstatic)  
We *broke* the rules. And they *fucking love us*.

**BILL** (grinning)  
The craziest part? I didn’t even get tackled.

### **INT. YELLOW CAB – STILL. TRAFFIC. FOREVER.**

**JEFF** shifts in his seat like he’s being slow-roasted.

**CAB DRIVER** (cheerfully, oblivious)  
You guys in that band? Sounded pretty wild out there!

**JEFF** (flat)  
We committed mass auditory homicide.  I’d like to go home now.

### **INT. PRIVATE DRESSING ROOM – NIGHT**

**KATHY** arches, breathless.  She pulls the Jersey Guy’s gold chain, eyes glazed with triumph and release.

**KATHY (V.O.)**  
*Best set of my life. Best lay I’ll forget by morning.*

She smirks.

**KATHY (V.O.)**  
*God bless dumb, pretty men and blackout-level adrenaline.*

### **EXT. STADIUM PARKING LOT – NIGHT**

**JIM and BILL** raise their arms like boxers after a title fight.

The crowd chants, *"Commuted! Commuted\!"*

**BILL**  (to Jim)  
You realize we're not going to survive this tour, right?

**JIM**  (winks)  
Yeah. But we’ll *ascend.*

## **INT. CAB – JEFF – FINAL BEAT**

The cab jerks forward again.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
*Let me off at the monastery.*  *I need ice, darkness, and forgiveness.*

*He closes his eyes.*  *Traffic groans. Sirens wail in the distance.*  *The migraine plays drums behind his eyes.*

---

**SMASH TO BLACK**

Silence.  Then:

---

## **MORNING AFTER – HANGOVER TIMES SIX**

### **1. KATHY – HOTEL ROOM – 8:13 A.M.**

She wakes up *face-down* on a hotel comforter with her red dress around one thigh and a cigarette still tucked behind her ear.  No sign of **Jersey Guy**. Just a $10 bill, a ripped condom wrapper, and a crumpled paper napkin with the words:

*"You’re the most powerful woman I’ve ever met." – Vinnie*

She squints. Sits up.

**KATHY (V.O.)**  
*Was that his name?*

*Her head throbs like a club bassline and her mouth tastes like gin and eyeliner.*  She grabs her phone, blinks at 16 missed calls from **Sarah Malcolm**, and mutters:

**KATHY**  
Fuck me gently with a lawsuit.

### **2. JEFF – HOTEL BED – 8:17 A.M.**

Complete darkness. Curtains sealed like a tomb.  Jeff lies under two blankets, one ice pack, and what appears to be a Gideon Bible acting as a forehead stabilizer.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
*Did we do it?*  *Did we really pull it off?*

*He shifts. Pain pulses like Morse code in his spine.*

**JEFF (V.O.) (CONT’D)**  
*No encore is worth this.*

The room phone rings. He doesn’t move. Just mutters:

**JEFF**  
Leave a message at the sound of my corpse.

### **3. JIM – HOTEL BATHROOM – 8:22 A.M.**

Jim is *shirtless*, brushing his teeth while still wearing his *backstage vest* and someone else’s *bracelet*.

He spits, looks in the mirror, and smiles like a war criminal who just won the Nobel Prize.

**JIM (V.O.)**  
*My knuckles hurt. My thighs are sore. My voice is shot.*

(grins wider)
*I’ve never felt more alive.*

*Behind him, there’s a phone number written in lipstick on the bathroom mirror.*

He squints.

**JIM**  
…“Call me, tambourine girl”?  What the hell did I do?

### **4. BILL – HOTEL LOBBY – 8:28 A.M.**

Bill’s sitting upright in a lobby armchair, *motionless*.  A single bloodshot eye stares at a half-empty coffee cup.  He’s still wearing the suspenders.  His synth backpack is on the floor like a crime scene.  He looks like he’s been there *since 6 a.m.*

**BILL (V.O.)**  
*I signed a baby.*  *Someone handed me a prescription bottle and asked me to autograph the side effects.*

(beat)
*I think I might be in love with a stage tech named Carla. Or Cora. Or Clawdia.*

He takes a sip. Winces.

**BILL**  
This isn’t coffee. This is vengeance.

### **5. JEREMY – DINER BOOTH – 8:35 A.M.**

Jeremy sits in a corner booth with a full breakfast spread and *no appetite*. He’s holding a cold beer with both hands like it’s a sacred relic.  Sunglasses on indoors. Across from him, a child is crying. Loudly.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**  
*This is karma for saying “I want a cold beer” out loud in the presence of God.*

A waitress asks if he wants anything reheated.

**JEREMY**  
Just me.

### **6. CREMEANS – HOTEL BUSINESS CENTER – 8:39 A.M.**

Cremeans is in the same clothes as last night, typing furiously. His laptop is surrounded by crumpled receipts, scribbled call sheets, and one *open bottle of Tums*.  He’s on the phone with someone at Island Records.

**CREMEANS**  
Yes, I understand the Post is running *another* piece. No, I do not know where Kathy is.  No, I don’t know who “Tambourine Girl” is.  Yes, I will send the setlist for approval next time, assuming they ever follow it.

(pause)
…Yes, they’re alive. *Barely*.

He hangs up. Rubs his eyes.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**  
*I work for a band of beautiful, brilliant lunatics.*  *And I’m going to die before the tour bus even gets an oil change.*

### **FINAL BEAT – MONTAGE**

**“Born to Run (Live Bootleg Version)”** plays *distorted and lo-fi* under a fast cut of:

* Gilley still asleep in the hallway of the hotel, hugging a Fender case like a teddy bear.
* A fan outside the stadium showing off a signed *parking ticket*.
* Someone holding up a bootleg T-shirt: *“I Survived Commuted – Giants Stadium 2000”*
* Kathy lighting a cigarette with last night’s setlist.
* Jeff slowly dragging himself to the minibar like a war veteran going for rations.
* Bill staring at a blank TV, whispering, *“Did we win?”*

**FADE TO BLACK.**

**TEXT ON SCREEN:**  **Commuted never played New Jersey the same way again.**  **But no one else ever did either.**

---

# **ASBURY PARK PRESS**

**Sunday, September 24, 2000**  
**FRONT PAGE HEADLINE:**

## **"They Played the Boss—and Got Away With It"**  
***Commuted’s Jersey Gamble Pays Off in Pyro, Piano, and Pure Blasphemy***
**By: Maureen Scalzo – Senior Music Correspondent**

**Giants Stadium hasn’t seen anything like this since the E Street Band turned it into a cathedral.**  But last night?  It was something *else entirely*.

Commuted—known nationally for their grinding guitars and erratic setlists—took the stage looking like they’d stepped out of a Martin Scorsese fever dream and into Bruce Springsteen’s house *uninvited*.

And then they *played “Born to Run.”*  

Their way.  No horns.  No Clarence.  No apologies. Just a harmonica in place of the sax.  
A haunting piano intro that felt more funeral than freeway.  And a lead singer in a white t-shirt and blue jeans who had the audacity to grin like he’d *earned it*.

> *“It was like watching Springsteen’s ghost get mugged by Patti Smith and then hugged by Tom Waits,”* said one fan, still tear-streaked and barefoot outside the stadium.

The band opened with the *Sopranos* theme again—straight as a razor—and then *hooked* the audience by yanking them headfirst into a version of “*Born to Run*” that was equal parts gospel, garage, and open-mic séance.

**It should have been a disaster.**  It wasn’t. It was *criminally brilliant*. And somehow, they got away with it.

**A few things worth noting:**

* **Kathy Espich’s performance was operatic chaos.** Dressed like a mob widow on her third alimony check, she turned the opening verse into a confessional. Her piano work alone had half the crowd in stunned silence.
* **The harmonica solo worked.** No one knows how. It shouldn’t have. It did.
* **Gilley looked like a Bruce impersonator who just got off a bender in Reno—but sang with surprising grace.**
* **The encore was an entirely improvised mess of blues covers, sex noise, and synth solos.** The crowd *screamed for more*.

> **“This wasn’t just a tribute. It was a takeover,”** said New Brunswick resident and longtime Springsteen fan Ed B. “They didn’t borrow Bruce. They *hijacked* him—and then dropped him off back home with a note that said thanks.”

**The Asbury Park Press doesn’t often endorse musical trespassing.**  But we’ll say this: If you’re going to break into the Church of Springsteen…**You better come correctly.**

Last night, *they did*.

> [!sidebar]
>**Fan Report – Section 223**  
>*“The second deck was literally swaying. I thought we were going down. I would’ve died happy.”*

---

## **INT. BRUCE SPRINGSTEEN’S KITCHEN – COLTS NECK, NEW JERSEY – SUNDAY MORNING**

Early light filters through the windows. The coffee’s hot. The toast is burnt. A golden retriever sighs under the table.

**BRUCE SPRINGSTEEN** sits at the head of the table in a Springsteenian uniform: gray t-shirt, jeans, socks with a hole in the toe. A quiet Sunday morning—same as ever.

Except…He’s reading the **Asbury Park Press**.  Front page.  Full spread.  **“They Played the Boss—And Got Away With It.”**

*He reads it slow.*  Like he does everything.  Line by line. Sip by sip. Across the kitchen, **Patti Scialfa** enters, tying her robe.

**PATTI**  
Please tell me they didn’t butcher it.

**BRUCE** (gruff, unreadable)  
They didn’t.

*He goes quiet again. Flips to the second page.*

**PATTI**  
Was it respectful?

**BRUCE** (grinning)  
Nope.

**PATTI** (sits, raising an eyebrow)  
Was it good?

*He folds the paper once, then again. Sets it down.*

**BRUCE** (sips coffee)  
Yeah.

(beat)
It was *real good.*

**PATTI**  
Should we sue?

**BRUCE**  
Nah.

(pause)
Let ‘em run. They were *born to.*

---

## **INT. ISLAND RECORDS OFFICE – MONDAY MORNING – 9:14 A.M.**

Phones are ringing. Coffee is bitter. Assistants are crying in cubicles.  **SARAH MALCOLM** stands in her glass office, phone to ear, staring at the *as-yet-unpaid invoice* for 27 broken microphone stands and a “property damage fee” from Giants Stadium.

**SARAH** (into phone)  
Wait—Bruce who?

(beat)
…Oh.  Oh.  Shit.

---

## **INT. CREMEANS’ HOTEL ROOM – 9:18 A.M.**

**CREMEANS** is sitting at a tiny hotel desk with six sticky notes on his forearm, a legal pad full of names, and one working phone charger.  His eyes are bloodshot. His coffee is more Advil than caffeine.

**SARAH (V.O., on speaker)**  
So Bruce’s team—his actual management, like *the holy order of Springsteen*—just called.

**CREMEANS**  
Please don’t say cease and desist.

**SARAH (V.O.)**  
Worse.

(beat)
They want a *copy* of last night’s **“Born to Run.”**  The board audio. The real deal.

**CREMEANS** (blinks)  
They’re asking for the master?

**SARAH (V.O.)**  
They want to hear it in full fidelity. Bruce *reads the damn paper*, and now he’s curious.

**CREMEANS** (sits back, half-laughing, half-terrified)  
Okay. Okay. We’re good.  We can do this.  I’ll get the stems from Bill. Bounce a clean export. No edits, no crowd bleed. Just straight fire.

(beat)
Should I watermark it?

**SARAH (V.O.)**  
No. This isn’t some blogger. This is *The Boss.*

**CREMEANS** (softly)  
God help us.

### **INT. BILL’S HOTEL ROOM – MINUTES LATER**

**BILL** opens the door shirtless, holding a synth cable like a snake.

**CREMEANS**  
Get your laptop.  Bruce wants the mix.

**BILL** (squinting)  
*Springsteen Bruce?*

**CREMEANS**  
You think this is about Caitlyn Jenner?

### **INT. HOTEL LOBBY – LATER**

CREMEANS walks through the lobby holding a flash drive like it’s a *sacred relic*.

He doesn’t blink. He doesn’t smile. He just walks it to the courier like he’s carrying the **Ark of the Covenant in khakis**.

---

## **INT. BRUCE SPRINGSTEEN’S HOUSE – THAT NIGHT**

The sun sets over Colts Neck. The house is quiet. In his office, Bruce plugs in the flash drive.  Puts on his headphones.  Hits play.  He closes his eyes.

*Piano—low, ghostly.*  *Harmonica—cracked and alive.*  *Vocals—broken, beautiful, dangerously sincere.*

Bruce listens.  No smile. No frown.  Just *deep, deep listening*. He leans back.  Eyes closed.  Taps one hand lightly on the desk.  And mutters—*just loud enough*:

**BRUCE**  
…Damn.

### **INT. BRUCE SPRINGSTEEN’S HOUSE – LATE NIGHT – COLTS NECK, NJ**

Flash drive still plugged in.  Headphones off.  Bruce’s chair *creaks back* as he stands, slaps his palms on the desk like a judge delivering a sentence.

**BRUCE** (to no one)  
Alright.  Alright! That’s how you *fucking do it.*

---

## **INT. ASBURY PARK STUDIO – NEXT MORNING – 10:02 A.M.**

**Commuted** is groggy, half-assembled in a local rehearsal space. Jim’s drumming with one eye open. Kathy is face-deep in an iced coffee. Jeff is sipping black tea like it’s morphine.

**CREMEANS** bursts in holding a battered flip phone like it just spoke in tongues.

**CREMEANS**  
Guys.  *Brace yourselves.*

**BILL**  
We getting sued?

**CREMEANS**  
Worse.

(beat)
We’re getting *Springsteened.*

**JIM** (grinning)  
Define that.

**CREMEANS**  
He’s coming.  **To the show.**

**ALL** (stunned silence)
...

**CREMEANS**  
Tomorrow night. MSG.  He’s not calling.  He’s *bringing a mic and his boots*.

**KATHY**  (sharp inhale)  
Holy. Shit.

**JEFF**  
You sure he’s not coming to punch Gilley in the face?

**CREMEANS**  
If he is, he’ll *do it on beat.*

---

## **INT. MSG – NIGHT OF THE SHOW**

Final encore. Crowd’s electric. Stage is hazy with sweat and feedback.

**GILLEY** walks to the mic, still glowing from the “Devil’s Jersey Gospel” version of *No One Leaves Clean.*

He raises the mic.

**GILLEY** (to audience)
Alright, Jersey.  We got one more surprise.

The crowd *screams*.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
We borrowed his song.  His soul.  And maybe his patience.  So tonight…He’s here to *take it back.*

The band parts like the Red Sea. And through the fog, in blue jeans and boots—

**BRUCE SPRINGSTEEN walks on stage.**

The crowd *damages the roof screaming*.  Two bulbs explode.

**KATHY** (stepping back from the mic, stunned)  
Well holy hell.

**BRUCE** (grabs the mic like it’s a weapon)  
Let’s finish what you started.

---

**MOMENTS LATER – FULL BAND ONSTAGE**

*1… 2… 3… 4\!*

And they *tear into “Born to Run”*— **the real one.**  But with Commuted behind him—*louder*, *meaner*, *on fire*.

Springsteen doesn’t hold back.  He’s not covering himself.  He’s *reclaiming the anthem*— 
and sharing it.

**The crowd’s crying.**  **The rafters are shaking.**  **History is being rewritten.** *Loudly. As it should be.*

---

**BACKSTAGE – LATER THAT NIGHT**

**BRUCE** hugs Kathy, fist-bumps Jim, throws an arm around Gilley.

**BRUCE**  (to the whole band)  
You kids are dangerous.

(beat)
Don’t stop.

---

## **INT. MADISON SQUARE GARDEN – BACKSTAGE – LATER THAT NIGHT**

**The dressing room is quiet.** No screaming. No rushing. No broken monitors.  
Just the band—sitting, slouched, legs up, *stunned into satisfaction*. There’s half a pizza on the table. One bottle of chilled champagne. No drugs. No handcuffs.

Just *them*.

**KATHY** (staring at the ceiling)  
I can die now.  Like, *actually*.  No notes. No edits.  That was it.

**JIM** (grinning, eyes still wild)  
And for once… nobody was high.  Nobody bailed.  Nobody got *arrested*.

**BILL** (pouring the cold champagne)  
That feels… off-brand.

**JEFF** (sips)  
Good.  Let it feel weird.  We *earned* weird.

**JEREMY** (sincerely)  
I’ve never felt it like this before.  Like we *meant it*, and they *heard* it.

**GILLEY** (sinks into the couch, eyes closed)  
Bruce didn’t punch me.  He sang with me.

(beat)
I’m good to die tomorrow if the bus hits me outside the hotel.

**CREMEANS** (from the doorway, clipboard still in hand)  
You die and I *swear to God*, I will reanimate your corpse for press week.

*They all laugh.* Long, real, *earned* laughter.

---

**FINAL MOMENT**

The lights flicker. The noise dies. The adrenaline fades.  But the feeling?  *That stays.* They did it.  **Together. Sober. Free. Alive.** **Career-defining.** No overdoses.  No mugshots.  Just *music* and *myth*.

**Consensus:** *We can die now.*  *And die well.*

---

**FADE OUT.**

**TEXT ON SCREEN:**  *That night, no one got arrested. No one got high. No one got lost.*  *Just loud.*  *And that was enough.*

---

## **INT. MTV NEWSROOM – TRL HQ – 7:52 A.M. – SEPTEMBER 26, 2000**

Coffee in one hand, script in the other, **KURT LODER** is already dressed like a man who’s read three newspapers and *judged them all*. He looks into the camera like it owes him rent.

**KURT LODER (V.O.)**  
*Well… it happened.*  *Commuted—yes, that Commuted—played Madison Square Garden last night…**And Bruce Springsteen walked onstage during their final encore.*

**CUT TO: TITLE CARD – “MTV NEWS: BREAKING”**
*“THE NIGHT COMMITTED MET THE BOSS”*  *SPRINGSTEEN JOINS COMMUTED IN MSG SHOCKER*

---

## **INT. MTV STUDIO – ON CAMERA – LIVE TAPING**

**KURT LODER** sits at the desk, deadpan but clearly *buzzing*.

**KURT LODER**  
The band that last week opened a stadium show with *The Sopranos* theme and ended it with a blues-inflected, harmonica-drenched version of *Born to Run* just got their reckoning.

Except instead of lawsuits or public spankings, it came with *an invitation*.

Bruce Springsteen—rock deity, New Jersey icon, and the only man alive who can wear a denim shirt without irony—took the stage during Commuted’s encore at Madison Square Garden last night.

He sang with them. Played with them. *Endorsed them.*

Let me be clear: Bruce doesn’t do that. Bruce is *Springsteen*. He *is* the last line. The final word.

But last night?

He passed the torch. Or maybe he just lit theirs on fire.

---

**CUT TO: FAN FOOTAGE – MSG – GRAINY CAMCORDER**

Bruce and Gilley, shoulder to shoulder, tearing into the final chorus of “Born to Run.”  
Kathy hammering the piano like a mad priestess.  The crowd *screaming as one*.

---

**BACK TO KURT – LIVE**

**KURT LODER**  
Was it reckless?  Sure.  Was it sacrilegious?  A little.

But here’s the thing: it was *good*.  No overdoses. No arrests. No hotel fires. Just a band at their absolute peak, and a legend saying, “Yeah. I see you.”

Consensus?  Commuted didn’t just pull it off.  They wrote their name in the gospel of American rock—and Bruce helped them sign it.

**FINAL LINE – LOOKING DIRECTLY AT CAMERA**

**KURT LODER**  
I’ve covered this scene for twenty years.  And trust me—You *don’t* come out of New Jersey alive unless the Boss says so.  Last night? He said so.

*MTV News jingle plays. The screen fades to black. The legend grows.*

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – EARLY MORNING – SEPTEMBER 27, 2000**

The bus is rolling down the interstate somewhere in North Jersey. Everyone is half-alive. The sun is *offensive*. Jim is wearing sunglasses indoors. Jeff has a cold towel over his face. Gilley is trying to eat Funyuns and failing.

**KATHY** stands at the front of the aisle like a general about to change history.

**KATHY**  
Spa day.

*Everyone groans.*

**JEFF**  
No.

**KATHY**  
Yes. All of you.  You can barely walk. You smell like stadium beer and failure.  I’m booking us the *whole goddamn place.*

**JEREMY**  
Wait—like… massages?

**KATHY**  
Massages. Facials. Body wraps. Steam rooms.  Silence. Cucumber water. The *soft whirr of privilege*.

**JIM** (grinning)  
Does it come with mimosa service?

**KATHY**  
It comes with **me not stabbing you.**

*That gets everyone's attention.*

---

## **EXT. LUXE DAY SPA – 90 MINUTES LATER**

The band climbs out of the bus looking like rock-star carnage wrapped in thrift store cool.

The spa is tranquil. White stone walls. Bamboo. A water feature that sounds like a fairy pissing into a crystal bowl.

**CREMEANS** (whispers)  
Do they know we’re a rock band?

**KATHY** (grinning)  
No. They think we’re *indie film producers*. Play along.

---

## **INT. SPA – DRESSING ROOMS – MOMENTS LATER**

**KATHY** emerges in a white robe, hair tied up, glowing already.

**KATHY**  
I swear to God, the robe alone just healed my credit score.

---

**SPA MONTAGE – SET TO INSTRUMENTAL “Born to Run (Lo-Fi Remix)”**

* **Jeff** lies facedown on a massage table, flinching every time the masseuse touches his back.

*“Is it supposed to hurt this much?”*  
*“Only if you’ve been carrying generational trauma in your shoulders.”*  
*“…Okay, yeah. That tracks.”*

* **Jim** sits in the sauna, towel over his head, sipping something herbal and declaring:

*“I’m sweating out my sins. I can feel 1998 leaving my body.”*

* **Bill** is wrapped in seaweed, eyes closed, whispering, *“Tell no one of this. Ever.”*
* **Jeremy** cautiously dips into a hot tub like he’s afraid it might be sentient.
* **Gilley** wanders the quiet room, munching spa almonds and loudly asking where they keep the beer fridge.
* **Kathy** lies back during her facial, serene.

*“See? Told you idiots.”*

---

## **INT. SPA LOUNGE – HOURS LATER**

The band lounges in silence, glowing, damp, vaguely human again. Soft harp music plays. No one speaks for a full minute.

**JEFF** (eyes closed)  
I think my headache moved out.

**JIM**  
I would cheat on my therapist with that hot stone girl.

**JEREMY**  
I understand what inner peace feels like now.  It's like warm pudding inside your ribs.

**BILL**  
If this is what rich people feel like all the time…I kind of get it.

**KATHY** (smiling, robe perfect)  
I’m telling you—**rock and roll is temporary. Spa days are *forever*.**

---

## **INT. SPA LOUNGE – POST-SCRUB GLOW – AFTERNOON**

The band is lounging in plush robes like the world’s most chaotic luxury cult.  Steam curls in the air. There’s a faint scent of eucalyptus and absolution.  Everyone is **deeply relaxed**—until reality rears its golden head.

**BILL** (sipping cucumber water)  
Man, if this is what rich people do every week…

**JEFF** (sits up, deadpan)  
*Bill.*

(beat)
*You **are** fucking rich.*

**BILL** (blinks)  
What?

**JEFF**  
You just bought **three million dollars** in studio gear for your gig in Over-the-Rhine.  Like, *casually* spent three million ducats.  You have parking spaces with your name on them.

**JIM**  
You have a *second* espresso machine. In your *synth room*.

**JEREMY**  
You paid for your tour rig in **cash**. Who even *does that*?

**BILL** (defensive)  
It was an auction!

**JEFF**  
It was **Sotheby’s**, dude.

**KATHY** (laughing, kicks her foot up)  
Everybody calm down. This isn’t a *peen-comparison* contest.

(leans back, smug)  
*Because I’ve got the biggest peen of all.*

**JEREMY** (sips tea, fires back deadpan)  
Don’t be so sure, *bitch.*

*The room explodes in laughter.*

**JIM**  
I can’t believe we’re fighting over imaginary dicks in bathrobes.

**KATHY**  
Imaginary? Speak for yourself, percussion boy.

**CREMEANS** (walking in with his ever-present clipboard)  
Okay, did I miss the part where we all got rich *and* started doing gender-flex sword fights with our portfolios?

**GILLEY** (grinning)  
If I’d known we could afford robes this soft, I would’ve stopped blowing all my royalties on tequila and laser tag.

**KATHY**  
You *still* smell like both.

They all collapse into their seats again, chuckling, glowing, *loose in a way only legends can be when they’ve survived themselves*.

**JEFF** (quietly, raising his glass)  
To having made it out.

**KATHY**  
And to maybe, just maybe, finally acting like it.

**ALL**  
Cheers.

---

## **INT. SPA LOUNGE – EARLY EVENING**

The crew is sprawled out like pampered royalty, *lotioned, loosened, and low-key glowing*.  **JEFF** sits up with a sigh, cracking his neck, towel still around his shoulders like a dojo master.

**JEFF** (muttering, satisfied)  
If you all had listened to me in *last year*, you would’ve made bank…or at least *kept* it.

(beat)
But no. Tech stocks were gonna “go to the moon.”

(looks pointedly at **Jeremy**)  
Fucking *Cisco*, huh?

**JEREMY**  (staring off, face deadpan)  
Fucking *Cisco*.

*They both nod solemnly, like veterans of a war fought in Excel sheets.*

**BILL**  
I bought AOL stock like it was a war bond.

**JIM**  
Didn’t you try to expense a *Beige G3* as “stage equipment”?

**BILL**  
It powered my synth patches!

**KATHY** (eyes closed, smirking)  
Y’all were out here playing Dot Com Monopoly and I was stuffing my royalty checks in my mattress like a Depression-era widow.

**JEFF**  
And now you own half a co-op in Echo Park and don’t even know it.

**KATHY**  
Exactly. Who needs Wall Street when you’ve got a walk-in closet and spite?

**CREMEANS** (suddenly appearing like spa-gliding doom)  
If I hear one more word about *Cisco Systems*, I’m going to *personally fax you all your 401(k) balances with a death threat attached.*

*Everyone cracks up again.*

**GILLEY**  
Wait… so I shouldn’t have bought shares in Ask Jeeves?

**EVERYONE (simultaneously):**  
*NO.*

---

## **INT. SPA LOUNGE – SAME EVENING**

The steam’s gone. The robes are staying. The vibe is post-glow *rich idiot energy*. Everyone’s lounged around, full of cucumber water and entitlement.

**BILL** (suddenly, out of nowhere)  
You guys remember when the Rolling Stones licensed *Start Me Up* for the Windows 95 launch?

**JEFF** (grimaces)  
Yes. And then I remember *watching my soul exit my body* via my butthole during the commercial.

**BILL** (leaning forward, mock-serious)  
Okay, but like…Does anyone think there’s *any* universe where *Come Inside Me* could get that kind of love?

**JEREMY** (blinking)  
From… *Microsoft?*

**BILL** (laughing)  
I’m just saying, if Bill Gates had balls, we could’ve been the official theme song for *Clippy*.

**KATHY** (cackling)  
“Looks like you’re trying to *come inside someone*. Need help with that?”

**JIM**  
*“Would you like me to format your document… slowly?”*

**CREMEANS** (rubbing temples)  
Please, for the love of all things contractually binding, stop imagining *Come Inside Me* as enterprise software branding.

**JEFF** (grinning)  
To be fair… it’s catchy.  Uncomfortably catchy.

**JEREMY**  
Can you imagine the Microsoft event? *“Welcome to the Future of Office Integration.”*  
*\[Cue: COME INSIDE MEEEEEEE\!\!\]*

**KATHY**  
Just confetti and awkward clapping from 20,000 middle managers in pleated Dockers.

**GILLEY** (a little too sincerely)  
I’d play that gig.  And bang someone.

**BILL**  (raising his glass)  
To missed branding opportunities.  To the song that will never score a product launch but *did* make someone cry in a Porta Potty at Giants Stadium.

**ALL**  
Cheers.

---

## **INT. SPA LOUNGE – SAME EVENING, STILL IN ROBES, STILL RIDICULOUS**

Everyone’s laughing, still high on the idea of *Come Inside Me* scoring a Microsoft keynote.  Empty cucumber water glasses. The faint echo of classical music.  And then—

**KATHY** (turning to Gilley, cocking an eyebrow)  
Serious question, frontman.

(beat)
Would you *actually* want to sell one of our songs to somebody who’s gonna use it to sell *Aftersave*?  Or I don’t know… fuckin’ *Metamucil*?

*The room goes quiet for a beat—just long enough for the question to land like a philosophical grenade in a bathrobe.*

**GILLEY**  (grinning)  
Well, that depends.

(leans back dramatically)
Are we talking *sensitive skin Aftersave* or the kind that makes you feel like you just rubbed mentholated regret on your face?

**JIM**  (smiling)  
Clarifying questions are important.

**KATHY**
