I’m serious.  We build this whole *machine*, this whole messy, glorious sound… and some *branding intern in khakis* wants to sync it to a commercial about keeping your fiber regular?

**JEFF**  (quietly)  
I think Come Inside Me actually *causes* irregularity.

**BILL**  (pensively)  
You know, a remix of *The Left Hand* would really pair well with high-end razor ads. Or artisan knives. Or… murder podcasts.

**JEREMY**  
I’m gonna be sick.

**KATHY**  (turning back to Gilley)  
So?

Would you let them take one of our songs—*your lyrics*, your little confessional art poems—and slap it on a bottle of fuckin’ *metabolic balance tonic*?

**GILLEY**  (pause… then, sincerely)  
Only if we got to write the commercial ourselves.

(beat)
And I get to narrate it like a goddamn prophecy.

(puts on his gravely stage voice)  
*“There comes a time in every man’s life… when his gut flora calls out in the night…”*

**EVERYONE**  
*NO\!*

**KATHY**  (throwing a pillow at him)  
*Absolutely not.*

**CREMEANS**  
I am *begging* you people to stop. We’ve barely survived the copyright inquiries from Giants Stadium. I’m not fighting a cease-and-desist from fucking GNC.

They all collapse into laughter again—half ridiculous, half exhausted, *fully themselves*. 
And Kathy just shakes her head, smiling.

**KATHY**  
I swear to God, if we ever sell one of our songs to a laxative company, I’m starting a solo noise project called *Permanent Clench*.

---

## **INT. SPA LOUNGE – EVENING WINDING DOWN**

The room’s come down from the Metamucil jokes and branding nonsense.  
Everyone’s sunk deep into post-laughter silence.

**BILL** (suddenly, quietly)  
…Seriously, though.

(beat)
I’ve been thinking about doing movie scores a whole bunch.

*Everyone turns to him like he just announced he’s becoming a monk.*

**JIM**  (stares)  
*Bill?* Movie scores?

**JEREMY**  
What, like full orchestral, John Williams-level movie scores?

**BILL** (shrugs)  
Not *exactly*.  Not all that *French horn and heroic bullshit*. More… modern. You know, *textures*. Emotion.  Radiohead’s doing it. Or at least the two blokes—Jonny Greenwood, and the other one with the cheekbones.

**JEFF**  
Thom Yorke?

**BILL**  
Yeah. That guy. Cheekbones and doom.

*He sips his tea.*

**BILL (CONT’D)**  
I don’t know. The way film’s going… it’s not about melodies anymore. It’s about *atmosphere*. You can tell a whole story with just the *right tone*, the right low-end swell, one decaying chord.

**KATHY** (staring at him, halfway between impressed and amused)  
Jesus Christ, Bill. That’s the most poetic thing you’ve said in six years.

**GILLEY**  
I thought the most poetic thing he said was “please don’t put your beer on my Juno-60.”

**CREMEANS** (chiming in dryly)  
That was less poetry, more a cry for help.

**BILL** (smiles, quietly)  
I’m serious, though.  I want to score something *sad*. Or weird. Or sad and weird.  Some indie flick with long shots of gas stations and people not talking.

**JIM**  
Okay, now it sounds like you just want to live inside an A24 trailer.

**BILL**  
Maybe I do.

(beat)
Don’t get me wrong—I love what we do. But this tour’s gonna end. The fire’s gonna cool off. And I want to keep *building something*, you know?  Even if it’s *quiet*.

*Everyone sits with that for a moment. Not in judgment. Not in disbelief. Just… respect.*

**KATHY** (sincerely)  
You’d be good at it, Bill.

**JEFF**  
*Really* good. Like emotionally manipulative in a slow-burning, synth-drenched kind of way.

**JEREMY**  
You’d make people cry about coffee mugs and missed texts.

**JIM** (raises his tea glass)  
To future Oscar winner Bill Davenport—composer, philosopher, robe enthusiast.

**ALL**  
Cheers.

---

## **INT. SPA LOUNGE – EVENING, STILL IN ROBES, NOW WITH DEEPER REFLECTIONS**

**BILL** has just stunned everyone with his low-key ambition to compose modern, haunting film scores. The room sits in rare, reflective silence.

And then—

**JEFF** (clears his throat, casually)  
I’ve actually… thought about doing something similar.

(beat)
But not for movies.

*Heads swivel.*

**JEFF (CONT’D)**  
Video games.

*Blank stares.*

**JEFF (CONT’D)**  (at one hundred million miles an hour)
Unreal Tournament’s got me obsessed.  I’ve been playing it between shows, and there’s something there— not just in the gameplay, but in the *sound design*.

(he gets going, warming to his own idea)
Right now the music’s mostly loops and atmosphere, but once computers get *faster*, like *really fast*, there’s going to be this moment…Where games, movies, music, and real-time interaction all *fuse*.

(beat)
They’re going to need *blazing rock tunes*.  Something dynamic. Reactive. Full of adrenaline.  Imagine writing a riff that *changes depending on what a player does*.  Combat music that evolves. Sad moments underscored in real time.  It’s not just scoring—it’s *designing emotion on demand*.

(looks around)  
Does anybody… think they’d be interested in that?

*The silence stretches just a little too long.*

**KATHY** (flatly)  
No.

**JIM** (definitively)  
Absolutely not.

**GILLEY** (grinning)  
I’m barely interested in *video games now*.

**JEREMY**  
I played *Oregon Trail* once. That’s the limit of my engagement.

**BILL** (sipping tea)  
I support your vision.  But I will not join you in that foxhole.

**CREMEANS** (crossing arms)  
I understand how royalties work for real songs.  I’m not learning *polygonal licensing*.

**JEFF** (nods, accepting the rejection like a king watching fools miss prophecy)  
Cool.  I’ll remember this when I’m scoring a deathmatch and sipping scotch in 2035.

**KATHY** (smirking)  
You do that. I’ll be at Sundance, accepting my third Lifetime Achievement Award in fishnet tights and spite.

They laugh again, but *there’s something in Jeff’s tone*. Something quiet, strange, *too smart*.  Because *he's not wrong*.  And they know it.  But for now?  **Spa day continues.**

---

## **INT. SPA LOUNGE – EVENING, POST-BANTER CALM**

The laughter from Jeff’s doomed video game dream fades.  Teacups clink softly. Eucalyptus hangs thick.  A thoughtful silence settles in. Robes shift.

**JEFF** (quiet, curious)  
Kathy?

(beat)
What’s your thing with *Sundance*?  You joke about it, but like… Are you *actually* interested in film and TV?

*Everyone turns slightly, surprised. Kathy doesn’t flinch.*

**KATHY** (sits up straighter, eyes sharp)  
Highly.  Not necessarily *in front* of the camera.  I mean, sure—I’ve been on enough stages to know how to perform.  But what interests me now?  *Behind* it. 

(leans forward, serious now)
Directing.  My first taste on a video?  Oh, man, I got wet. Fireside Confessions?  Fucking sex with sunshine.  But maybe I could be producing, once I get some capital together.  I want to build something *artful*. *Strange*. *Unapologetic.*  I’m talking *real arthouse shit*.  The kind of films that get booed at Cannes and win the Independent Spirit Award six months later.

**JIM** (grinning)  
Like long takes of naked people smoking and arguing about mortality?

**KATHY**  
Exactly. But make it *queer, broke, and dangerous*.  No easy heroes. No clean endings. Just raw people flailing inside gorgeous color grading.

**GILLEY** (stretching)  
So basically… the Commuted biopic?

**KATHY** (smirks)  
If I ever direct our biopic, no one gets out alive and half the dialogue is in subtitles.

**BILL** (sipping his tea)  
I’d score the hell out of that.

**JEREMY** (staring)  
I didn’t know you wanted that.

**KATHY**  
Not many people do.  I kept it close for a long time.

(beat)
But I’m done shrinking.

*The room goes quiet—not awkward. Respectful.* A new kind of silence. The kind that knows:  Kathy Espich is *not* done evolving.

**JEFF** (softly, but with weight)  
I’d watch anything you make.

**KATHY** (sincerely)  
Thanks, Jeff.

---

## **INT. SPA LOUNGE – EVENING, POST-REVELATION, POST-STEAM**

The mood is *warm*.  Refined chaos.  Ambition lingers in the air like essential oils and former trauma.

**JIM**, still sprawled, towel behind his neck like a spa king and court jester, squints toward **KATHY** with that crooked half-grin that always precedes a *blunt-as-hell question*.

**JIM**  
So…This whole *queer thing* you’ve been riding lately— Is this a phase?  Or are you, like… *gay now*?  Or what the hell’s the deal?

*A beat of silence.*

**JEFF** (sotto, warning)  
Jim…

*KATHY raises an eyebrow. Not offended—just tired. She leans forward, rests her arms on her knees, voice calm but sharp as broken glass.*

**KATHY**  
I’m *very flexible*.  And it’s *none of your fucking business*.

(beat)
But, sure.  Let’s call it out.  I’m not *straight*.  I’m not exactly *queer*, either.  I’m just… me.

(leans back, exhales)
It’s an *Ohio thing*.

**JEREMY** (nods slowly)  
That’s probably the most accurate explanation I've ever heard.

**JIM** (grinning, hands up)  
Alright. Just checking.  You know me—I ask, I learn, I adjust.

**KATHY** (smiles, just barely)  
You adjust like a chainsaw, but sure.

**BILL**  
You’re basically a sensitivity training wrapped in a drumstick.

**GILLEY**  
Don’t worry, Kathy. If anyone comes at you sideways, we’ll write a three-minute synth revenge anthem and release it on vinyl only.

**KATHY**  
Perfect.  Make it weird.  Make it sweaty.

*The tension dissolves—not erased, but metabolized. This is a band. A family. A mess.*  They may not *get it*, but they’ll *fight for her anyway*.  And Kathy?  Kathy’s just fine being the only person who really knows *what she is*.

---

## **INT. SPA LOUNGE – SAME EVENING**

The laughter’s died down again. The spa haze is a little looser now—like truth is drifting in with the eucalyptus.

**KATHY** (suddenly, fully upright, voice clear and direct)  
You know what?  Let me lay this all the way out. Right here. Right now.  I’m a third-wave feminist.  
I don’t owe anyone a fixed label, a punchline, or a *comfortable definition*.  If I want to fuck women, men, or *whatever's emotionally stable enough to pay for dinner and shut the fuck up afterward*, *I will.*  Because I can.  Because I want to.  And because I’ve earned it.

(beat)
*Thank you.*

Dead silence. Everyone stares. Not in shock—just deep respect. And then…

**JEFF** (tilting his head)  
So does that mean we gotta go see *Camille Paglia* lecture again?  Because—listen—she was hot for like ten minutes, but after that it was just kind of a spiral into disappointment.  Not a *single* tank battle.  Nothing exploded.  And at no point did we cover the *defenestration of Prague*.

*Beat.*

**JEREMY** (low voice)  
God, the Prague thing again.

**JIM**  
He’s not wrong. I wanted explosions and feminist artillery. All we got was a monologue about Madonna’s pelvis and a fight with the bookstore clerk.

**KATHY** (grinning, not even mad)  
Y’all are unwell.

**GILLEY**  
Didn’t she call herself a “dissident of the left” and then quote *Rush Limbaugh*?

**BILL**  
And somehow still managed to not bring up laser cannons, which seems like a waste.

**CREMEANS** (walking in just in time)  
Are we arguing about Paglia again?

**KATHY**  
Jeff brought her up. I was making a point about sexual autonomy and not needing anyone’s permission to fuck across the spectrum.

**CREMEANS**  
Good.  Now please, for the love of my migraine, don’t say “fuck across the spectrum” again while I’m holding a clipboard.

*They all laugh. Even Kathy. She’s still glowing—truth told, stakes claimed, and not a single apology in the air.*

He said fuck.  They heard it.  And they’re still here.  Because that’s this band: *messy, loud, wrong sometimes… but never afraid of the truth*.

---

## **INT. SPA LOUNGE – EVENING, POST-TRUTH, POST-TEA, NOW FULL DEGEN MODE**

Everyone’s draped across spa furniture like post-battle philosophers. The mood is *loose*. **Kathy** just dropped her sexual sovereignty mic. Silence lingers.

And then—

**JIM** (squinting at her, mock-accusatory)  
Okay, but real talk?  We gotta talk about your *accent*, Kathy.

**KATHY** (eyebrows raised)  
Oh no.

**JIM**  
It’s an *Ohio accent*, yeah, but every now and then?  You *dip*.  Just the tiniest *little* slip of Kentucky crawls out your mouth like it paid rent.

(imitating her)  
*“Y’all need to back up.”*  “*Y’all*.”  Kathy.  It’s *you all.*  This ain’t *coal country Shakespeare*.

**KATHY** (arms crossed, grinning)  
You got a lot of mouth for someone who says *wooter* instead of *water*.

**JIM**  
Oh no no no. Don’t redirect.  Let’s talk about the **Evans brothers** for a minute.

(turns to **Jeff** and **Jeremy**, mock horror growing)
Y’all’s *Midwestern accents*?  *Jesus H. banjo Christ.*  Sometimes it's like Appalachia rolled itself into a **Meijer’s parking lot** and begged for a record deal.

**JEFF** (half-smiling)  
We’re just giving the people what they expect: trauma and good diction.

**JIM**  
*Good diction?!*  You say “*deeshes*.”

(he stands, performs like he’s in court)
That’s not D-I-S-H-E-S.  That’s D-E-E-S-H-S.  **“Deeshes.”**  And then the goddamn crown jewel:  
**“deeshwarshers.”**  *There is no R in dishwasher\!*

(screaming to the ceiling)  
**FUCKIN’ FUCK, GUYS\!**

**GILLEY** (sliding off a chaise, laughing hysterically)  
You sound like you need a drink and a speech therapist.

**BILL**  
I once heard Jeremy say “melk.”  I thought it was a joke. It wasn’t.

**JEREMY** (defensive)  
It’s a *regional vowel dip*! It’s *cultural\!*

**KATHY**  
I grew up ten minutes from three trailer parks and an abandoned Arby’s. You want me to sound like Cate Blanchett?

**JIM**  
Honestly? Yes. Just once. I want you to look me dead in the eyes and say *“wherefore art thou, y’all?”*

*The room is now howling. Pillows are flying. Someone spills tea. A eucalyptus candle dies quietly in the chaos.*

**CREMEANS** (passing through again, dry as dust)  
I swear, the accents get stronger when you’re relaxed. Like possums in warm weather.

**KATHY** (grinning)  
Say “deeshes” again, and I’m writing a song called “Rinse Cycle of Shame.”

**JIM**  
And I’ll add *Kentucky banjo-core breakdowns*. Let’s go.

---

## **INT. SPA LOUNGE – NIGHT**

Steam fading. Teacups empty. Muscles relaxed.  The gang has dissolved into **total Midwestern linguistic anarchy**.  Accents roasted. Regional pride wounded. **Kathy** is still threatening to write *“Rinse Cycle of Shame.”*  Then, **GILLEY** leans forward—eyes twinkling, grinning like a man about to set fire to *peace itself*.

**GILLEY** (slow, dangerous)  
I can detonate *six people* at the same time.

*Everyone freezes.*

**KATHY** (suspicious)  
With *what*?

**JIM**  
If it involves your harmonica again, we’re gonna have a problem.

**JEFF** (skeptical, arms folded)  
How the *hell* are you going to cause *six people* to explode at once, bro?

**GILLEY** (winks)  
Watch.

(he casually notions over to one of the spa staff walking by)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
Excuse me— I’ll take a *soda*, please.

*The room goes dead silent for half a second—*

Then:

**ALL (IN UNISON):**  
*It’s POP, FUCKHEAD\!*

**GILLEY** (stands, bows)  
You made my point.  Peace.

*He strolls out of the room, towel over his shoulder, like a victorious prophet leaving a collapsed temple.*

**JEFF**  (to no one)  
You know what?  I hate that he’s right.

**KATHY**  
I hate that I yelled it.

**CREMEANS** (entering on cue)  
Did someone just start a regional dialect war again?

---

## **INT. SPA LOUNGE – AFTERMATH OF THE “POP” INCIDENT**

Everyone’s settled back in after Gilley’s soda-bomb mic drop.  There’s a moment of reflection. Of shared trauma. Of… *curiosity.*

**JEFF** (squinting toward the door Gilley just swaggered through)  
Okay, but like—real question.  How long ago did Gilley *actually* move from L.A. to Clark County?  Because he does *not* sound like someone from the 310.  He sounds like he was raised in a field full of Snapple bottles and car parts.

**JEREMY** (sipping his tea, noncommittal)  
Probably kindergarten?

**JEFF**  
Nah.  *First grade.*

**JEREMY** (surprised)  
How do *you* know?

**JEFF**  
Because I *remember*.  He showed up with a “California” t-shirt and a lunchbox with *Space Jam* on it.

(beat)
Also, he pronounced “Nevada” wrong, and my mom said, *“Yup, new kid’s from the coast.”*

**KATHY** (blinking)  
Wait—hold up.  *That guy was born in L.A.?*

**JIM**  
Supposedly.

**KATHY**  
No.  No way.  What part? Like… actual L.A.? *Orange County?*

**JEREMY** (shrugs, a little too vague)  
I mean… maybe?  I’ve never really… *dug that deep* into Gilley’s bio.

**BILL**  
You mean to tell me you’ve shared microphones, hotel rooms, and *custody of multiple synths* with a man whose birth certificate location is *unconfirmed*?

**CREMEANS** (deadpan, from the doorway)  
I tried to run a background check once. The trail ends around a Little League trophy and a photo of him at Knott’s Berry Farm.

**KATHY** (disbelieving)  
He’s a *legend*, and we don’t know if he’s *Inglewood or Irvine*?

**JEFF**  
He *claims* his mom lived in Silver Lake for a bit, but I’ve heard him say “holler” without irony.

**JIM**  
His *accent* is so Clark County it should come with a four-wheeler and a gas station burrito.

*They all sit in silence, considering the truth:* **Gilley may be a myth.**  **But his backstory?**  *It’s folklore.*

**JEREMY**  
Next tour… I’m stealing his Social Security number.

**KATHY**  
If it starts with a 5, I’ll believe him.

**JEFF**  
If it starts with “classified,” I’m *calling the FBI.*

---

## **INT. SPA LOUNGE – MINUTES LATER**

The gang is *still spinning* from the Gilley origin investigation. A pause in the air—conspiratorial silence.

Then, like *clockwork chaos*—**GILLEY** re-enters.

Same robe.  Same smug strut.  Holding what *may or may not* be a pilfered spa cookie.

**GILLEY** (to Jeremy, no context needed)  
You know, considering you have the *same mother* as Jeff— maybe drink *less* wine and more soda.

(beat)
For bone density.  And moral clarity.

*Jeremy blinks.*

**JEREMY**  
What?

**GILLEY** (ignoring him, launching into the middle of a long-simmering declaration)  
See, that’s the problem. Nobody respects **greatness** anymore.  I mean—**Marcus Allen. Jim Plunkett.**  The **1983 Los Angeles Raiders** were the *apex* of football and American male identity.

(he’s pacing now)
People talk about dynasty? Talk about legacy?  *They beat Washington 38 to 9.*    They *obliterated* the league. Defense like religion.  Speed. Violence. Swagger. The silver and black was a *philosophy*.

(beat)
**“Just Win, Baby.”**  It’s not just a motto.  It’s my *second-most important core value.*

**KATHY** (sighing, but smiling)  
I hesitate to ask what the *first* core value is.

(beat)
Does it involve removing women’s panties?

**GILLEY** (grinning)  
I mean…What *else* could be the best in life?

**JIM** (sits up, solemn, then with sudden precision—launches into a thick, deliberate Austrian accent)

> [!danger] **QUOTING CONAN**
> *“To crush your enemies…”*  
> *“To see them drawn forth before you…”*  
> *“And to hear the lamentations of their women.”*

*He folds his arms. The room loses it.*

**KATHY**  
Jesus, that was so good it shaved my legs.

**JEFF**  
That wasn’t an impression. That was *channeling*.

**BILL**  
You didn’t just quote Conan. You *summoned* him.

**CREMEANS** (entering, again, somehow always entering)  
Is this a football debate, a cult initiation, or a film studies class at Wright State?

**GILLEY**  
All of the above.

**JIM** (raises his glass)  
To victory.

**GILLEY**  
To the Raiders.

**KATHY**  
To panty removal, I guess.

**JEREMY**  
To soda, apparently.

**JEFF**  
To the lamentations of their women.

*They clink glasses. Robes. Spa sweat. Banter. Myth.*  Because only **Commuted** could make *Raiders fandom, Conan quotes, and gender politics* feel like a family dinner.

---

## **INT. SPA LOUNGE – NIGHT PUSHING INTO ABSURDITY**

The robes remain. The lighting is soft. Someone’s queued up a spa playlist that now sounds *suspiciously epic*, like it’s waiting for a broadsword.

**JEREMY** (stretching, eyes gleaming)  
Okay.  Real question.  Who here could actually *co-star* in a Conan movie?  Like, if Conan needed a sidekick? Someone to ride a horse, kill a warlock, maybe pose in leather?

*Everyone pauses.*

**JEFF** (flatly)  
It’s not me.  I’ve got the endurance of a sick librarian and the fight choreography of a napkin.

**KATHY** (thinking)  
I could probably do it… But let’s be honest, they’d want to show my tits in the second scene.

So—*that’s out.*

**JIM** (pensively)  
I’m probably too much of an accountant.  Like, I’d be the guy Conan meets in a tavern who says, "Do you really need that enchanted ax? It’s not deductible in most provinces.”

*Laughter.*

**JEFF**  
Yeah, you’d die in act one and your ledger would be found smoldering in the wreckage.

**JEREMY**  
But *Bill*…

(turns dramatically)
*Bill* could do it.

**EVERYONE turns to BILL.**

He’s leaning against a chaise lounge. Robe hanging open just enough to reveal **actual muscle tone**, looking like a lost member of a synthwave boy band.

**GILLEY** (awed)  
He’s got the build.

**JIM**  
He’s buff.

**JEFF**  
And that *luxury hair*… It’s *insulting*.

**KATHY** (squinting)  
That hair’s not out of the 80s.  It’s out of the **70s**.

**BILL** (quietly)  
I condition.

**CREMEANS** (to no one, under his breath)  
He’s like if Fabio did calculus.

**KATHY**  
You’d play Conan’s mysterious ally who doesn’t talk until the last act, then says something *profound* like—*“The blade only sings for those who bleed.”*

**BILL**  
Or I’d just play the horse.

**JIM**  
We’d all be the horses, Bill.

**JEREMY**  
Speak for yourself. I’m playing the talking skull that gives bad advice.

*They’re howling now. The spa’s closing down. But they don’t care. They’ve written themselves into sword-and-sorcery legend, and Bill’s already halfway cast.*

**GILLEY**  
Wait… who’s directing this?

**KATHY** (smiling)  
*I am.*  And everyone dies except me.

---

## **INT. SPA LOUNGE – NIGHT, FINAL PHASE: DELIRIUM AND TRUTH**

The lights are dim. The air smells like lavender and ego. The last spa attendant has wisely retreated. Empty glasses and wild declarations litter the room.

**KATHY** (sitting cross-legged, robe tied like a battle sash)  
Jeremy.

(leans in)
Give me some *bad advice*.  I don’t care what the fuck it’s about.  I just want a **ton** of bad advice.  I promise I will *try* to follow it…*unless I’m already doing it.*

**JEREMY** (leans forward like a cursed oracle)
Alright.  Number one—**get bangs**.  Not a trim. *Full, regrettable bangs.* Right before an album cover shoot.

**KATHY**  
Writing that down.

**JEREMY**  
Two—text your ex.  The *second* one.  The one who thinks crystals control time.

**KATHY**  
I did that *last week.*

**JEREMY**  
You’re thriving already.  Three—quit music and open a boutique salt shop.  No signage. Just a locked door and a velvet rope.

**GILLEY** (awed)  
That's… kind of brilliant.

**JEREMY**  
Four—buy a jet ski with *cash*.

**JIM**  
She doesn’t live near water.

**JEREMY**  
Even better.  Five—sleep with someone whose name you can’t pronounce.  On purpose.

**KATHY**  
Done.  Regretted it.

**JEFF**  
Wasn’t that the guy from Berlin?

**KATHY**  
He said it like “Charnald.”  It was spelled with *three silent Gs*.

**JEREMY**  
Six—if anyone gives you relationship advice, respond with “thanks, Dad” even if it’s a stranger.  Seven—buy a sword and carry it at airports.  Just say it’s for “emotional protection.”

**BILL**  
You’ll be arrested.

**KATHY**  
Only if you *break character.*

**JEREMY**  
Eight—when in doubt, tattoo the doubt.

**CREMEANS**  
What does that even mean?

**JEREMY** (shrugging)  
See? It’s already working.

**KATHY** (sighing happily)  
God, you’re so *stupid*.  Thank you.

**JEREMY**  
I aim to mislead.

*They collapse into laughter. Deep, exhausted, earned.*  Because **bad advice from Jeremy** is still better than *good advice* from most people.

---

## **INT. SPA LOUNGE – VERY LATE NIGHT**

The laughter’s dying. The robes are getting itchy. The water feature has looped its calming trickle one too many times. Empty teacups everywhere. Someone’s foot is in a potted plant.

**CREMEANS**  (clapping once, too loud, voice fraying at the edges)  
Alright, children of eucalyptus and nonsense—Just because our next tour date is in *Baltimore* doesn’t mean we don’t have to *get back on the dang bus* and *get down the interstate.*

(beat)
Because *uh-huh*, I can only take so much of this.  I can only take so much of *this.*

*He gestures broadly at the robes, the spa, the psychic ruin of Gilley’s Raiders monologue and Jeremy’s bean sprout tattoo.*

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**  
Let’s get going.

*The band starts rising, slowly, groaning like reanimated corpses in thousand-thread-count cotton.*

**JIM** (stretching)  
Kathy, seriously…thanks.  It was completely worthless.

**JEFF**  
No productivity. No structure. No assets gained.

**BILL**  
I did not learn a single musical thing.

**JEREMY**  
I might’ve lost IQ points, actually.

**GILLEY**  
And I have never been more hydrated in my life, which feels like betrayal.

(beat)
But…

**ALL (almost in unison):**  
It was a *great time bonding.*

**KATHY** (smug as hell, robe flowing like a Roman senator)  
You’re welcome.

*They shuffle out one by one, each giving her a pat on the shoulder, a nod, a grin. No one says it, but they all feel it—*That was **the break they didn’t know they needed**.

**CREMEANS** (following them out, mumbling)  
Next time I’m bringing horse tranquilizers. For *me*.

*The spa doors close. The lights dim. The silence returns.*  Until the next show.  Until the next explosion.  Until *Baltimore*.

**FADE OUT.  TEXT ON SCREEN:** *Commuted returns to the road. Hydrated. Unrepentant. Slightly more moisturized than before.*

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – SOMEWHERE ON I-95 – NIGHT**

The bus hums along, dimly lit, packed with after-spa debris—half-empty water bottles, rolled-up robes, and *spiritual detritus* from a day of cucumber therapy and Gilley’s monologues.  
**CREMEANS** is at the tiny kitchenette, grumbling over a clipboard, muttering to himself about venue curfews and “Baltimore parking hell.”  **JEFF** sits on the bench, strumming quietly on an unplugged travel guitar, eyebrows low, voice dead calm.  

**JEFF**  
Hey, Cremeans.

(beat)
I just want to *strongly caution* you. It would probably be a really fucking *bad idea*—and I mean, on a scale of 1 to 10, this is a *solid 6*…

(leans forward)
Maybe even like a **Hindenburg exploding** level bad idea…To bring *horse tranquilizers* onto this bus. With *people like me* on it.

**CREMEANS**  (defensive, exhausted)  
It was *a joke*, Jeff.

**JEFF**  
Was it? Because you said it with the voice of a man who’s read about ketamine on WebMD and liked what he saw.

**CREMEANS**  
It was for *me*, Jeff. Me.  Do you know how long I’ve been carrying this band’s spiritual luggage?

**JEFF**  
That’s nice.

(beat)
Let’s just… keep the horse tranqs *off* the bus. No syringes. No paste. No powder.  Not even a *pamphlet*, man.

(quietly)
*I* know what I’m capable of in a depressive spiral.

**GILLEY** (from the back, loud)  
If anyone’s gonna be sedated on this bus, it’s *me*, and I want it to be *romantic*, not *livestock-related*\!

**KATHY** (lying on her bunk, muffled)  
If I see so much as a hoof print on this floor, I’m calling PETA and your mom.

**JIM**  
Horse tranqs on a tour bus… yeah, that’s the beginning of a Netflix documentary, not a band memoir.

**JEFF** (flat, to Cremeans)  
Let’s keep our vices human.  That’s all I’m saying.

**CREMEANS** (fading into his seat, muttering)  
Stupid musicians.  Can’t even threaten light chemical sedation without a moral inquisition.

*Silence. Then the rumble of the bus.* The whole band, still buzzing. Still weird. Still alive.  And—thankfully—**tranquilizer-free**.

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – NIGHT – HALFWAY BETWEEN PHILLY AND BALTIMORE**

The cabin is dim.  Streetlights arc past the windows like comets.  The only sound is the low drone of the engine and the occasional rattle of some unsecured object in the kitchenette. **KATHY** leans against the narrow hallway wall, arms crossed, eyes focused. She's in a hoodie, barefoot, tension coiled in her shoulders like a second spine.

Across from her, **JEFF** sits in the lounge seat near the window. Headphones in, not listening to music—just *silence* with insulation. He sees her. He pulls one bud out.

**JEFF**  
Yeah?

**KATHY** (low, steady)  
I want my own bus.

(beat)
Later on this tour.  I’m not asking for a marble bathtub or a gold espresso machine.  I just… want space.  To think.  To sleep.  To *not* be in a tin can with six farts and Gilley’s shirtless existentialism.

*Jeff blinks, slowly.*

**JEFF**  (sincere)  
Fair.

(beat)
Are you okay?

**KATHY**  
Yeah.  Just tired. Tired of being *on* every second. Tired of being the only girl in a frat house built from trauma and B minor.

**JEFF** (smiles slightly)  
That’d be a good lyric.

**KATHY**  
Then write it down.  Just not on *my* bus.

*Silence stretches. The engine hums. They pass a burned-out rest stop with a flickering sign.*

**JEFF** (slowly)  
You deserve it.  We’ll figure it out.

**KATHY**  
Thanks.  And don’t take it personal. I love you guys.  I just also love *doors that close* and *mirrors that don’t fog up with testosterone.*

**JEFF**  
Trust me.  We’ll all sleep better knowing we’re not gonna walk in on you shaving your legs while threatening Jim with a hot spoon.

**KATHY**  
That was *one time.*

**JEFF**  
It was *legendary.*

They sit in companionable silence as Maryland rolls by—dead warehouses, sodium lights, and forgotten factories that look like they gave up in 1976.

**KATHY** (quietly)  
Thanks for not arguing.

**JEFF**  
We’re too old for drama. And you’ve earned the hell out of your own square footage.

*They watch the night blur past the window, saying nothing more.* It’s late. It’s honest.  It’s friendship without decoration.

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – STILL NIGHT – A FEW MILES FROM BALTIMORE**

**JEFF** leans back in his seat, arms folded, gaze fixed out the window at the glowing carcasses of truck stops and sleeping steel towns.

**JEFF** (low, measured)  
You want your own bus? Then should talk to **Cremeans**. He’s the one who signs the check and takes the blame when shit hits the fan.  You know the drill.

*He doesn’t say it with bitterness.*  *Just with that bone-deep, Jeff-brand **honesty** that feels like a blade in a velvet case.*

**KATHY** (silent a moment)  
Yeah.  Okay.

### **INT. REST STOP – LATER THAT NIGHT**

Everyone else is asleep or pretending to be.  **KATHY** finds **CREMEANS** sitting outside the bus on a metal bench, clipboard balanced on his knee like always. The sodium lights above buzz like bad decisions.

**KATHY** (quiet)  
Got a second?

*Cremeans doesn’t look up. Doesn’t nod. Just flips a page and holds up a finger. Finishes his note. Then closes the clipboard with deliberate finality.* He looks up. His face is carved out of worry and discipline.

**CREMEANS** (quiet, sharp)  
You want your own bus.

**KATHY**  
Yeah.

**CREMEANS** (beat)  
You know why you *don’t* have one?

*Silence.*

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**  
Because we’re still **watching you.** Because no one’s gonna say it out loud on a spa day or between soundcheck and setlist, but—

(voice like steel)
We’re still trying to figure out if you’re going to start **using again.**

*The wind blows. Maryland’s nothingness hums behind them.*

**KATHY** (stiffening, jaw clenched)  
That’s not fair.

**CREMEANS**  
It’s not about fair.  It’s about **alive.** You know what happens if you relapse on a solo bus, and no one’s there to stop you?  You become a headline.  You become a *tribute montage* at the Grammys with someone singing one of your songs *off-key*.  And I’m not letting that happen again. Not on *my* watch.

*They lock eyes. It’s not anger. It’s love with a fuse.*

**KATHY** (low, shaking)  
I’m not her anymore.

**CREMEANS**  
Then prove it. Stay clean.  Stay close.  You’ll get your bus. You’ll get *everything*.

He stands, clipboard back under arm, and walks to the bus without another word.  Kathy stays on the bench. Breathing. Shaking. Thinking.

A long, brutal beat of silence.

**KATHY (V.O.)**  
Maybe I’m not her anymore.  But they still see her.  And maybe… sometimes, I do too.

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – KATHY’S BUNK – 4:03 A.M.**

She’s awake.  Lying flat on her back, eyes open, headphones in but nothing playing.  A bottle of water half-drunk. Her notebook on her chest, unopened. The hum of the bus is steady, but inside her chest, it’s *rattling*.

**KATHY (V.O.)**  
Off heroin since ‘98.  Off heroin since that *godawful 120 Minutes* OD backstage in Toledo that nobody can talk about.  Not even in jokes.

*She stares at the ceiling. The bunk lights above her flicker like a glitch in a confession.*

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**  
It wasn’t dramatic.  It wasn’t poetic.  It was just *ugly.*  Cold sweat. Seizure.  The EMT called me “sweetheart” and I bit him. That’s the part they *don’t* put in the documentaries.

She rolls onto her side, eyes scanning the dark.

**KATHY (V.O.)**  
But coke? Coke is a different beast. Not on a first-name basis with me.  But we’ve carpooled. Same playlists.  Same bars.  Same fucking dressing room drawer that’s always unlocked when you *don’t* want it to be.

*She closes her eyes. Tight. Like the darkness is safer than the memory.*

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**  
I don’t *use* anymore.  But I still think about it like an old boyfriend who’s gotten hot again.  I smell it sometimes.  Even when it’s not there.

*Silence. Just the rumble of Maryland passing.*

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**  
Cremeans thinks I’m still dangerous. Maybe I am. But danger isn’t a relapse. It’s a decision.  And I’m *deciding* every damn day.

*She opens her notebook. Writes four words:* *“I am not her.”*

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – KATHY’S BUNK – 4:19 A.M.**

She hasn't moved.  Not really. Notebook still open.  Water untouched.  Her robe draped over the side like it gave up first.

**KATHY (V.O.)**  
I haven’t touched coke in a *week*.

(beat)
But that was almost *eight months ago*, too.  So which number do I believe?

Her hand moves absentmindedly across the page. She’s not writing. She’s *remembering*.

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**  
I’m not *using*.  I’m just *wired*.  And tired.  And… watching myself like I owe me an apology I haven’t written yet.

A long pause.  Bus hum.  Distant sound of **Jim** snoring through his mouth like a minor traffic accident.

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**  
The *patriarchy* can’t handle the choices I make.  That’s what I tell myself.  That I’m *reclaiming something*.  That every manic set, every weird interview, every open wound in a song is a *strategy*.

She exhales. It shudders out of her.

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**  
I’m sure **Jeff** is spying on me. I’m *sure* of it.  Or not. Maybe he’s just paying attention.  Which is worse?

She shifts, frustrated, like the mattress is lying to her.

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**  
Maybe after the stadium tour ends… I’ll take a break.  Not rehab. Not another *statement*.   Just a *pause*.  Get some help.  Or just… get a *better fucking opening act* so I’m not carrying the whole show like a burned-out Joan of Arc with eyeliner and half a throat.  She laughs softly to herself. It’s not a happy sound.

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**  
I’m so damn wired and tired.  It’s like my blood is carbonated.  Like I’m living one BPM too fast.

She closes the notebook.  Rolls over. Stares at the wall. Eyes wide open. *Nothing left to say to the dark.*

---

## **EXT. M&T BANK STADIUM – LOADING DOCK – EARLY AFTERNOON**

The crew is unloading gear. It’s humid, overcast, and the massive stadium looms like a *concrete spaceship dipped in electric grape Kool-Aid*. Everything is purple—the signage, the seats, even the lighting rig they're testing feels *absurdly violet*. **BILL** steps off the bus in shades and a sleeveless hoodie, blinking at the venue like it personally offended him.

**BILL**  (low, half to himself)  
It’s really…*freaking purple* in here.   Like, *aggressively* purple.

**JEFF**  (suddenly grinning)  
Hey, Bill. Got an idea. *Deep Purple.*

(beat)
What can you do with that?

**BILL**  (tilts his head, considering)
You mean like… the *band*?

**JEFF**  
Sure. Or the color. Or the mood.  Or a new religion.  I just want to see what happens when you get *inspired by this much ultraviolet vengeance.*

**BILL** (smirking now)  
Alright. I might just flex a little.

*He walks off toward his rig like a man on a mission—something dark, synthy, and majestic cooking in his head.*

---

## **INT. STAGE AREA – HOURS LATER – SOUNDCHECK**

Bill sits behind his setup—synth fortress glowing like a digital cathedral.  He’s laid in a new **opening drone** for the night: something slow, menacing, *regal*, and purple as hell.  Pads that shimmer like stained glass. A sub-bass note that *feels like royalty losing its mind*.

**JIM** (whistles from behind the drum kit)  
You weren’t kidding.  That’s Deep Purple meets a cathedral built by androids.

**KATHY**  
It sounds like *glam apocalypse*.

**GILLEY**  
It sounds like what would happen if Prince fought a dragon… and won.

**JEFF**  (nodding)  
Good. Let’s make Baltimore *remember this color*.

---

## **INT. STAGE – M&T BANK STADIUM – LATE AFTERNOON**

The sun’s dipped low. The **LED rigs** buzz faintly. Simple setup—clean, sharp, tight whites and purples.  *High-def control meets minimalism.*  This isn’t about spectacle. This is about **color as weapon**.

**CREW MEMBER** (to lighting op)  
Keep it clean. Violet main wash. Punch accents in midtempo.  Let it breathe.  It’s not a disco ball. It’s a *funeral for subtlety.*

### **INT. DRESSING ROOM – SAME TIME**

**KATHY** stands in front of a mirror with **WARDROBE** behind her, methodically applying **plum lipstick** like it’s battle paint.

**KATHY** (quiet, pleased)  
This is fucking *delicious*, Connie.

*The color is bold, rich, with the right amount of danger. A little noir, a little riot.*

**WARDROBE LEAD**  
We have six backup tubes.

**KATHY**  
If the set collapses and the power fails, I’ll still be standing, lips first.

### **INT. STAGE – SOUNDCHECK BEGINS**

The band steps into place. **BILL** triggers the opening swell. The **Deep Purple theme** surges from his rig:  *Velvety synths, low-end menace, cathedral reverb with a touch of war.*

**JIM** counts in on snare taps—loose but surgical. **JEFF** joins on bass, finding the groove that cuts through the drone like a pulse. **GILLEY** tests his mic with a slow, sinister spoken line.  It echoes. It *lands*. And **KATHY**? She walks out slowly, lips already stained deep plum, eyes locked on the empty stadium like it’s prey.  No sound.  Then she sings a single line. No context.  No explanation.

*“We’re still breathing in the ruins.”*

The sound cuts like silk over concrete.

**CREMEANS** (off to the side, arms folded)  
Yup. That’s gonna work.

**JEREMY** (to no one in particular)  
I wonder how the rest of this soundcheck’s gonna go.

**JEFF** (same tone)  
We all do.  That’s why we *have them.*

*The music grows.*  *The purple grows.*  *The soundcheck becomes more than a test.*  *It becomes **foreshadowing.***

---

## **INT. STAGE – M&T BANK STADIUM – SOUND CHECK CONTINUES**

The drone is still humming. Lights are testing strobes. Kathy’s mic is hot. Gilley’s pacing in his boots, working out if he’s going to make the crowd cry or riot.

**BILL** (twisting a knob, then real casual)  
Let’s work in **“Speed King.”**  That’s *really* Deep Purple.

*Everyone turns. Slight pause.*

**JEFF** (grins)  
Seriously?

**BILL** (Shrugs)
Why not? Big. Loud. Chaos in 4/4. Synth version of a blown amp.  I could *murder* that riff with Moog brass.

**JIM** (snorting)  
You know the lyrics?

**BILL** (flat)  
No.  Ask Jeeves.

*Beat.*

**KATHY** (eyes narrowing)  
You’re *kidding*.

**BILL** (smirking)  
Mostly.

**GILLEY**  
Only guy on earth who could say *“ask Jeeves”* and mean it as a joke *and* a threat.

**JEREMY**  
What’s the plan? We butcher it, rewire it, and call it a tribute?

**BILL**  
We don’t cover it. We *hijack it*.

*Kathy nods slowly, already hearing it in her head—slowed down, more ritual, more danger.*

**KATHY**  
We open with it.

**JEFF**  
No intro. No speech. Just drop in like a bomb.

**CREMEANS** (offstage, clipboard in hand)  
Do I even *want* to know what’s happening?

**ALL (in unison):**  
*No.*

*They launch into a test—Bill hitting the core riff on synth, dropping the speed to a crawl, making it sound like it’s *coming from beneath the stadium.*  It doesn’t just work.  It *mutates.*

---

## **INT. BACKSTAGE GREEN ROOM – M&T BANK STADIUM – NIGHT**

Lights hum overhead. Cases of gear line the walls. Stage rumble seeps through the concrete. Everyone’s half-dressed, half-zoned out, sipping electrolytes or muttering lyrics to themselves.  **CREMEANS** stands dead center, holding the clipboard like a shield against chaos.

**CREMEANS**  
Okay. Here’s a thought.  A *revolutionary concept*, even. What if—just *this once*—we *stick to the setlist*? We agreed to this in *March*.  They asked us out. We confirmed.  We *printed merch* with the order, for God’s sake.

**JEFF** (sitting on a flight case, rubbing his temple)  
Cremeans…We’ve been at this for *five and a half months*.  Same shows, same songs, same filler stage banter. Every night.  Every other night. *Same old, same old.*

(beat)
We’re tired. We’re *ready to go home.*

**JEREMY**  (from the couch, eyes closed)  
Amen.

**JIM** (sits up, smiling)  
But Giants Stadium? That was *everything* to me.  That was a *career high point*. That moment—what we pulled off— that validated everything I ever said about this band.

**BILL** (nods, tone calm but charged)  
And I want to do it *again*. Not the same song. Not the same stunt.  Something *wild*.  Something that reminds us this isn’t just a job.

*He looks up.*

And if it’s not tonight…

(beat)
Then it’s in *Charlotte*. That’s where we end, right?

**JEFF** (sighs, nods)  
Yeah. Charlotte. Final stop.

**CREMEANS** (flat, dry)  
I love how “final stop” never feels *final* with you people.

**KATHY** (stretching, pulling on her boots)  
It’s not about disrespecting the setlist, Cremeans. It’s about *escaping it*.  *Owning* it. And maybe, just maybe… leaving the crowd with a version of us they weren’t expecting.

**JEFF** (grinning at her)  
Spoken like a woman who’s not going home to Cincinnati.

**KATHY**  
Cincinnati *is* the escape plan. Don’t tempt me.

*Silence. Cremeans stares at the clipboard, sighs, and folds it shut.*

**CREMEANS**  
Fine. But if we go off-script tonight, someone better catch fire on stage.  I want *drama*.  I want *insurance claims*.

**JIM**  
Deal.

*They start heading toward the tunnel.*  *Purple light builds from the stage.*

**BILL (quietly, to Jeff):**  
Charlotte’s gonna be insane.

**JEFF**  
If I survive Baltimore first.

---

## **INT. BACKSTAGE TUNNEL – M&T BANK STADIUM – MINUTES TO SHOW**

They’re half-suited, half-wired, waiting for their cue.  Bill’s fiddling with a patch cable.  Kathy’s lacing her boots with muscle memory and contempt.  The purple LED wash is already flooding the tunnel.

**JIM** (stretching, grinning)  
I’ve seen her *skinny naked ass* all over *Cincinnati*.  Don’t you forget it.

**KATHY** (eye roll weaponized)  
Oh, for *fuck’s* sake.

**JIM**  
Playboy, downtown newsstand. *May issue*. Right next to the Marlboros and day-old muffins.

**KATHY**  
It was *tasteful.*

**JEFF** (grinning, not looking up)  
Yeah, I remember how that *tastes*.

*Instant silence.*

**KATHY** (turning, voice flat, deadly calm)  
Jeff.

*Beat.*

**KATHY (CONT’D)**  
*Boundaries.* Or I’m gonna kick you in the *ass*.  And not in the fun way.

**JEFF** (hands up, mock-innocent)  
Noted.

**GILLEY** (from off to the side)  
That’s why the *centerfold crease* still lives in my tour binder.

**JEREMY**  
Yeah, and that’s why you’re not allowed to pack merch anymore.

**CREMEANS** (stepping in like a substitute teacher sick of it all)  
Okay!  We’re about to walk into 60,000 people and purple stage fire. Maybe let’s *not* sexually harass each other before we hit the chorus?

**KATHY** (grinning as she throws on her mic pack)  
I’ll take that under advisement.

*The band lines up at the edge of the stage. The roar of the crowd swells.* And behind the jokes, behind the jabs, there’s love.  *Brutal, weird, totally inappropriate love.*  That’s what makes them work. Even on their *last nerve*. Even on their second-to-last show.

---

## **INT. STAGE RIGHT – M&T BANK STADIUM – SECONDS BEFORE CURTAIN**

The purple floodlights pulse like *blood through a stained-glass heart*.  The crowd is deafening, a wave about to break. The band huddles in the wings—tight circle, shoulder to shoulder, sweat already starting to bead.

**JIM** (arms raised, eyes closed like a Southern preacher)  
Sweet Baby Jesus…

We come before you and *beseech*…

(beat)  
Let our grooves be *wicked*,  Our asses *shake freely*,  And, uh…I don’t know, help me out, guys. I haven’t done the Sweet Baby Jesus pregame show pep talk in a *long* time.

**KATHY** (smiling, loose)  
Let’s just let rip.

**BILL**  
You know how to start it.

**JEFF**  
Make the *Navy* feel it out there in *Nullfark*.

**JEREMY** (grinning, stretching)  
Yeah. I’m gonna blow *somebody’s* eardrums out tonight.  Like, *legally*.

**JIM** (eyes wide, pulling them all tighter)  
Okay. All right. All right. *Let’s get settled*.

(beat)
Now—on *four*.

**JIM (CONT’D)**  
One.  Two.  Three.  Four—

**ALL** (roaring, fierce, unstoppable)
***COMMITTED!!***

*The lights drop.*  *The purple surges.*  *The synth drone rises like a battle hymn.*  *Baltimore’s about to learn something eternal.*

---

## **INT. STAGE – M&T BANK STADIUM – CURTAIN MOMENTS**

The **purple light surges**.  **Bill** steps onto the platform like a synth-clad god. The opening drone **builds**, massive and cinematic. The crowd **erupts**—a *violent, beautiful roar*. And right behind the curtain—**Jeremy** is frozen.

**JEREMY** (urgent, low, leaning toward Kathy)  
Where the fuck is *Nullfark*?

**KATHY** (blinking)  
What?

**JEREMY**  
Back there.  In the huddle. Jeff said “make the Navy feel it in Nullfark.”

(beat)
Did he mean *Norfolk*?

**KATHY**  (staring toward Jeff, her smile gone)  
Shit.

**JEFF** is at his mic position, blinking under the lights.  He’s *too still*.  His bass hangs just a little *off-center*.  He’s *not moving like Jeff*.

**JEREMY** (to Jim, sharply)
Is he gonna have a *memory episode*?  *On stage?*

**JIM** (eyes scanning, adrenaline rising)  
He hasn’t had one since Miami.  But he also didn’t *misspeak* like that back then.

(beat)
Nullfark isn’t a slip. That’s *scrambled memory*.  That’s *wrong brainwire*.

**CREMEANS** (off-comms, shouting from side stage)  
*Spot’s hot! GO GO GO!*

**The lights hit.**  **The crowd EXPLODES.****Bill** walks out, already deep in the opening bars.**Kathy** follows like a queen with a sword.  **Jeff?** Still *offbeat*. Still blinking.  Still *Jeff—but maybe not*.

**JEREMY** (muttering, staring out at 60,000 screaming people)  
Okay. All right. *Not now, Jeff. Not now.*

---

## **INT. STAGE – M&T BANK STADIUM – MIDWAY THROUGH SHOW**

**Bill’s synth is soaring.**  **Kathy’s voice is razorwire and gospel.**  **Jim and Jeremy are locked in like a two-man thunderstorm.**  **The crowd is *feral*.**  And Jeff?  **He’s playing.**  But it’s *just shy*. A beat late here. A missed slide there.  They slam into the last song of Act I—**"Country Fair Confession."** *It rips. It stomps. It bleeds Americana through a fuzz pedal.* And yet—**Everyone in the band feels it.**  Something’s *missing.*

### **INT. BACKSTAGE – POST-ACT I BREAK**

**Steam. Sweat.** Screaming crowd still echoing.  Jim throws his sticks down onto the rack, breathing hard.

**JIM** (to Bill)  
That was *hot as hell*—  Except the *bottom half was ghosting us*.

**BILL**  
Dead zones in the bridge. Verse two was hanging on *air*.

**KATHY**  
Jeff was **off**.  He *held on*, but those weren’t just skips. That was a *gap*.  It’s like his hands were playing—but his head wasn’t plugged in.

**JEREMY** (quiet, intense)  
He missed *half the bass chords* on *Country Fair Confessions*.  I could *feel* it.  Like he was phoning it in from 1997.

**CREMEANS** (stepping in, clipboard gone, just a concerned manager)  
He’s back in his corner. Sitting. Didn’t grab a towel. Didn’t say a word.

*They all look over.*  **Jeff** is on a road case.  Bass on his lap.  Head down.  *Just…still.*

**KATHY** (slow, firm)  
We finish the show.  But *after*, we figure out what the hell is going on with him. Because that wasn’t just *fatigue*.

---

## **INT. BACKSTAGE – M&T BANK STADIUM – INTERMISSION BETWEEN ACTS**

**The stadium crowd is buzzing**, high from the first act.  The lights are pulsing. The crew is resetting the stage.  But behind the amps, in the shadows, **Jeremy** zeroes in on **Jeff**, who hasn’t moved from his perch on the road case. He walks over, crouches low.

**JEREMY** (quiet, urgent)  
Dude.  What the *fuck* is wrong?

**JEFF** (voice sharp, trembling)  
I’ve got a *migraine*. Not a headache. Not a little pressure.  It feels like someone’s *drilling into my skull from the inside out.*

(leans closer, eyes burning, almost whispering)
The *spots*—those lights? They gotta *go*.  Or I’m gonna *die* on stage.

**JEREMY**  
Jeff—c’mon, man, you’re—

**JEFF**  
No. No no no.  Don’t *talk me down*.

(voice climbing, fast and cracked)
I mean *DIE*, Jeremy. Not a joke.  Not a figure of speech.  Not “ugh, I’m so tired I could die.”  I mean *seizure*.  I mean *drop*.  *Flop like a fucking fish*.  I mean *eyes roll back*, hit the deck, lights out, *DEAD*. You *understand me*?

**JEREMY** (staring, speechless, stunned)  
Jesus, Jeff.

Jeff is shaking.  Not dramatic. Not flailing.  *Controlled collapse* just under the surface.

**JEFF** (softer now, but raw)  
I’m not trying to be a diva.  I’m not trying to derail the show.  But I’m in *agony*, man.  And I don’t have a lot of runway left.

(beat)
We gotta pull the spots.  Or I’m gonna *die*.  And I *don’t want to die in Baltimore.*

**JEREMY** (silent, eyes scanning Jeff’s face)
Okay.  Okay, okay. Just—*stay here*.  I’ll go talk to Cremeans.  We’ll fix it.

*Jeremy stands fast, his pulse pounding. The brother banter’s gone. This is fear now. Full-blown, cold fear.* He looks back once more—  Jeff is still clutching the bass like it’s the only thing holding him to the ground.

---

## **INT. STAGE RIGHT – MOMENTS AFTER JEFF’S BREAKDOWN**

**Jeremy** storms toward **Cremeans**, who’s neck-deep in the cue list and trying to wrangle pyro, set times, and catering.

**CREMEANS**  (not looking up)  
What now?

**JEREMY**  
Jeff’s not okay. He’s got a **migraine seizure-level** situation.  He’s not being dramatic. He’s *scared shitless*.  We need to pull the LED spots for Act II. And we’re changing the encore.

**CREMEANS** (glancing up like someone just told him the sun is taking a day off)  
You want to **redo the entire lighting arrangement** for the second half of the show? And then you’re proposing to **skip the encore**?

**JEREMY**  
Nope.

(beat)
We’re still doing the encore. But it’s going to be **acoustic**. We’re going to **improvise** it.   No lights.  No amps.  We *walk back out* there stripped to the bone and we *burn the place down quietly.* And maybe, we’re going to **shove Jeff into a car** and get his ass to the ER.

**KATHY** (entering mid-sentence, arms crossed, eyes wide)  
Hold on. *Acoustic set?*  We’ve *never* done that. You want me to just…*wing it*?

(beat)
With *no distortion*, *no delay*, *no wall of sound to hide behind*?

(beat)
What the fuck are you talking about, Jeremy?

*She’s breathing fast now.  Excited.  Terrified.*

**JEREMY** (to Kathy, firm)  
I’m talking about *doing the right thing*. We cover for Jeff.  We buy him time.  We still give the audience something *really cool*, maybe more stripped down than we’ve ever given them. No showboating.  Just *us*.  And a couple guitars.  When he's good, he deals himself back in.

**KATHY** (takes a step back, blinking)  
Holy shit.  This is either going to *ruin us*…

(beat)
Or it’s going to be the most *sexy, dangerous, honest* thing we’ve ever done.

**CREMEANS** (still stunned, but registering the storm)  
You realize you’re throwing out *months* of planning.

**JIM** (grinning, stepping in)  
Good. Because this crowd? They don’t need a light show tonight. They need a *moment*.

**CREMEANS** (staring at them all)  
You people are *really lunatics*.

**BILL**  
Yeah.

(beat)
That’s why they buy the tickets.

---

## **INT. BACKSTAGE – STAGE LEFT – SECONDS FROM SHOWTIME**

**The plan is forming fast.**  Acoustic set. Jeff out of the spotlight. Jeremy buying time.  And then—

**GILLEY** (storming in, voice breaking into full bellow)  
**No.** No. No. *Absolutely fucking not.* We are **not** sending Jeff back out there.

*EVERYONE freezes.*

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
This is ***fucked in the head***. You want him to walk back on that stage?  *With that seizure knocking on the door?*  No. ***FUCKING NO.***There’s **no goddamn way in hell** he’s going back out. I *refuse* to go out if he goes out.  I will ***fucking quit*** if you go out.  *That’s it. ***The end.***

*They all just stare at him.* Because they’ve *never* seen **Jeremy Gilley** like this.  Not angry. Not lashing out.  But *shaking*, *furious*, and *dead serious.*

**GILLEY** (quiet, ragged)
Jeff is my *brother*.

**CREMEANS**, stunned, takes a step back.

**CREMEANS** (soft, like he’s watching someone turn into a different person)  
Jesus Christ.

(beat)
Okay. Jeremy. How fast can we do an *acoustic* set? What do we *have* that works acoustic? I can throw the interlude track on a loop.  It’ll buy you *ten minutes*. Maybe *twelve*.

**Cremeans** steps over to **Jeff**, who is now sitting on the edge of a crate, head in his hands, visibly trembling.

**CREMEANS** (softly)  
Jeff. Jeff, can you hear me?

(beat)
We’re going to fix this.

*Jeff barely lifts his eyes. It’s not working. Cremeans turns back.*

**CREMEANS (louder, decisive)**  
I’m calling an *audible*. Let’s get an ambulance. *Now.*

**BILL**  
Okay, so instead of doing an hour of unplugged chaos—  Jeff’s got a *great* guitar tech.   **Emilio.**  We get Emilio to cover bass. He knows the whole damn set front to back.

**GILLEY** (snaps, fangs out)  
***Over my dead fucking body, fuckhead.***

**BILL** (not backing down)  
We *need* someone to cover. The show has to go on.

**GILLEY**  
No it *doesn’t.*  Not like *that*. We go out as *us* or we ***don’t go out***.

*Silence. The weight is unbearable.*

**KATHY** (quietly, to Gilley)  
So what *do* we do?

**GILLEY**  (steady now, eyes burning)  
We go out. ***Acoustic.  Raw.  Feral.*** No tricks.  No stand-ins.  No substitutes. Just us.

(beat)
We play like we’re *all Jeff tonight.*

*The band nods, one by one.*  *Cremeans exhales like he’s letting go of ten years of stress.* The loop music starts over the PA, crowd getting restless.*They’ve got **ten minutes**.

---

## **INT. SIDE STAGE – M&T BANK STADIUM – CROWD RUMBLING**

The *interlude music* is looping again. It’s been **twelve minutes**. The crowd is **restless**, the atmosphere turning *frantic*. Backstage, **Kathy, Jim, Gilley, Jeremy, Bill, and Cremeans** are huddled in a tight circle.

**CREMEANS** (low, serious)  
Alright, so what the heck can we tell the fans? Because if we just walk out acoustic and stripped down *without a word*,  they’re going to think Jeff *died* in the back.

**JIM** (arms crossed, eyes sharp)  
What’s the *argument*, then? We can’t say “medical emergency” and bounce into *Mountain Gospel '98* like it’s nothing. We need a *frame*. Something that makes them lean in, not freak out.

**KATHY** (thinking fast)  
We tell them it’s an *experiment*.  A one-night-only, **Baltimore exclusive**.  A stripped-back, alternate-universe Commuted. No lights.  No frills.  Just us.

**BILL**  
It’s not a lie.

**JEREMY**  
It’s just not the whole truth.

**GILLEY** (eyes cold, voice low)  
You want a frame? Here’s one. “Tonight, we’re changing the plan.  No tracks. No tricks.  This is what it sounds like when a band *takes off the armor*.”

(beat)
Let the fans *feel it*.  They’ll know something’s wrong.  But we *don’t lie*.  We just show them what *pain* sounds like when it sings.

**CREMEANS**  (staring at Gilley like he’s grown new teeth)  
…That’s actually not bad.

**JIM**  
That’s terrifying.  And kinda beautiful.

**KATHY**  
Yeah. Let’s tell them the truth—but wrapped in sound.

**GILLEY**  
I’ll say it.  Right before the first song. Let me handle the *words*. Y’all just handle the *hurt*.

*Silence. Then nods all around.*

They *can’t save Jeff right now*.  But they can give the crowd something *real*.  And in doing that, maybe they save *something else*.

---

## **INT. SIDE STAGE – M&T BANK STADIUM – FINAL MOMENTS BEFORE WALK-ON**

The *loop track is dying*.  The crowd’s energy is teetering between *eager* and *angry*.  They need *something*.  And Gilley—eyes blazing, pacing like a televangelist in a blackout—is *ready to give it to them*.

**GILLEY** (almost laughing, teeth bared)  
Alright. You remember the *fucking content* we shoved down people’s throats in Japan for the **anime side project**? That *weird-ass* setlist they didn’t know how to process? We’re doing *that*. Acoustic. *Raw as hell.*  It’s what they won’t expect.  It’s what they *won’t survive*.

He rattles off titles like bullets—no hesitation, no breath.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
First song—**Amateur Night.**  
Second—**I’d Win.**  
Third—**Craftsmanship.**  
Fourth—**Go Tip Her.**  
Fifth—**You Were Taking Too Long.**  
Sixth—**Come Here.**  
Seventh—**Something, Babe.**  
Eighth—**Good Girl.**  
Ninth—**Last Chance to Run.**  
Tenth—**The Ride of Your Life.**  
Eleventh—**Correct Answer.**  
Twelfth—**Bullets.**

And then we *drop* with an **acoustic version of “Come Inside Me.”** I will handle it *my fucking self.* Four chords. No gimmicks.  Just me.  And Kathy? You’re gonna *coo*.  Like it’s a lullaby. Like we didn’t build our empire out of **rage and orgasms and synth fire**. It’s gonna be the most fucking *ironic thing* you’ve ever put on stage.

**JEREMY** (pacing, stunned)  
That’s… actually not bad.  That’s kind of *experimental*.

(beat)
Fuck it. Let’s do it.

**BILL** (staring, half-in disbelief)  
You want to strip **“Come Inside Me”** down to *four chords*…and Kathy’s *voice*?

**GILLEY** (grinning, wicked)  
*Watch me.* Do try to keep up. I’ll put my balls on the chopping block. You guys?  *Just follow along.*

He turns to **Jim**, dead center.

**GILLEY** (soft, calm now)
I got this, Jim.

(beat)
I got this.

**JIM** (quiet, holding his sticks like he’s ready to march to his own funeral)  
Okay.

**GILLEY** (raising his fist)
On four. One. Two. Three. Four—

**ALL (roaring, more out of muscle memory than belief):**  
**COMMITTED!!**

*But none of them feels very committed.*  They feel **scared**.  **Unarmed.**  **Unready.** And maybe that’s exactly what this show needs.

---

## **EXT. M&T BANK STADIUM – CENTER STAGE – NIGHT**

A *single spotlight* drops from above, cutting through the black.  **GILLEY** steps into it like it was *built for him*.  No guitar. No mic stand. Just a **handheld mic**, black jeans, and the calm grin of a man about to make **half the stadium ovulate and the other half question their place in the universe**. He holds the mic like a cigarette and waits just long enough for the roar to peak and drop into a *tense, feral silence*.

**GILLEY** (low, smooth)  
City of …Baltimore.  Whatever name you want to wear tonight—*I'm talking to you.*  All of you.  Every eye. Every hand.  Every goddamn person in this place who thought they were coming to a concert—*You were wrong.*

(beat)
This is not a show.  This is a **problem**.  Because I came out here to *seduce* you.  **All** of you.  At the *same time*.

(The crowd ripples—confused, aroused, and already buying in.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
Now I want to talk about a little **trip** I made to **New Orleans**.  It was **Mardi Gras**.  There were **beads**, there was **brass**, there were **decisions** that still haunt at least three bartenders and a tattoo artist named Maurice.

(he pauses, sly)
And no, Maurice was not the one who *cried* afterward.  *I* was.

The audience LAUGHS, shocked, riveted.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
Ladies—  If you feel the urge to *flash me* during the second set, I’m going to need you to **control yourselves.**

(beat)
Or at least coordinate with each other. I’m trying to tell a **story**.

The spotlight tightens. He takes a single step closer to the edge of the stage. His voice drops.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
Because what I walked into down there…What I *barely escaped*?  Was a **hen party from hell.** *Thirteen women. One rented balcony. A bucket of absinthe and a list of dares that read like a war crime tribunal transcript.*

The crowd is now *fully locked in*.  No music. No band. Just **Gilley**—ripping the rulebook to shreds with nothing but his voice.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
Tonight?  You’re that party.  And I’m the poor bastard they hired to dance on the bar.  So let’s burn the playlist.  Forget the lights.  We’re gonna make this place *sweat*.  Together.

---

## **INT. BACKSTAGE – M&T BANK STADIUM – POST-SHOW MADHOUSE**

The band stumbles in from stage left. **Kathy’s makeup is half-melted**, **Jeremy’s hair is plastered to his face**, **Bill looks like he just channeled a comet**, and **Jim’s shirt is more sweat than fabric**.

Gilley **struts** in dead last—shirt open, chest gleaming like a religious statue from a cursed museum—and **first words out of his mouth**:

**GILLEY**  
Where’s the food? I thought we had a **caterer**.

*He looks around like someone’s supposed to present a roast duck and a gold-plated protein shake.*

**KATHY** (sitting on an amp case, unbothered)  
Well, *geez*, thank **God** he’s thinking with his **stomach** and not his **dick** for once.

**BILL** (still catching his breath, eyes closed, serene)  
Honestly? I appreciate the candor.  Because she’s right.  He *is* thinking with his stomach.  And *not* his dick. And that’s *growth*.

**JEREMY** (walking in wide-eyed, overwhelmed)  
We need to focus on what went **right** tonight. Because that… That was *transcendent*.  That was *beyond.*

Oh my *God*.

**GILLEY** (grinning, pointing both fingers at nothing)  
Uh-huh.  **What’d I tell you?** Trust the Gilley.  Always bet on purple.

**CREMEANS** (entering from stage left, still gripping the clipboard like a trauma doll)  
You know…If you’d *apply yourself*, Gilley— If you’d *really* apply yourself…

**GILLEY** (interrupts, hands in the air)  
If I applied myself—I’d be **carved on Mount Rushmore**. But I’m just in it for the *dames*, baby.

**JIM** (laughing, peeling off his damp bandana)  
Somebody *embroider that shit* on a throw pillow.

*They collapse onto chairs, gear trunks, each other. Laughter rising through the exhaustion, through the ache, through the afterburn of something miraculous.*

**KATHY** (muttering with a grin)  
Mount Gilley.  God help us all.

---

## **INT. BACKSTAGE GREEN ROOM – M&T BANK STADIUM – LATE NIGHT**

The energy has come down *hard*.  A few crew members are packing up. The last of the stadium echo is fading behind steel doors.  The band is sitting in silence—**ice packs, towels, Gatorade**, the scent of dried sweat and reality hanging in the air.

**JEREMY** (quiet, steady)  
Cremeans…What’s the update on Jeff?

**CREMEANS** (sits forward, finally lowering the clipboard)
They’ve sedated him.

(beat)
He’s got some kind of *massive neurological migraine episode*—not just pain, but *light sensitivity, auditory chaos, orientation stuff*.  He couldn’t sleep through it, so they put him under.  They’ll run tests in the morning.  MRI. Bloodwork. The works.

*Silence. A beat too long. Then—*

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**  
And honestly?  I’m thinking about *canceling Charlotte.*

Everyone looks up. Kathy stops mid-sip. Bill raises an eyebrow.

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**  
We’re gonna move the *set*.  All the gear.  All the roadies. All the lights, the merch bins, the cases, the racks—We’ll *drive it to Charlotte*.  But we’re not setting up at the stadium. Not yet.  We’ll park it.  We’ll *wait*.  And if Jeff’s okay tomorrow?  We do it.  But if he’s *not*—I think we cut our losses.  We cancel.  Call it clean.  No disaster. No embarrassment.  No press leaks. Just… end it here, with dignity.

*He looks up at them, for once not managing them, but asking them.*

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**  
What do you think, guys?

*Beat.*

**KATHY** (quietly)  
If he’s not okay, there’s no show.  Not for me.

**JIM** (shaking his head)  
Same. Jeff’s *core*.  He’s not a part of this. He *is* this.

**BILL** (soft)  
We played the weirdest, rawest set of our career tonight.  We don’t need to top it.  We just need him alive.

**JEREMY** (staring down, fists tight)  
He didn’t say “I’m scared.”  He said “I’m gonna *die*.”

(beat)
We don’t go on without him. *Not in Charlotte. Not anywhere.*

**CREMEANS** (sighs, nodding)
Okay.  We hold.  We drive.  We wait.  Tomorrow—If the light’s green, we hit it.  If not… we end it here.

The room breathes.  It’s not closure.  But it’s *honest*.

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – LEAVING BALTIMORE – HIGHWAY AT NIGHT**

The bus hums through darkness. The city lights fall away behind them. Everyone’s in post-show, post-hospital silence… until:

**GILLEY**  (suddenly, from the couch, voice too loud in the quiet)  
I could *do* that again. But do you have **any idea**—I was **clenching my asshole** for *58 minutes straight.* *Fifty-eight!*  Not even a second to breathe.

**KATHY**  (sipping water, without looking up)  
You were glowing like a cult leader.

**GILLEY**  
I have **never**—and I mean *never*—been more terrified about a creative choice in my **entire fucking life**.

*Pause.*
But…How about a **fucking live album**, Mr. Cremeans?

(leans into the air like he’s pitching to a record exec)
This thing?  This *Baltimore Unplugged from Hell*? This’ll *top out*. I don’t know…This’ll beat **Live at Pompeii.**  It’ll **blow away Nirvana Unplugged**.

**CREMEANS** (from his bench, eyes half-shut)  
You were crying during “Correct Answer.”

**GILLEY**  
That was *emotion*. That was *range*. That was **marketing gold**.

(he spins to Jeremy)
How about it?  You think this could hang with the *big dogs*? **The Who Live at Leeds**? You think we’re *there*?

**JEREMY**  (slow blink)  
Um…I’m gonna let **Jim** answer that one. Because, uh…Yeah. *It was.*

**JIM**  (from his bunk, without hesitation)  
Yep. We did something **genuine** tonight. That’s not a bootleg. That’s a *legacy*.

*The bus rides on. The lights are dim. No one’s talking now.* Because for once? They don’t need to. They’re already *etched* into something.

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – SOMEWHERE ON I-95 SOUTH – 3:42 A.M.**

The inside of the bus is quiet.  Too quiet. Everyone else is either asleep or faking it. **Jeremy** sits alone in the little bench at the kitchenette, knees pulled up, a cup of coffee going cold in front of him. The hum of the tires on the interstate is the only rhythm left.  Outside the window, **Maryland becomes Virginia**, becomes **night**, becomes *nothing*.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**  
For the better part of the last **27 years**,  I’ve lived my life less than **300 feet** away from my brother. Sometimes the same bunk.  Same bus.  Same venue.  Same headaches. 
Even when we weren’t speaking, we were still *orbiting each other*. And now? He’s in a hospital room in **Baltimore**.

He rubs his eyes with the heel of his hand. Tries to breathe. Fails.

**JEREMY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**  
I’m heading south. He’s… not. I know he’s sedated.  I know the docs are watching him.   But I can’t *feel* him. And that’s what’s breaking me.

He presses his forehead against the cool window.  Feels the pull of the dark road beneath him.

**JEREMY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**  
I’ll wake up in **Charlotte**, I guess. The bus will stop.  Cremeans will yell.  Kathy’ll make some joke.  Bill will play something weird over the intercom. And Jeff won’t be there.

He closes his eyes.  Takes a breath. Doesn’t let it out for a long time.

**JEREMY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**  
I wonder…Am I gonna fall asleep? Or am I gonna just…*arrive*?

*FADE TO BLACK.*  Just the sound of highway.  The hum of memory.  The ache of not knowing.

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – STILL MOVING – PRE-DAWN DARKNESS**

The bus is half-asleep. Charlotte’s creeping up somewhere on the horizon, but no one’s looking at maps anymore.**Jeremy** sits with his arms crossed, hood up, headphones in—but not listening. **Jim** walks up with two cups of coffee—sets one down in front of him, sits across without asking.

**JIM** (soft, shrugging)  
You know…It’s a migraine. Not like Jeff isn’t *weird* all the time.

**JEREMY** (slowly looks up, deadpan)  
Are you trying to make me feel better? Or are you trying to make me want to *rip out your vocal cords* and *strangle you with them*?

**JIM** (sips his coffee)  
Little from column A, little from column B.

(beat)
Yeah. Okay. I hope he’s better. *I do.*

**JIM (CONT’D)**  
That show tonight? That was fucking **awesome**.  It was *spectacular*. We pulled off something I never thought we could— something *only we* could have done.  But…

(he looks down, fingers flexing around the coffee cup)
In our greatest moment of triumph? It rings a little *hollow*. Because we were way too stripped down. *Because we didn’t have your brother on bass.*

*Jeremy says nothing for a moment.*  *Then he exhales hard—like a punch he’s been holding in his chest.*

**JEREMY**  
He’s the pulse. You know? Even when he’s off, even when he’s buried in his own head…He’s the fucking *center.*

**JIM** (nods, quiet now)  
Yeah. We missed him.

**JEREMY**  
And I think maybe he missed us too. I just don’t know how far *gone* he was when he realized it.

*The silence sits between them. Heavy. Honest.*  *Jim reaches for a lighter joke—then lets it go. Just sips his coffee and stays with his bandmate.*

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – STILL MOVING SOUTH – LATE NIGHT TURNING INTO EARLY MORNING**

The bus interior is dim, quiet, humming. A highway rest stop rolls past outside the window, but no one’s paying attention. **Jeremy** hasn’t moved. Still in that corner bench, coffee cold, hoodie up.  **Jim** still across from him, holding the silence like a brother, not a bandmate. But Jeremy finally looks up.

**JEREMY**  
You were sitting in the back during the first set.

(beat)
What was your *impression* of Jeff? 

*Long pause. Jim doesn’t dodge it.*

**JIM**  
I’m gonna be frank? He **sucked**.

(beat)
He was *late*.  He was *inattentive*.  He was missing **half the chords**.  He looked like he was *sleepwalking* with an instrument strapped to his chest.

**JEREMY** (flat, staring at the floor)  
Do you think he was *stoned*? Or on *mushrooms*?

**JIM** (shaking his head slowly)  
Probably not.

(beat)
At least… I **hope** not.

*Jeremy takes that in. Doesn’t flinch. Doesn’t argue. Just files it.*

**JIM (CONT’D)**  
I think he was in *pain*. Not *emotional*, not some existential meltdown. I mean **neurological, system-failure** kind of pain. He was playing like his *brain* was working against him.

**JEREMY** (quiet)  
Yeah.

(beat)
That’s what scared me the most.

**JIM**  
He’s not sloppy.  He’s *never* been sloppy. Even when he was *spinning out emotionally*, he could play through it. This? This wasn’t *that*.

**JEREMY** (nods slowly)  
So we wait.

**JIM**  
Yeah.  We wait.

*They sit together in the dark, brothers in orbit around a third who isn’t there.* The engine hums. The road rolls. The night holds its breath.

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – PRE-DAWN, SOMEWHERE NEAR CHARLOTTE**

The cabin light is dim.  The highway feels *longer* than usual.  Everyone else is asleep or pretending. But **Jim and Jeremy**—still sitting, still holding vigil—have reached the part of the night where the optimism finally *cracks*.

**JIM** (running his hands through his chest hair)  
Christ. 

(beat)
We’re *fucked*.

**JEREMY** (shifts, slow)  
Don’t say that yet.

**JIM**  
If he can’t go…

(beat, voice tightening)
If he *can’t go*, we’re **fucked**. *Because we can’t be us without a throbbing bass line.*  Without that *anchor* in the center of everything. It—it’s not gonna work.

**JEREMY** (quiet, thinking fast)  
Don’t be entirely sure. If push came to shove, we could throw…I don’t know…Yeah, we could throw **Bill** at it.

*Jim just **stares** at him. Flat.*

**JIM**  
Get *realistic*.

(beat)
That would wreck our entire—*our entire sound.*The floor would be gone. The tension, the swing, the *fuck-you growl* in the low end—**Poof.**We’d *suck*.  Yeah.

**JEREMY** (slumping back)  
Yeah.

**JIM**  
We’re a chair with three legs.  Jeff’s the fourth. You try to sit on that thing without him?  It *collapses.*

*Silence. Just the hum of tires.* There’s no backup plan. Just hope. And **one empty bunk.**

---


## **INT. TOUR BUS – EARLY MORNING LIGHT BLEEDING THROUGH CURTAINS**

They’re still riding south.  **Charlotte’s coming**, but there’s no certainty left.  Just conversations like this—*truth, stripped raw*. Jim exhales, still slumped on the bench. Jeremy leans forward, both elbows on the table, talking slowly—like he’s worked this out a hundred times in his head but never said it out loud.

**JEREMY**  
There’s not a *single sound* we can realistically subtract. *Not one.*

**JIM** (nods, dead tired)  
Go on.

**JEREMY**  
You want to drill it down? We’re not famous because we’re tight.  We’re not famous because we’re smart.  We’re famous because we make *ridiculous sounds*—and we sound *ridiculous about sex*.

**JIM** (grinning)  
You’re not wrong.

**JEREMY** (leaning in, eyes sharper now)  
We’ve got **two people** at the front of house—*Gilley* and *Kathy*. And they are, hands down, the **world’s biggest salesmen for sex**. They get out there and they make people *want* things they can’t even say out loud. And the rest of us? We’re the *machine behind the sin.* We’re the engine of that *seduction.*  The rhythm section is the *foreplay*.  The synths are the *film grain*.  And Jeff’s bass?

(beat)
It’s the *thrust*.

**JIM**  (sits back, laughing softly, sad and honest)  
God. That’s so gross. And so *true*.

**JEREMY**  
We subtract *any one* of those elements? The *chemistry’s gone*. The spell breaks. And we’re just five weirdos in boots yelling about orgasms with bad timing.

**JIM** (smiling now, but tired)  
What a fucking band.

**JEREMY**  
What a fucking band.

*The wheels hum. The sky lightens.* They don’t have an answer yet.  But they know the question matters.

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – EARLY MORNING – STILL EN ROUTE TO CHARLOTTE**

The light is starting to change—faint blue leaking in through the tinted windows.  Outside: trees, highway signs, *early sunlight*.  Inside: a haze of sleep and half-empty Gatorade bottles. **Jeremy** stretches once, a full-body shake like a dog after a storm. He slumps back into his bunk, hoodie still up, eyes ringed with exhaustion.

**JEREMY** (voice low, almost cracked)  
Thanks for talking.

(beat)
I’m gonna pass out.

*He tucks himself in, head buried in the pillow.*

**JEREMY (CONT’D)**  
If somebody’s got news about Jeff…

(beat)
Wake me up. But *not before eight o’clock*.

(eyes already closing)
It can wait… till *eight o’clock*.

**JIM**  (quietly, from across the aisle)  
Got it. Sleep.

*The bus rolls on.*  *The engine hums.*  *The sky brightens.* And for the first time in what feels like **a lifetime**,  **Jeremy Evans sleeps.**

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL – RADIOLOGY – 6:15 A.M.**

Fluorescent lights. Chill in the air.  That medical-clean scent that always smells like it’s hiding something.  **Jeff** lies perfectly still in the **MRI tube**, arms by his sides, headphones on—but no music.  Just the cold voice of the tech: *“This scan will take approximately 20 minutes. Try to stay very still.”*  And then—**the machine starts**.

---

**KATUNK-KATUNK-KATUNK.**  
**WHUM. WHUM. WHUM.**  
**DAKADAKADAKADAKA.**

---

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
Goddamn.  That’s a *beat*.

(beat)
That’s *deep*.  Visceral.  Repetitive in a *machine-made* kind of way.  Like a rhythm that doesn’t care if you’re listening or not—it’s *coming anyway*.  If it were just **louder**—

(he smiles, the faintest ghost of one)
It’d be **danceable**.

*He closes his eyes, lets the sequence wash over him, start to loop in his head like a pattern waiting to be fleshed out.*

**JEFF (V.O.) (CONT’D)**  
That could be a drop.  That could be the *backbone* of something—No bassline.  Just that rhythm.  Somewhere in between **industrial gospel** and a panic attack.

Another pulse. Another sequence.

**CLUNK-CLUNK. TIKTIKTIKTIK. TROMP.**

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
We sample this, slow it down 6%, layer some low synths and whispered vocals?  Could be quite *sinister*.  Could be *sacred*.

*He breathes. Pain’s still there, but dulled.*  *His head still hurts—but for the first time in hours, his mind is working again.*  ***Creating**, not surviving.*

**JEFF (V.O.) (CONT’D)**  
I gotta get out of this tube.  Not because it’s tight.  But because I got a song to write.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL – RADIOLOGY RECOVERY ROOM – 7:00 A.M.**

Jeff’s on a gurney, sitting upright now, IV still in. His face is pale, but his eyes are **sharp again**—not in pain, but *focused*.  A nurse checks his vitals, clipboard in hand.

**JEFF**  
Hey—Quick question.  Can I get **audio** of the MRI?  Doesn’t have to be mine. I just want to record it. *Someday*.  

The nurse freezes mid-blood pressure cuff, clearly thrown.

**NURSE**  
Um…Mr. Evans…That’s not exactly—I mean, we don’t… **record** MRIs for audio content.  And more importantly…

(awkward smile)
Having **metal objects** near the machine?  That’s, uh, **counterproductive.**

**JEFF**  
Yeah, yeah, no, I get it.  But, like—What happens if you *do* put a metal object in there?  Like a real old-school **tape recorder**?

(leans in, totally serious)
Does it *spark*?  Does it **explode**?  How expensive would it be to *find out*?

The nurse’s face goes from polite confusion to mild horror.

**NURSE**  
That… would be a **catastrophic violation** of federal safety protocols.

(beat)
And probably a **six-figure** cleanup.

**JEFF**  
Okay, okay, just spitballing.

(beat)
Do you guys have, like… *demo scans*?  Like a **great-sounding MRI** file?  Something with **real percussive rhythm**?

**NURSE** (still stunned)  
Are you asking me if we keep an *audio sample library* of our MRI machine…?

**JEFF**  
You’d be surprised how often this *exact* thought comes up in post-rock production.

(beat)
Also, I’m not on any painkillers right now.

**NURSE**  
That’s… reassuring?

*Jeff leans back on the bed, satisfied with the exchange, already composing something in his head using **thunk**s and **pulse tones** and **magnetron whirs**.*

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
They gave me medicine to sleep.  But what I really needed was *new percussion*.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL – DOCTOR’S OFFICE – 7:45 A.M.**

Fluorescent lights.  Monitor glow.  Lab printouts in a clear sleeve.  **Jeff’s attending physician**, mid-40s, bone-tired but sharp, reviews the latest results from his folder—speaking half-aloud to himself and the *disbelief hanging in the air*.

**DOCTOR**  
Okay. Urinalysis, blood work…

(squints, flipping pages)
Well, **fuck**.  There’s no sign of—

(half-muttering)
