No mushrooms.  No weed.  No cocaine.  No heroin.  No LSD.  No ketamine.  No benzos.  Not even a **bad decision** in here.

He leans back in his chair, eyes closed for a beat.

**DOCTOR (CONT’D)**  
Mildly **dehydrated**.

(beat)
**Dumbass.**

He stands, stretches like a man about to yell into a closet.

**DOCTOR (CONT’D)**  
Do you know how many issues can be *solved*—*properly*—with **hydration**?  Like, a bottle of water and a moment of adult responsibility?  People walking around with world-ending symptoms when what they really need is a **Gatorade and a nap**.

He tosses the report on the desk, paces once.  Looks toward the terminal where the **MRI is still uploading** into the radiology system.

**DOCTOR (CONT’D)**  
So what the **fuck** does the MRI show?  Because if he’s clean…If he’s *sober*…Then we’re either looking at **neurological misfire**, **stress event**, or some kind of rare-ass *vascular fluke* that’s about to rewrite his setlist *and his life*.

He checks the clock.

**DOCTOR (CONT’D)**  
It’ll be a little bit.  These scans don’t interpret themselves.  But when they do…*I want to be the first one to know if this guy’s brain just tried to write a post-industrial concept album out of its own pain.*

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL – RECOVERY ROOM – 8:02 A.M.**

Jeff’s sitting up in bed, propped on pillows. The IV drip is still going, but his color’s better. His hair’s a mess. There’s a beeping monitor somewhere behind him, but he doesn’t care.  **Nurse Alana**, mid-30s, whip-smart and professionally unfazed, is checking his vitals. Clipboard in one hand, cool gaze in the other.  Jeff watches her with the **lazy confidence** of a man who’s *trying it* even though he knows he probably shouldn’t.

**JEFF** (low, raspy)  
So, uh…Tell me something, Nurse Alana.  You ever think about waveform resonance?

She raises an eyebrow without looking up.

**NURSE ALANA**  
Can’t say that I do.

**JEFF**  
That’s a shame.  Because you are radiating a **very specific frequency** right now…And it is… *unmistakably disruptive*.

**NURSE ALANA** (flat, flipping to the next chart)  
Disruptive like how?

**JEFF**  
Disruptive like **feedback on vinyl**.  Like static you want to *lean into*.

**NURSE ALANA**  
Your blood pressure’s dropping back to normal.  That’s cute.

**JEFF**  
Oh, I haven’t even **started** being cute yet.

She finishes her vitals and steps back, tapping her pen once.

**NURSE ALANA**  
You know you’re in a gown that’s half-open in the back, right?

**JEFF** (leans in just slightly)  
Well, then we’re already halfway to sex.

She doesn’t even blink.

**NURSE ALANA**  
If you so much as try to explain the **sub-bass frequencies of flirting**, I’m replacing your IV with **pickle juice**.

**JEFF** (smiles wide)  
Can I at least get your number?

**NURSE ALANA**  
Yeah.

It’s **9-1-1**.

*She turns, walks out of the room with a slight smirk. Jeff leans back, wincing, still a little wrecked, but suddenly a lot more alive.*

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
God, I missed *being me.*

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL – NURSES’ STATION – 8:07 A.M.**

The fluorescent lights are warming up. Coffee cups steam. Clipboards shuffle. It’s shift change, and **Nurse Alana**, still putting the finishing touches on her rounds, leans over to brief her replacement.  **Changeover Nurse**, early 40s, unflappable, glances over the chart.

**ALANA** (points toward Jeff’s room)  
Room 218?  That’s **Jeff Evans**.  He’s alert.  Vitals are good.  Headache’s easing off.  *Dangerously upright.*

**CHANGEOVER NURSE**  
Musician?

**ALANA**  
Oh, **dear lord**, he is **such** a musician.

**CHANGEOVER NURSE**  
*That kind*, huh?

**ALANA**  
That kind.  Full-on “lemme talk to you about waveform theory while trying to make eye contact with your cervix” kind.

**CHANGEOVER NURSE** (casually clicks pen)  
So, basically doomed?

**ALANA** (grinning, walking away)  
Try to keep your **panties on**.  But yeah.  **You’re doomed.**  **We’re all doomed.**

*The changeover nurse sighs, smiles, and opens Jeff’s chart with the weary resolve of a woman about to walk into the jazz club of her professional life.*

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL – ADMIN OFFICE WINDOW – 9:12 A.M.**

Jeff’s been wheeled down to **registration**, still in a robe that’s holding together mostly out of luck and hospital-grade polyester.  At the desk, **Tasha**, early 30s, all business in glasses and sharp black scrubs, is ready to **check his chart, scan his card, and move the hell on**.  She’s not here for the drama.  Jeff, though?  He sees an opportunity.

**TASHA**  
Legal name?

**JEFF**  
Jeffrey W Evans.  Though I also respond to *“Hey bass player,”* *“You ruined me,”* and *“Please don’t stop.”*

**TASHA** (deadpan)  
Date of birth?

**JEFF**  
July 23.  The day "Sweet Child O' Mine" entered the Top 40.  The day everything changed.  The day *trouble* was made legal.

**TASHA** (raising an eyebrow, not impressed)  
Insurance card?

Jeff pulls it from a plastic hospital bag and slides it across the counter like it’s a love letter. He leans in, elbow propped up, smile slowly curling.

**JEFF**  
I’ve never tried to **seduce someone** while handing over my **insurance information**.

(beat)

I consider this a *milestone* in my personal evolution.

**TASHA** (checks the card without missing a beat)  
Your copay is $50.  Your flirting is *declined.*

**JEFF** (struck, laughs)  
That was *good.*

**TASHA**  
I get *rock stars* in here every once in a while.  You're all the same.  Except you're the first one trying to mack it up with a **hospital wristband** and bedhead that looks like a hawk crash-landed on you.

**JEFF**  
That’s branding.

**TASHA**  
This is **admission paperwork**.  Sign here.

*Jeff signs, grinning, not winning—but loving the game anyway.*

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
I’ve played stadiums.  I’ve stared down critics, press, exes, a goddamn fire marshal.  But this woman?  She could ruin me with a clipboard.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 9:25 A.M.**

Jeff’s been wheeled back to his room.  He’s feeling *better*, if not exactly **alive**—still buzzing from the flirtation, still hungry for something *outside the realm of “clear liquids.”*  There’s a knock at the door. **A hospital tech** rolls in a tray with the resigned energy of someone who’s seen too many broken men try to reengage with **medically sanctioned sausage links**.

**TECH**  
Breakfast, Mr. Evans.

*The tray lands with a gentle clunk. A beige dome covers something vaguely warm.*

**JEFF** (squints)  
Is that for me?  Or is that what we give prisoners before sentencing?

**TECH**  
Scrambled eggs, oatmeal, two slices of toast, and…

(he lifts the dome)  
A thing we legally describe as **fruit**.

**JEFF** (staring at the tray like it insulted his family)  
What else do I get to eat?  Like, is there a *menu*?  A black-market omelet situation?  Can I *bribe someone* for bacon?

**TECH**  
If you have a good nurse, you might be able to con some peanut butter out of her.

**JEFF**  
Peanut butter…My kingdom for a spoonful of Peter Pan peanut butter.

He stares at the **eggs**, pokes them with the plastic fork.  They jiggle in defiance.

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
I’ve survived green rooms in Albania.  I’ve eaten gas station sushi in Toledo.  But this?  This means *war*.

*He picks up the toast. It snaps.*  *He puts it down.*

**JEFF**  
Do I get to *flirt my way into pancakes*?  Or is this just my punishment for being interesting?

**TECH**  
We also have applesauce.

**JEFF**  
Do I look like a man who deserves *applesauce*?

*The tech shrugs and leaves. Jeff sighs, takes a bite of the oatmeal, and winces like it insulted his ancestors.*

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
I faced death.  And now I face **hospital breakfast**.  Truly, no man survives everything.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 9:42 A.M.**

Jeff stares at the untouched tray of eggs like it’s plotting against him.  He pushes the tray an inch away with the same disdain he might reserve for a bad review from *Pitchfork*.  He’s back in bed, phone in hand, wallet on the tray.  **His voice rings out into the sterile silence:**

**JEFF**  
Alright.  The next person who walks in here—I’m giving them **five hundred bucks**.

(beat)
All they have to do is go **buy me a bag of Fritos**—and a **cold Mountain Dew**.

*He sits back like he’s just placed a hit on his own diet.*

**JEFF (CONT’D)**  
I *know* there’s a vending machine in this building.  I saw it.  Right next to the volunteer desk and that weird painting of a heron that looks like it wants to stab someone.

He pauses, eyes narrowing.

**JEFF (CONT’D)**  
Five hundred dollars.  *Cash.*  For **crunchy salt and corn**, and a **liquid nuclear sweetener**.

He looks to the door like he’s trying to manifest a nurse with the soul of a gas station.

**JEFF (CONT’D)**  
You think **Nurse Ratched** herself wouldn’t *blink* at five hundred?  Hell, she'd probably *sprint*.  She'd grab me a **full six-pack** and tell me to enjoy it *before the lobotomy*.

*Silence. Still no one at the door.*

**JEFF (CONT’D)**  
I swear, if someone comes in here and asks me how the toast was, I’m throwing a bedpan like it’s a championship discus event.

*He picks up the remote.*  *Not to change the channel.*  *Just to have something to hurl if he needs to.*

**JEFF (V.O.)**  
I’ll never take gas station snacks for granted again.  Hospital food humbles you.  And also gives you deep cravings for chemical corn chips.

---

## **INT. CHARLOTTE HOTEL – BAND SUITE – 9:52 A.M.**

Morning sun cuts through the slats. The room is a graveyard of kicked-off shoes, half-zipped gear bags, and open water bottles.  **Cremeans** is on the phone, pacing like a man trying to will good news into existence.  The rest of the band—**Kathy, Jim, Jeremy, Bill**—sits in a loose half-circle. Some holding coffee, some holding breath.  Cremeans hangs up.

**CREMEANS**  
Alright. Here’s what we know.  *Jeff is sober.*  Completely clean.  No substances.  No synthetics.  Not even fucking *NyQuil*.

**KATHY** (exhales)  
Thank **fuck** for that.

(pause)
There’s a first time for everything.

**JIM** (smirking despite himself)  
If this is what clean Jeff sounds like, maybe we’ve had it backwards all these years.

**BILL**  
He did once write two verses of “Bullets” on a mushroom trip in St. Paul.

**JEREMY** (quiet, serious)  
This wasn’t drugs.  It wasn’t *anything* like that.  That’s what scares me the most.

**CREMEANS**  
They’re still waiting on the full MRI interpretation.  But all his blood work, tox screen, hydration levels?  Other than being a little dried out—and, quote, “full of opinions”—he’s *medically boring.*

**KATHY** (chuckles softly)  
Boring is good.  Boring means he didn’t OD.  Boring means I don’t have to read some Billboard obituary that uses words like “mercurial” and “troubled.”

*Silence. That kind of heavy, grateful silence that feels like a reprieve.*

**CREMEANS**  
We’ll get the full update later.  But for now—he’s alive.

**JEREMY**  
Then let’s just… sit with that.

*They do. No jokes. No tension. Just relief.*

---

## **INT. CHARLOTTE HOTEL – BAND SUITE – 10:15 A.M.**

The morning’s cleared slightly.  Coffee’s being refilled.  Everyone’s been hit with the **news: Jeff is alive, clean, and waiting on MRI results**.  The room has that *edge of something serious coming*.  **Kathy** stands by the tiny kitchen counter like a high priestess in slippers.

**KATHY** (claps once)  
Okay.  Emergency **band meeting**.  Now.

**JIM** (groaning)  
Do we need to be dressed?

**KATHY**  
Not unless your balls are planning to vote.

**CREMEANS** (sits down with his clipboard, because of course he does)  
This should be good.

**KATHY**  
I’m calling the **roll**.  Because if we’re gonna talk about *Charlotte*, and *Jeff*, and whatever the fuck comes **next**, then we’re going to do it like we’re not a bunch of tequila-spilling toddlers with amps.  We’re going to act like a **band**.

She looks around.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**  
**Jim.**

**JIM**  
Present and emotionally underqualified.

**KATHY**  
**Bill.**

**BILL**  
Here. Synthesizing regret.

**KATHY**  
**Jeremy.**

**JEREMY**  (sits up straighter)  
Here. Ready to vote, scream, or cry, depending.

**KATHY**  
**Cremeans.**

**CREMEANS**  
Non-voting. But here to control the panic.

**KATHY**  
**Kathy.**

(pause, deadpan)
Present. Also fabulous.

She takes a deep breath. Crosses her arms.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**  
Now…Let’s talk about what the *fuck* we do with this *final show*.

---

## **INT. CHARLOTTE HOTEL – BAND SUITE – 10:17 A.M.**

The circle is formed.  Kathy’s got her arms crossed, jaw tight.  Everyone’s bracing.  But there’s one chair **very noticeably empty**.

**KATHY**  (staring at the seat like it owes her money)  
Where the **fuck** is **Gilley**?

(beat)
I swear to **fuck**—If he’s off **getting himself some pussy** while we’re trying to decide if our band *has a future*? I will **fucking throttle him.**

**JIM**  
He was at breakfast. I saw him…

(looks at Bill)
What time was that?

**BILL**  
Mmm… Nine?  He had three eggs and said something about “riding the lightning.” Could’ve been a metaphor or a motorcycle.

**JEREMY**  
I swear to God, if he’s giving some poor barista a spiritual experience while we’re out here debating legacy, I’m gonna break his harmonica in half.

**KATHY**  (takes a breath, eyes darting)  
Where is he, **guys**?

**CREMEANS**  
Well, I thought I saw him leave the hotel 30 minutes ago.

**KATHY**  
**Fucking classic.**

*She picks up her phone, texts furiously.*  *No reply.*  *She looks ready to **set something on fire**.*

**KATHY (CONT’D)**  
I am this close—

*holds fingers together like a guillotine gap*

—*this close* to calling a bounty hunter.

**JIM**  
Let’s not cancel the show *just yet*. He could be—

**JEREMY**  
Don’t say “on a vision quest.”  I’m not emotionally ready for a Gilley vision quest today.

**BILL**  
Odds he’s just getting a coffee?

**CREMEANS**  
Odds he’s getting a coffee *while getting blown*?

**KATHY** (snarling, pacing)  
He better be at a funeral. His own.

---

## **INT. CHARLOTTE HOTEL – BAND SUITE – 10:22 A.M.**

The room is *thick* with tension. Kathy’s pacing like a predator.  Cremeans is mid-rant. Bill’s half-meditating. Jeremy’s staring into his coffee like it’s got answers.  And then—The door opens.
**GILLEY saunters in**, barefoot, **wearing only a bathrobe**.  He smells like **perfume, sin, and coconut shampoo**.  His hair is sex-wrecked. His grin is *impossible*.

**GILLEY** (arms out like he’s hosting a game show)  
*What’s up, guys?*  What’s up? Did I miss anything?

*Everyone just stares.*

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
Bill—*good morning*.  You look like a monk who regrets nothing.  Kathy—

(tilts his head)
You don’t look good.  Kinda got that “smother someone with a pillow” vibe going on.  Jeremy— *How’s your brother?*

**KATHY** (stalking toward him, absolutely *done*)  
Gilley.  **What the fuck.**

**GILLEY** (relaxed, arms still open)  
What?  I had a *spiritual encounter*. There were *two* of them, actually.  Very enlightening.

**JEREMY** (slowly)  
We’re planning the possible *end* of this band—And you were out getting **laid in a bathrobe**?

**GILLEY**  
No.  I *left* in the bathrobe.  Let’s not twist the timeline.

**CREMEANS**  
Jesus Christ. I was this close to calling **local law enforcement**.

**KATHY**  
You’re lucky I didn’t call *my ex* who owns a backhoe and has no conscience.

**GILLEY** (holding both hands up, finally semi-serious)  
Alright. Alright. I get it.  I’m late.  I smell like *French vanilla bad decisions*.  But I’m here now.  *Let’s talk.*

*Everyone glares.*  *No one says it.*  *But deep down—they’re a little relieved.*  *Because as infuriating as he is, **Gilley’s presence means the band is still whole**.*  *For now.*

---

## **INT. CHARLOTTE HOTEL – BAND SUITE – 10:24 A.M.**

Gilley’s still half-smirking in his bathrobe.  Kathy’s vibrating with tension.  Jeremy’s wrung out.  Cremeans is ready to snap his clipboard in half.  **Bill**, sitting in a kitchen chair with legs crossed like he’s at a city council meeting, sets his coffee down with the precision of a man about to do something *official*.

**BILL**  
Alright.  Enough wandering.  I move that we **cancel the Charlotte show**.

*The room stills.*

**BILL (CONT’D)**  
Not postpone.  Not delay.  *Cancel*.  We’ve already done the impossible in Baltimore.  There’s no encore without Jeff.  There’s no plan worth more than *his health*.  And there’s no need to chase closure when we already burned the house down *acoustic*.

**KATHY** (quiet, controlled)  
Seconded.

**BILL**  
Then it’s on the floor.  Let’s vote.  **All in favor—yea.**

**KATHY**  
Yea.

**JEREMY**  
Yea.

**JIM** (quietly)  
Yea.

**CREMEANS** (non-voting, but nodding)  
It’s the right call.

**BILL**  
Nays?

*A long pause. No sound but the hum of hotel AC.*

**GILLEY** (sighs, robe tied tight)  
…Yea.

*Beat. That’s it.*

**BILL**  
Motion carries.  Charlotte is **off**.

*They all sit with it.*  *Not relief. Not regret.*  *Just… truth.*

**KATHY**  
We ended it in Baltimore.

**JEREMY**  
Where Jeff *wasn’t*.  But somehow… *still was*.

*Silence. The kind that means it’s over.*

---

## **INT. CHARLOTTE HOTEL – BAND SUITE – 10:26 A.M.**

The air is *flat*.  Still.  Decision made, future now *unwritten*.  **Cremeans** nods, already pulling out his phone, walking toward the window with that grim, do-the-job energy. He’s about to **end the tour officially**.

**GILLEY**  (muttering, low, tired)  
Go end it, boss man.  Take care of it.

He **slumps** into the chair. Robe loose. Chest rising and falling like a man *post-battle*. The adrenaline’s gone. The jokes are gone.  What’s left is the truth.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)** (soft, distant)  
We’re in the wrong fuckin’ town.

*Everyone freezes.*  He’s not wrong.  They didn’t come here to **close** anything.  Because the show *already closed itself*.  *Jeff’s collapse. The unplugged miracle. The stripped truth in purple light.*  It all happened **back there**.

**KATHY** (sits down slowly)  
Yeah.  We left the ending behind.

**JIM**  
And maybe that’s okay?

**JEREMY**  
We’ll go back.  Even if just to see him.  Even if just to say…

(beat)
*Thanks.*

They don’t need to say more.  For once, they all agree—**Charlotte’s just geography.**  The **story ended in Baltimore**.

---

## **INT. CHARLOTTE HOTEL – BAND SUITE – 10:29 A.M.**

Silence has settled like fog.  The meeting’s over.  The decision made.  Then—suddenly—**GILLEY SHRIEKS**.

**GILLEY** (shouting from the chair, then standing like a man possessed)  
**ROAD TRIP.**

(last burst of manic joy)
***Last one on the bus is a DUMB MOTHERFUCKER!!***

**He SPRINTS** out of the room—bathrobe flapping, hair wild, a blur of *bare legs and chaos*—headed full tilt toward the **parking lot**.

**KATHY** (blinking)  
…Is he—?

**JIM**  
He’s—

**BILL**  
Did he just—

**JEREMY** (staring after him, brow furrowed)  
Is he saying…He wants us to *go back*?  To **Baltimore**?

**CREMEANS** (still on the phone, already juggling cancellation logistics)  
Oh Jesus *Christ*.

They all slowly get to their feet, drifting toward the door like they’ve just heard a prophecy written in gas station graffiti.

**KATHY** (grabbing her sunglasses)  
If he’s doing a **reverse farewell tour**, I swear to God, I’m bringing a taser.

**JIM**  
He’s not wrong though.

**BILL**  
Baltimore’s where we left it all.

**JEREMY** (slow smile forming)  
Let’s bring it home.

---

## **INT. CHARLOTTE HOTEL – LOBBY – 10:35 A.M.**

**Cremeans** is on the phone, headset clipped in, pulling up contracts, refund clauses, and final expense reports. He’s in the middle of managing a **logistical landslide**.  **Jeremy**, calm but clearly on a mission, steps beside him.

**JEREMY**  
Hey.  Quick question.  Can you, uh… **wrap up the show?**  Like, *everything*?  Venue, staff, gear.  All of it.

**CREMEANS** (still half-listening)  
Yeah. That’s what I’m doing.  Why?

**JEREMY**  
Would you mind if we borrowed one of the **tour buses**?

**CREMEANS** (blinks, now paying attention)  
Borrow?

**JEREMY**  
Just… for a bit.  Just us.  To **Baltimore**.

**CREMEANS** (tilts his head)  
You wanna road trip?  *Back*?

**JEREMY**  
It’s not *that* far, right?  How far is it, boss man?

**CREMEANS**  (staring at him, then sighing)  
Roughly **430 miles**.  Six and a half hours.

**JEREMY**  
Easy.

**CREMEANS** (staring at him, then quietly)
You driving?

**JEREMY**  
We’ve got Gilley in a bathrobe sprinting through the parking lot like it’s the apocalypse.  We’ll *make it happen*.

**CREMEANS**  
You go.  I’ll handle this.

(beat)
But you better come back with a *goddamn epilogue* worth printing.

**JEREMY** (soft smile)  
We’re gonna write it in real time.

---

## **EXT. CHARLOTTE HOTEL – PARKING LOT – 10:38 A.M.**

**Gilley**, robe billowing like a deranged cult leader, is halfway across the asphalt, yelling something about *“driving into destiny.”*  **Jim** is double-fisting cold brews.  **Jeremy** is laughing for the first time in days.  **Bill** is jogging slowly like he’s in a European art film.  Meanwhile, **Kathy**, sunglasses on, calm as an assassin, turns in the opposite direction and mutters to no one:

**KATHY**  
There’s *no way* any of you dumb shits have a **commercial driver’s license**.

She pivots and heads back toward the **bus compound** where the actual **professional drivers** hang out between gigs—probably smoking, napping, or *considering quitting*.  She scans the parking area, spots one of the familiar drivers—**Tom**, mid-50s, denim vest, hairline that gave up before Y2K.

**KATHY**  (strolling up, casual but firm)  
Hey, Tom.  Quick favor.

**TOM** (turns, wary but interested)  
Please tell me this doesn’t involve Jeff eating Doritos out of your crotch or Gilley’s naked ass again.

**KATHY**  
Depends.  How do you feel about **seven hours back to Baltimore**?  Right now.

**TOM** (blinks)  
You're joking.

**KATHY**  
Not even a little.  We’re doing a **reverse victory lap**. Jeff's in a hospital bed, and this band’s got a **psychic debt to settle**.  We’ve got five musicians, zero licenses, and one shared brain cell that’s currently screaming.

**TOM**  
And what do I get?

**KATHY**  
The most meaningful road trip in American music history.  And, like, fifty bucks and whatever Gilley’s got in his jacket lining.

**TOM**  
Gimme ten to get coffee and a legal pad.  Then I’ll take you idiots to war.

**KATHY**  
Love you, legend.

*She turns and heads back toward the circus.*  *The bus will have a driver.*  *The band will have a second shot.*  And **Baltimore**?  Better fucking be ready.

---

## **EXT. CHARLOTTE HOTEL – TOUR BUS – 10:49 A.M.**

The band is gathered at the open bus door, adrenaline buzzing, half-packed gear tossed back inside like a cinematic prison break.  **Kathy** returns, triumphant, strutting like a general with news from the front.

**KATHY**  
Okay, dumbasses—listen up. We got **Tom**.  Yes, **that Tom**.  Chain-smoking, denim vest, still drives like it’s 1987.  He’s caffeinating and coming back in ten.  And I’m paying him a bonus of **fifty bucks** to do it.

**GILLEY**  (staring at her like she just invented electricity)  
That’s… that’s *pretty goddamn cheap.* Fifty bucks? To drive a **band full of emotionally unstable rock stars seven hours back into their trauma?** That’s *a deal*.

He pauses. Then gets *very* Gilley.  Reaches down into his bathrobe, produces his **stage jockstrap** from a pocket that should not exist.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
*Alright, people.*  Let’s make this a **true band affair**.

He holds the jockstrap out like it’s the Holy Grail. Worn, sweat-stained, and undeniably Gilley.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
Anybody want to **pony up some money** for our glorious pilgrimage?  Ladies and gentlemen—Fill it up.  **Fill. It. Up.**

**BILL** (half-gagging)  
I swear to God if that thing still has body heat, I’m moving to Vermont instead.

**JIM**  (sighing, pulling a twenty from his wallet)  
For Jeff.

(beat)
And because this is somehow not the worst way we’ve raised money.

**KATHY**  (throws in a ten, deadpan)  
This is a sex cult now. Fully confirmed.

**JEREMY**  (throws in a twenty, grinning despite himself)  
If we make a documentary, this goes in the cold open.

**CREMEANS**  (watching from a distance)  
You people are the reason I drink Gatorade with aspirin in it.

**GILLEY**  (jockstrap in the air like he’s leading a revolution)  
Thank you!  Thank you, America!  This jockstrap is now an official **fuel fund**.  Let’s go **rescue our bassist** and *reclaim our myth*\!

*They pile onto the bus, cash in the jockstrap, destiny on the horizon.*  The wheels start to turn. And somewhere up I-95?  **Jeff Evans** is about to receive the greatest **fucking surprise** of his life.

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – SOMEWHERE NORTHBOUND ON I-95 – 11:17 A.M.**

The bus hums. Gilley lounges across two seats in his half-tied robe, sipping something fizzy and illegal from a thermos labeled *Tom’s Electrolytes*.

Everyone else is sprawled—Kathy with her boots off, Jeremy watching the road like it owes him answers, Jim working on some kind of makeshift percussion on the table.

**GILLEY** (loud, to the ceiling)  
Alright.  We’re on this **epic northbound odyssey**…This *reverse triumphal march*.  What the fuck are we supposed to **do** with ourselves?  We can’t just sit here **vibing and farting** like a band of tone-deaf hobbits.

**(beat)**

He turns to **Bill**, who’s seated near the back with a notebook, headphones in, legs crossed like a philosopher on deadline.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
Bill.  What sort of **plot notes** you got?  You’re the **sad-synth screenwriter** of the group.  Give me a **structure**.  A story.  A *quest*.

**BILL** (takes one earbud out, doesn’t look up)  
Okay.  Act I — **Delusion of Control**.  That was us in Charlotte. Thinking we could wrap things up neatly.  Act II — **The Fracture**.  That’s Jeff collapsing. Baltimore. The unplugged set. Everything changed.  Act III — **The Reckoning**.  That’s this trip.  This is us *not accepting the end*.  This is the band **trying to undo gravity**.

**GILLEY** (nodding, impressed)  
Oh, fuck, that’s good.

**BILL**  
Act IV — **The Return**.  Not a show.  Not a redemption.  Just us, *carrying it back*.  Whatever "it" is.

**KATHY** (half-asleep)  
If this ends with a funeral, I want to be buried in glitter and spite.

**JIM**  
We should make Kendall *record this*. Every conversation. Every stop. This is the weirdest, rawest thing we’ve ever done.

**JEREMY** (quietly)  
We’re writing the real last album.

**GILLEY** (grinning wide, stretching arms)  
You heard the man.  This bus is a *myth machine now*.  Someone find me a notebook. I’m about to monologue so hard *Tom’s gonna weep at the wheel.*

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – CAB – JUST PAST FAYETTEVILLE, NC – 12:03 P.M.**

Tom’s got one hand on the wheel and one eye on the horizon, sunglasses on, jaw set like a man who has personally survived *at least* four bassists and one bus fire.

From the back—

**GILLEY**  (shouting up toward the cab)  
Hey, **Tom\!** You’re a **well-traveled man**, clearly.  Man of **culture**.  Of *refined taste*. Of *grit*.

Tom doesn’t say anything, just raises an eyebrow in the rearview mirror.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
So let me ask you something of **grave national importance**—Where can I get **good North Carolina barbecue** on **Interstate 95**? I want the real shit. Pork that’s been smoked since **Reagan was president**.  Sauce that bites back.  A hush puppy that could make me cry.

**TOM** (grunts, nods once)  
*White Swan.* Smithfield. Take the **95 Business Loop**.  Two turns. Cinderblock building.  
Looks like a shack. Smells like heaven.  They got chopped pork that'll make you rethink God.

**GILLEY** (slaps the wall of the bus)  
**YES.** This man knows.

**KATHY** (sarcastic)  
Should we detour 40 minutes off-mission for barbecue?

**JIM**  
Yes.  Absolutely.

**BILL**  
If this is the last tour story, it might as well end with vinegar sauce and regret.

**JEREMY** (to Tom)  
Can we swing it?

**TOM**  
Already taking the exit.*Y’all need more pork and less poetry.*

**GILLEY** (write this down, mock-serious)  
Chapter Seven: *Pulled Pork and Redemption*.

---

## **EXT. WHITE SWAN BARBECUE – SMITHFIELD, NC – 1:12 P.M.**

A plume of **woodsmoke and magic** floats out of the squat cinderblock building.  
The band has descended like a pack of apocalypse survivors with a limitless wallet and zero restraint.

They’ve ordered **everything**.

Pulled pork.  
Chopped pork.  
Ribs.  
Fried chicken.  
Slaw.  
Hush puppies.  
Brunswick stew.  
Banana pudding.  
Extra sauce.  
Extra napkins.  
Probably a brick or two of cornbread for *philosophical reasons*.

The **kitchen staff is bewildered**, the **cashier is terrified**, and the **band is triumphant**.

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – MINUTES LATER**

The bus smells like a Southern church picnic collided with a blues festival. Tubs of food are loaded in the aisle. Everyone’s got a Styrofoam container like it’s Christmas and the gift is **meat**. Tom sits in the driver’s seat, already half into a pile of ribs.

**JIM** (shouting from the back)  
We good to move, boss?

**GILLEY**  
Yeah, let’s wolf it all down. Or Tom, *you* wolf, we’ll eat on the road.

**KATHY**  (sincerely curious, licking sauce off her fingers)  
Tom, how does this *work*?  How do **bus drivers eat**, anyway?

**TOM**  (doesn’t even blink)  
*With our mouths.*

*The band loses it—laughing, sauce-drunk, road-happy for the first time in days.*

**BILL**  
This is the most nourishment we’ve had all tour.  Emotionally *and* calorically.

**GILLEY**  (holding up a hush puppy like it's a communion wafer)  
Bless this trip.  Bless this pig.  Bless the strange-ass decision to drive seven hours back into our own emotional reckoning.

**JEREMY**  (mouth full, happy for the first time in days)  
Amen.

*The bus rumbles back onto the highway.*  Next stop: **Baltimore.**  Next chapter: **Closure. Or something like it.**

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – BACK ON I-95 – 2:07 P.M.**

Greasy fingers. Sauce-streaked napkins.  The bus is alive with laughter and bad ideas. The *BBQ high* is peaking.

**Jim**, half-sitting on a cooler, drums lightly on a takeout box with two plastic forks, then **grins like a man possessed**.

**JIM**  
Alright.  Here’s a **stupid game**.  Let’s do a **jam session**.  *But*—**Nobody plays their own instrument.**

The bus groans.

**JEREMY**  
What are you trying to do? Summon chaos gods?

**JIM** (ignoring him)  
That means *somebody’s* gotta play **drums**.  And I swear to God, all you get is a **drumstick**. Maybe **two**.

**KATHY**  
What the fuck are we drumming *on*?

**JIM**  
The **bus**.*Only* the bus.

**GILLEY** (nodding, eyes lit up)  
Ooooh I’m into this.  Rhythms of the road, baby.

**BILL** (low)  
This is how we lose the deposit.

**JIM**  
Come on, come on. Let’s pick.  **Who’s gonna play drums?**  Not me. I’m off-limits.

They all look at each other. One beat. Two beats.  **Everyone turns toward Bill.**

**BILL** (suspicious, slow)  
Why me?

**KATHY**  
Because you have the calmest soul and the most repressed chaos.  It’s time to *let it out.*

**GILLEY**  
Also, I just *really* want to see you hit a window with a chicken bone.

**BILL** (quietly sets down his cornbread, rises)  
Fine. Give me the goddamn sticks.

**JIM** (tosses him two Sharpies)  
Good enough.

**BILL** (serious now, adjusting his posture)  
Let the ritual begin.

*The first strike hits the A/C vent. The second slaps a cupholder. The third thuds against a bulkhead.*A *beat* begins. And just like that?  **The dumbest jam session in rock history** is born.

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – STILL ROLLING NORTH – 2:19 P.M.**

**Bill** is locked in—tapping a rhythm onto the emergency window handle like it’s a sacred mantra.  
Everyone’s half-laughing, half-amazed at how **weirdly good** it sounds.  Then **Gilley**, still bathrobed and spiritually unhinged, stands dramatically in the aisle.

**GILLEY**  
Alright.  I’m calling my shot.  I’m on **synths**.

**KATHY** (suspicious)  
You’ve *never* played a synth in your life.

**GILLEY**  
Which is why it’s gonna be **revolutionary**.

**JEREMY**  
You're gonna ruin the bus speakers *and* the vibe.

**GILLEY**  
Correction—Kathy knows how to play piano, right?

**KATHY**  
Obviously.

**GILLEY**  
And piano is just a **pre-orgasmic synthesizer**.  The emotional foreplay to the real thing.

**JIM**  
Did you just call piano *edging*?

**GILLEY**  
I’m doing **synths**.  **Bill**, *hand it over.*

**BILL** (still calmly drumming on a seatbelt latch)  
There’s no synth on this bus.

**GILLEY**  
Then give me *whatever you have that beeps*.  *That counts.*

**BILL**  
You want the tour manager’s **walkie-talkie**?

**GILLEY**  
Oh *hell* yes.  That’s basically a monophonic delay box with rage issues.

**CREMEANS** (from the front, exhausted)  
If he breaks my walkie, I'm sending the invoice to his father.

**GILLEY**  
Thank you, boss man.

Let’s make some **buscore**.

*He grabs the walkie-talkie, flips it on, starts **looping mic feedback and voice call tones** into rhythmic sputters, pretending he’s playing Coachella 2041\.*

**KATHY** (to Jeremy)  
Why does he sound *kind of amazing*?

**JEREMY**  
Because he’s too stupid to know what failure looks like.

*The jam session intensifies.*  **Drumsticked windows. Walkie-talkie synth. Cupholder reverb.**  
It’s *terrible*.  It’s *brilliant*.  It’s **Commuted**.

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – STILL MOVING – 2:27 P.M.**

The **bus jam session** is in full, chaotic swing.  **Gilley** is cranking feedback out of a walkie-talkie like it’s a Eurorack synth from hell.  **Bill** is calmly tapping on emergency equipment like he's summoning minimalist jazz gods.  **Kathy** is pretending not to enjoy it.

Then—**Jim** stands up with his usual deadpan confidence and clears his throat.

**JIM**  
Okay.  I can **sing**.

**KATHY**  
You’re not allowed to say that with authority unless it involves stage fog and chest hair.

**JIM**  
Excuse you—I did that entire **Fifth Avenue thing**, remember?


**BILL** (frowns)  
What Fifth Avenue thing?

**JIM** (serious)  
Barbershop quartet.  **Kings Island.**  Summer job. *1990*.  I was in a vest and bow tie before any of you had stage monitors.

**GILLEY** (slowly turning)  
You were in a **barbershop quartet** at an **amusement park**?

**JIM**  
Yup.  Wore straw hats. Sang four-part harmony. Nailed *“Sweet Adeline”* so hard that a bachelorette party tipped us in tequila shots.

**JEREMY**  
*Jesus Christ.*

**JIM**  
So.  *I’m playing guitar.*  Jeremy, give me the guitar.

**JEREMY** (grinning, handing it over)  
Be my guest, Sinatra of Cincinnati.

**JIM**  
And you?  You’re on **vocals**.

**JEREMY**  
I can't sing for shit.

**JIM**  
Perfect. That’s *the point*.

*He settles in, tunes the acoustic guitar with surprising grace. Plucks a few chords. It sounds—somehow—like sincerity and sarcasm got drunk together and started a band.*

**GILLEY**  
What’s this called?

**JIM**  
It's called **“The End of the Fucking Tour Blues.”**  *Let’s make this a classic.*

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – I-95, NORTHBOUND – 2:31 P.M.**

The bus vibrates with dumb, beautiful noise.  It’s a tour that ended and refused to stay dead.  They’re heading toward closure—but doing it like **Commuted** always has: *Loud, weird, wrong, and right.*

**GILLEY** (arms out, walkie still in hand like a holy relic)
Alright.  We got **Jeremy** channeling Midwest gospel angst.  We got **Jim**, a literal theme park veteran, on guitar.  We got **Bill**, tapping out minimalist anxiety on an overhead luggage bin.  We got **Kathy**, who could kill us all with one raised eyebrow, holding the emotional center like she’s scoring an arthouse tragedy.

He pauses. Looks around.  Eyes shining, dramatic as hell.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
**Have I forgotten anybody?**

*Beat.*

Everyone looks at each other. Then—

**KATHY**  
If you forget **me**, I put you through the window.

**BILL**  
Tom hasn’t gotten a solo yet.

**CREMEANS**  
I’m not playing crap.  You let me sit in silence and *log mileage*.

**GILLEY** (grinning)
Noted. But I just wanted to make sure—Because we’re heading into **Baltimore** with our instruments wrong, our logic broken, and our **hearts stupidly full**.

He stands on a cooler.  Raises a hush puppy from earlier like a toast.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
To Jeff.  To closure.  To bad rhythm and worse harmonies.  Let’s go *end this thing right.*


---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – NORTHBOUND, STILL A BARBECUE-SCENTED HAVEN – 2:37 P.M.**

They’ve played plastic percussion on ceiling vents.  Jim’s strumming heartfelt nonsense.  Jeremy’s crooning in a key no one can identify.  Gilley’s bouncing in and out of the moment like a rock n’ roll game show host.  Then he stops, turns to **Kathy**, eyes narrowed with faux regret and real intent.

**GILLEY**  
Regretfully…**Regretfully**, *Kathy*—You’re gonna have to go back and play the guitar.  *One night only.*

(beat)
*Technically mid-afternoon, but you get my point.*

**KATHY**  (eyes narrowing, full fire)  
Nope.  **Nope nope nope.**I quit the guitar as a *performer*.  *That’s on the record.*

**GILLEY**  
Oh, this isn’t a **performance**.  This is a **jam**.  Big difference.  Do you see the distinction?  I *quite remember* you quit **performing**.  This?  This is *chaos with rhythm*.  So buckle up, **buttercup**.  Whip out your six-string.

**KATHY** (standing, hands on hips)  
You’re gonna rhyme at me now?

**GILLEY**  
Only in moments of moral crisis.

(turns to Jeremy, grinning)
**Hey Jeremy**, lend—uh—lend **Kathy** a guitar, *why don'tcha?*

**JEREMY** (torn between fear and joy)  
Do I get hit if I say yes?

**KATHY** (snatching the guitar mid-sentence)  
Just *tune it* first.

**JIM**  
We’re gonna need a new track name for this.

**BILL**  
Title it *“Relapse in Drop D.”*

*She sits, fingers already moving with old precision.  Pissed, but also—*slightly alive again.*

**GILLEY**  
Ladies and gentlemen…We are **whole again**.  Let’s finish this jam like it’s *our last mile home.*

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – STILL NORTHBOUND, NOW FULL-ON BAND ON THE RUN – 2:41 P.M.**

The bus has become a mobile music warzone.  Everyone has the wrong instrument.  Everyone is running on adrenaline, hush puppies, and *emotionally significant pulled pork*.  **Kathy** is begrudgingly tuning the guitar.  **Bill** is playing synth drums on the back of a seatbelt buckle.  
**Gilley** is conducting like a preacher on cough syrup.  And **Jeremy** stands up slowly, arms raised like he’s about to deliver a sermon.

**JEREMY**  
Alright.  Since I’ve been **elected** vocalist—And since I have **very limited range**, emotionally *and* vocally—I’m picking the first track.

(beat)
***Jeremiah was a bullfrog.***

*The bus goes still for a half-beat.*

Then:

**GILLEY**  
*FUCK YES.*

**JIM** (classic dad nod)  
That’s righteous.

**BILL**  
A bold choice. Spiritually loaded.

**KATHY**  
Only song dumber than this jam session. I approve.

**JEREMY**  (grinning now)  
*And hit it.*

**Kathy** strikes the first chord—gritty, raw, perfectly *off*. **Bill** slaps out a rhythm on a paper cup. **Jim** harmonizes like an off-brand barbershop ghost. **Gilley**? He’s dancing with a takeout box. And **Jeremy**, voice cracking with sincerity, launches into:

*“Jeremiah was a bullfrog—*  
*Was a good friend of mine…”*

The whole bus starts screaming the chorus before he even gets there.  It’s off-key, off-time, and **absolutely perfect**.

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – STILL BARRELING TOWARD BALTIMORE – 2:49 P.M.**

The band just **screamed through “Jeremiah Was a Bullfrog”**, and the bus is vibrating with joy, bad harmonies, and what might be divine nonsense. **Jeremy** is half-bent over, breathless, grinning, proud, *regretting everything*.  And **Kathy**, who has been waiting for this exact moment of **peak male vulnerability**, pounces.

**KATHY**  
Oh **okay**, Mr. Evans! *Big man on vocals\!* You wanna show us range? *You wanna do this?*

She leans in with dangerous calm, still strumming the wrong chords like a queen with a blade.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**  
Then **go Vogue.**

(beat)
As in **Madonna**.  **Vogue**, bitch.

**JEREMY**  (eyes wide, panic rising)  
No. Absolutely not.

**KATHY**  
**Suck it, Trebek!** Do it! This is what you get for having a **girl in the band**.

**JIM**  
You *did* say you’d sing whatever we threw at you.

**BILL** (slowly pressing record on his phone)  
This is archival gold.

**GILLEY**  
You better *strike a pose*, son. Or I swear I’ll remix this moment into a ringtone.

**CREMEANS** (from the front)  
If he vogues while in socks, I quit tour managing forever.

**JEREMY** (staggering to his feet, eyes darting, hands up)  
I don’t even know the—

**KATHY** (spits the first line at him)  
*“Look around, everywhere you turn is heartache…”*
*…It’s everywhere that you go—*

**GILLEY** (to Jeremy, whispering like an evil stage mom)  
You better find that flow, honey.

**JEREMY** (raising his arms like a hostage)  
FINE. But if I’m going down, we’re *all* going to hell with me.

He strikes a clumsy pose. Then another.  It’s part **nightmare**, part **drag brunch miracle**, part **gym teacher at prom**. And then he **sings**:

*“Strike a pose…*  
*There’s nothing to it—Vogue.”*

The whole bus **erupts**. **Kathy** is doubled over, cackling like a villain. **Jim** is harmonizing again, somehow making it sound like a gospel choir breakdown. **Gilley** is dancing with a roll of toilet paper like it’s a feather boa. And **Bill** just says one word:

**BILL**  
*Transcendent.*

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – STILL BARRELING UP I-95 – 2:57 P.M.**

The air is thick with **leftover barbecue** and the aftershock of **Jeremy’s Vogue performance**, which has left the band in *emotional tatters*.  They’re sprawled, laughing, rehydrating, buzzing.  Then **Kathy** leans forward, guitar on her lap, eyes sly and loaded.

**KATHY**  
Okay—I’ve been **thinking about this** for a second…

Everyone turns, bracing themselves.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**  
If **Jeff** were here?  If he were *actually on this bus*, doing this *insane-ass jam session* with us—You know what song he’d end up picking.

**GILLEY**  (squinting)  
Um…You’re gonna have to give me *something* to work with here.

**KATHY**  (lifts one eyebrow)  
It’d be **Duran Duran**.

*The bus goes silent for half a breath—*Then it **explodes**.

**ALL (in unison):**  
**“HUNGRY LIKE THE WOLF\!”**

**JIM**  
Yes! *Yes\!*  That’s *so Jeff*.

**JEREMY**  
He once said that song made him want to get laid *and* fight a tiger.

**BILL**  
He called it “synths with hair on their chest.”

**GILLEY**  (throws both hands up, already dancing)  
*I AM THE HUNGRY! I AM THE WOLF\!*

**CREMEANS**  (panicking from the driver’s area)  
If anyone breaks the overhead lights doing 80s choreography, I swear I will reroute this bus to Delaware and leave you there.

**KATHY**  
Alright. Who’s got the bass line?

**BILL**  
I got you.

*He starts thumping it out on the back of the bus fridge* like it’s a keytar from hell.

**JIM**  
Jeremy, you’re back on vocals.  Try not to die this time.

**JEREMY**  
Growl or no growl?

**KATHY**  
Full **predator mode**.

**GILLEY**  
It’s time.  Time to *honor Jeff* the only way we know how—*by making asses of ourselves* in the name of **pure synth passion.**

The bus erupts into the first clunky, glorious notes of the most unhinged **Duran Duran cover** ever performed **between highway exits**.

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – MOVING NORTH ON I-95 – 3:08 P.M.**

Everyone’s recovering from the musical car crash that was **“Hungry Like the Wolf.”**  **Jeremy** is sprawled on the couch, wheezing.  **Jim** is nursing a bottle of water like it's whiskey.  **Bill** is staring into the void, muttering something about sequencers and shame.  **Kathy** is silently handing out wet wipes like a camp counselor at a glitter cult.

**Gilley**?  Standing in the aisle, doing a final pose.  Then he blinks.

**GILLEY**  (squinting at the front of the bus)
Wait a minute.

**Everyone turns, following his gaze.**

There’s **Cremeans**, hunched over his clipboard, headset in, still multitasking like he’s commanding a military operation—completely unaffected by the synth-pop carnage behind him.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
*Wait.* *Hold on.* *I thought we left you back in **Charlotte**.* 

(beat)
**Oops.**

**CREMEANS**  (still writing, not looking up)  
I paid Tom twenty bucks to stay silent until someone noticed.

**KATHY** (half-laughs, half-chokes)  
We kidnapped our **tour manager**?

**JIM**  
Reverse hostage situation.

**BILL**  
You *chose* to be here?

**CREMEANS** (gruff, still working)  
You idiots can’t go to Baltimore unsupervised.

**GILLEY** (sincerely impressed)  
You’re either the **most dedicated man** alive or the **most broken**.

**CREMEANS**  
Both. Now shut up while I reschedule *your canceled encore* into a **post-hospital acoustic apology tour**.

**GILLEY** (nods solemnly)  
We don’t deserve you.

*And with that, the bus rolls on—toward Baltimore, toward Jeff, toward whatever weird redemption waits at the end of the highway.*

---


## **INT. TOUR BUS – ROLLING THROUGH NORTHERN VIRGINIA – 3:19 P.M.**

The bus still smells like sauce and music.  Everyone’s **sweaty**, **loopy**, and running on the fumes of emotional catharsis and synthetic 80s hooks.  Gilley bounces down the aisle like a man possessed by **Springsteen, cocaine, and cartoon physics**.

**GILLEY** (shouting to the front)  
Alright!  We’ve done the dumb, we’ve done the heartfelt, we’ve done the *deeply questionable*. Three more songs, people. **Three more**, and we’ll probably be in **another state**\!

He leans around the corner toward the front cab.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
Hey **Tom**— My man, my myth, my V8-powered prophet—How much longer? **How much longer there, buddy?**

**TOM** (glances at map, deadpan)  
One hour, forty-five minutes.

**GILLEY** (grins)  
Perfect. That’s like… **six songs** if we slow jam *“Bohemian Rhapsody”* and throw in a spoken-word breakdown.

**KATHY**  
Please no spoken-word breakdowns. We barely survived *Vogue*.

**JIM**  
Seconded.   If I hear Gilley say “let’s vibe with it” one more time, I’m throwing him out the roof hatch.

**GILLEY** (still bouncing)  
I’m just saying—This is our **rolling epilogue**. By the time we hit the city line, we need a **setlist that says something**.

**JEREMY**  
It’s saying something, alright. It’s saying *“this band needs group therapy and a salad.”*

**CREMEANS** (over his shoulder, still on the phone)  
Y’all need *Jesus* and *electrolytes.*

**GILLEY**  
Then give me a **banger**, people!  Let’s finish the **Buscore Sessions** strong!  We’ve got less than two hours.  Three songs minimum.  **Let’s get weird.**

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – RUMBLING THROUGH MARYLAND BORDER – 3:38 P.M.**

The mood is unhinged, glorious.  Sweat. Crumbs. Vinyl-slap percussion.  They’re a cult on wheels, chasing closure with barbecue breath and ‘80s hooks. Then **Kathy**, strumming idly on the borrowed guitar, looks up—cool, half-lidded, calculating.

**KATHY**  
Next song?  *Need You Tonight.*  **Michael Hutchence.**

(beat)
I **so** wanna fuck him.

**JIM** (cocking an eyebrow)  
I thought you said you were **queer**?

**KATHY** (turning, deadpan, razor-edged)  
I said—*and I quote*—**“You can’t label me.”**

**BILL** (to no one)  
That's going on a t-shirt.

**JEREMY** (tired, wary)  
Wait wait wait. If we do *Need You Tonight*, that means…

**JIM** (grinning, devilish)  
Then we’re doing **Mediate** as the **chaser track**.

(beat)
And *you’re rapping*.

**GILLEY** (bursting out of his seat)  
**HELL YEAH.**

**KATHY**  
Yup. You opened your mouth, now you’re **Hutchence-adjacent.**

**JEREMY** (defensive)  
I don’t rap.  I talk rhythmically when under duress.

**GILLEY**  
That’s perfect. That’s **exactly** what “Mediate” needs.

**CREMEANS** (from the front, without turning around)  
I’m calling the label and telling them the band’s releasing a concept record called *Bus Breakdown: Live from I-95.*

**KATHY**  
Alright. Hutchence time.  Gilley, get sultry.  Bill, do your digital voodoo.  Jeremy—

(spins to him, grinning)
Start warming up those white-boy syllables.

**JEREMY** (mutters)  
I swear, if anyone records this, I’m suing the group.

*The engine hums. The lights dim. The bus becomes a shrine to the **ghost of INXS**.*  And then the chords begin.

**KATHY (softly)**  
*Come over here…*

**THE BAND (in unison):**  
*'Cause I need you tonight…*

**GILLEY**  
Let’s get **horny and poetic**, people.

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – JUST OUTSIDE BALTIMORE – 3:51 P.M.**

The bus is a wreck of laughter, sweat, and empty banana pudding cups.  They’re maybe 30 minutes out.  The city looms.  But the energy is *still climbing*, and **Jim** rises like a conductor with malice in his heart.

**JIM**  
Ladies and gentlemen—The next song?  There’s **no way** Jeremy’s got the **range** for it.
Like, structurally.  Vocally.  Anatomically.

**KATHY** (grinning behind her guitar)  
He might just **lose a testicle**, so please keep your valuables tucked and your dignity intact.

**JIM**  
Jeremy?  You’re gonna need to **dedicate your very soul** to this one.

**He locks eyes with him.**

**JIM (CONT’D)**  
Next song:  **Take On Me.**  *And hit that note, dude.*

**JEREMY** (looks at Jim like he just suggested skydiving into a dumpster)  
This is the **broccoli of music**.

**KATHY** (snorting)  
You are **never** going to come close.

**GILLEY** (striking a dramatic pose)  
But that’s what makes it **art**.

**BILL**  
I'll approximate the synth line with a straw and an empty soda cup.

**CREMEANS**  
We’re gonna get pulled over for **sonic abuse**.

**JEREMY** (sighs, standing, cracking his neck)  
Fine.  I’ll go down like a **hero**.

**KATHY**  
No, sweetie. You’ll go down like a *dying elk*.

**JEREMY**  
Same difference.

*The beat kicks in—Bill whips up a synth impression so janky it’s perfect.*  *Kathy slams into the chords.*  *Gilley’s doing interpretive dance with a bag of Fritos.*  And Jeremy steps up to the invisible mic.

*“Talking away…*  
*I don’t know what…*  
*What to say I’ll say it anyway…”*

Everyone watches with slack-jawed awe.  He's not good. *But he is **committed.***

Until he hits *that note*—

*“TAKE… OOOON… MEEEEEEEEEEE—”*

**VOICE CRACK. VEIN POP. REGRET.**

**KATHY**  
OH MY GOD.

**JIM**  
*Down goes the testicle\!*

**GILLEY**  
That note just called its lawyer!

**JEREMY**  (grabbing his chest, gasping)  
*I saw the face of God… and it was falsetto.*

*The bus is **howling**.* And as they barrel toward Baltimore, they know: They’ve hit rock bottom **in the most beautiful way**.

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – CLOSING IN ON BALTIMORE – 4:07 P.M.**

The windows are rattling. The snack supply is decimated. Morale is at an all-time *unhinged*.

**Jeremy** is pacing like a preacher with a vendetta.  Everyone's still wheezing from the disaster of *Take On Me* when he stops, turns, and *locks eyes* with **Kathy**.

**JEREMY**  
You think you’re **hot shit**, don’t you?

**KATHY** (smiling coolly)  
Only because I am.

**JEREMY**  
Let me just run the timeline—You quit guitar, what… **five and a half, six years ago**?  Am I right?

**KATHY**  
Six years and three months.

**JEREMY**  
Perfect.  Because *this* is how we’re gonna end it.  *This* is how we’re going to **tie up everything**.

He steps back, sweeping his arm across the bus like a stage.

**JEREMY (CONT’D)**  
And this is where **Kathy Espich** either looks **really cool**—Or falls on her **fucking face**.

**GILLEY** (cackling)  
This better be a song with vengeance in its soul.

**JEREMY**  
Oh, it is.

(leans in, voice low and evil)
**Name that tune.**

**KATHY**  (leans back, unfazed)  
Bring it.

**JEREMY**  
***Welcome to the Jungle**, baby.*

(beat)
**You’re gonna die.**

*The bus **explodes** in screams and laughter.*

**JIM**  
This is either going to make history…Or a *lawsuit*.

**BILL** (quietly)  
I give it three measures before the bus needs medical attention.

**GILLEY** (swinging an empty water bottle like a mic stand)  
There’s no way she even gets *close* to what Slash was doing.  But my God, I want to *watch her try.*

**KATHY** (stretching her fingers, cracking her neck)  
You want jungle? I’ll give you *deforestation, bitch.*

She stands up, snatches the guitar from the corner like she’s grabbing a sword off a rack.  Starts testing the riff. It’s *clumsy at first*, the engine hiccups, but then—Something *clicks.*  The tone tightens. The notes land sharper. It’s not Slash.  It’s not perfect. It’s **Kathy**, six years removed, *sounding like revenge warmed over in leather and gasoline*.

**GILLEY**  
*OHHHHH SHITTTTT—*

**JEREMY** (palms in the air, mock-respectful)  
Okay. Okay. Let’s burn this jungle **down**.

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – FINAL STRETCH TO BALTIMORE – 4:12 P.M.**

The bus is practically **vibrating** with tension.  Everyone’s leaned in:  **Gilley** perched on the armrest like a groupie at a séance.  **Jeremy** half-grinning, half-wincing in advance.  **Jim and Bill** clutching air instruments like shields. Even **Cremeans**, dead-eyed from paperwork, is watching from the front mirror.

And then—**Kathy** stands.  No ceremony.  No preamble.  Just her, a six-string, and **six years of silence** breaking open like thunder.

She hits the first few chords of **“Welcome to the Jungle.”**  And it’s **not perfect**.  It’s *not clean.* But it is **alive**.  It’s raw, dirty, dangerous.  It’s the sound of someone **reclaiming a weapon they laid down in pain**.

The bus goes *dead silent* as the riff takes form—**Snarling. Staggering. Building.**

**GILLEY** (low, awed)  
She’s cooking.  **She’s really cooking.**

**BILL**  
We should have made her mad *years ago*.

**JIM**  
That guitar’s going through it like it owes her rent.

**JEREMY** (folding his arms)  
Okay, okay. I concede.

*She’s not falling on her face.* She’s **clawing it off someone else’s.**  Kathy hits the **signature drop** into the main riff and *doesn’t even smile*.She’s not playing for them.  She’s not playing for applause.  She’s playing for **herself**.

And somehow, in this sweaty bus flying toward the city where everything changed—  Kathy Espich becomes the **loudest person in the band**, without saying a single word.

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – CLOSING IN ON BALTIMORE – 4:15 P.M.**

**Kathy** ends the intro like a guillotine—sharp, loud, no apologies.  She nods once.  Then, without looking, **hands the spotlight to Jeremy**.

**KATHY** (low, satisfied)  
All yours, frontman. Let’s see what you’re made of.

**JEREMY** (staring ahead, blinking)  
I’m not ready.

**GILLEY**  
*Exactly.*

**JIM**  
*Earn your falsetto.*

**BILL** (whispers)  
He’s either going to ascend or combust.

*Jeremy inhales deep.*  *Straightens his spine.*  *Stands up like a man about to be sacrificed at a denim altar.* And then he **lets it rip**:

*“Welcome to the jungle—we got fun and games…”*

It’s not Axl.  It’s not clean.  But it’s got **teeth**. There’s a desperation to it. A growl. A *nervous rage* that feels almost **too real**. The band goes absolutely **feral** behind him.

**GILLEY**  (screaming in harmony)  
***“We got everything you want, honey—we know the names\!\!”***

**KATHY** (growling backup)  
Sing it like your throat’s on *fire and glitter*\!

**JEREMY**  (voice cracking gloriously)
*“Welcome to the jungle, it gets worse here every day—”*

He grabs a **Fritos bag** as a fake mic and leans into the aisle, working the imaginary crowd of bus seats and stunned bandmates.  By the time he hits:

*“You’re in the jungle baby—YOU’RE GONNA DIEEEEE\!”*

He *doesn’t even care* how bad it sounds.  He’s free.

The final chord hits.  ***HUAH***.  Everyone is *gasping, howling, applauding.* **Tom** honks the horn from the front.

**Cremeans** just says, flatly:

**CREMEANS**  
If the cops pull us over, I’m blaming Axl Rose’s ghost.

**GILLEY** (sprawled across a bench, breathless)  
We peaked.  It’s never getting better than this.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL PARKING LOT – BALTIMORE – 5:06 P.M.**

The **tour bus screeches to a halt**, coughing diesel fumes into the late afternoon light.  Everyone inside is sweaty, euphoric, and **absolutely done**.  As the band gathers their trash, instruments, and shattered dignity, **Tom** cuts the engine, takes off his sunglasses, and turns in his seat.

**TOM** (flatly, to the front of the bus)  
Hey, Cremeans?

**CREMEANS** (still scrolling through his phone, drained)  
Yeah?

**TOM**  
I want a **bonus.**

(beat)
I mean… *really, man?* *Really?*

**CREMEANS** (doesn’t even look up)  
You got hush puppies.

**TOM**  
I also got three hours of **synths played through a walkie-talkie**, a man in a **bathrobe doing interpretive dance**, and a **surprise falsetto Guns N’ Roses cover** that made me question the concept of pitch.

**GILLEY** (from the back, still shirtless)  
You *loved* it. Admit it. You honked the horn in time.

**TOM**  
That was muscle memory. From *war*.

**CREMEANS** (sighs, pockets his phone)  
You want hazard pay?

**TOM**  
I want **therapy pay**. And maybe a **gift card** to *anywhere that doesn’t smell like armpit and nostalgia*.

**CREMEANS** (grudgingly)  
You’ll get a **Target card and a therapist’s phone number**.

**TOM** (deep, satisfied nod)  
That’s all I wanted.

*The door hisses open. Baltimore waits. And Tom—driver, witness, silent saint—knows he has **earned every penny**.*

---

## **EXT. HOSPITAL PARKING LOT – BALTIMORE – 5:08 P.M.**

The band is **filing out** of the bus, groggy, triumphant, carrying sauce-stained bags of gear and hope.  **Tom**, still at the wheel, leans back, arms crossed, watching them go like a dad seeing his kids off to summer camp—for the fifth time this year.

He mutters, just loud enough for **Cremeans** to hear:

**TOM**  
Can’t wait for the **arena portion** of the tour.  Come **December**.

**CREMEANS** (slow head turn)  
You mean the one with **elevated rotating drum risers**, **hydraulic lifts**, and **ninety-minute soundchecks**?

**TOM**  
Yup.  With **two buses**, a **merch truck**, and **Gilley’s pyro demands** that *require fire marshal approval in three states*.

**GILLEY** (from outside)  
I want *flamethrowers that spell our name*, Tom.  It's called *branding.*

**TOM**  (sipping coffee from a Styrofoam cup like it's whiskey)  
I’m bringing **earplugs**, a **flask**, and a **handwritten will**.

**CREMEANS** (sighs)  
You’re gonna want the deluxe insurance policy.

**TOM**  
Already upgraded.  It’s under "**Survival Clause A: Emotional Damage from Prolonged Exposure to Musicians.**"

*He flicks on the hazard lights, chuckling dryly, as the band walks into the hospital lobby like they’re about to rescue a bandmate and, somehow, their collective soul.*

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL LOBBY – BALTIMORE – 5:11 P.M.**

The automatic doors whoosh open.  The band—sweaty, emotionally wrung out, still carrying takeout containers and absurd pride—files into the sterile light of the hospital.  At the front desk, they ask for **Jeff Evans**, then make their way down the corridor like a gang of overgrown children storming a birthday party for one.

**Kathy** leads the pack.  She’s **worn out**, **grimy**, and **completely done** being trapped in a 45-foot rolling pressure cooker with **five men and one harmonica**.

**KATHY** (speaking like a general who's seen war)  
**Three buses, Jeff.**

**JEREMY** (stifling a grin)  
We haven’t even seen him yet.

**KATHY**  
I don’t care if he’s *sedated*, *nude*, or *holding court with the nurses*—He needs to understand this.  **Three. Buses.**

**GILLEY**  
Three? That’s excessive. That’s diva behavior.

**KATHY**  
You put the **Evans brothers** on one.  You put **me** on **my own**.  And then you put the other **three idiots** in the third.  That’s **three buses**.

**BILL**  
Am I one of the three idiots?

**KATHY**  
You **drummed on a refrigerator handle**, Bill. Take a guess.

**JIM**  
So just to clarify: You want a bus for **guitar, glitter, and emotional stability**?

**KATHY**  
I want a bus for **quiet**.  And *moisturizer*.  And *my own goddamn Bluetooth speaker*.

**CREMEANS** (from the back, quietly)  
No Kathy, you're not gonna get one to yourself.

**GILLEY**  
But she’s gonna be broadcasting *Sade and vengeance* at volume 6 for 300 miles straight.

**KATHY**  
Exactly.  **Three buses.**  Or next time, I quit and start a solo ambient noise project called *Get Out of My Face*.

They reach the door to Jeff’s room.  Kathy stops.  Smooths her hair.  Takes a deep breath.  Then—

**KATHY (softening, barely)**  
But first, we say hi.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL – OUTSIDE JEFF’S ROOM – 5:14 P.M.**

The band gathers around the door like a group of sleep-deprived fugitives carrying takeout and trauma.  A **young nurse** stands in front of them, clipboard in hand, trying to maintain order with professional calm.

**NURSE**  
Just so you’re aware—You’ll need to be **very, very quiet**.  He’s been **resting comfortably** since this afternoon.

**KATHY** (squints)
Oh yeah?

(beat)
Then *who sucked his dick*?

*The hallway freezes. Every band member stiffens like someone just fired a gun full of glitter and lawsuits.*

**KATHY (CONT’D)**  
Because that’s the **only way** I know Jeff *rests comfortably*.

**NURSE** (blinking, stunned)
Excuse me?

**CREMEANS** (dry as dust)  
She processes stress… *creatively*.

**JIM** (to the nurse, half-whispering)  
That’s not even the worst thing she’s said today.

**GILLEY** (sincerely)  
We had a walkie-talkie synth solo. This is nothing.

**KATHY**  
I’m just saying—If he’s *actually resting*?  Somebody in this building deserves a **thank-you bouquet and a confidentiality agreement**.

**NURSE** (trying not to smirk, failing)  
He’s sedated. And stable. And clean.  But… I’ll let him know you were concerned.

**KATHY**  
You're a peach.  Now let us in before we accidentally jam again.


*The nurse opens the door.  The band walks in, absurd and aching and ready to bring their brother back into the fold—With hugs. With food.  And, unfortunately, with **Gilley** still in a bathrobe.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – JEFF’S ROOM – 5:15 P.M.**

**Jeff Evans** lies in bed, deeply sedated, a soft beeping monitor his only rhythm.  The band is crammed inside the small room like a rock & roll hostage situation—bags of food, sweat, and unresolved emotion **everywhere**.  They all stare.  For a long, quiet second.

Then—

**JEREMY**  
Jesus…He’s **still sedated**?

**GILLEY** (after a pause)  
This is kind of **lame**, not gonna lie.

**JIM**  
We jammed for **seven hours**.  On the **interstate**.  With **trash instruments**.  And he’s just here… *asleep?*

**KATHY**  
Did we just drive across three states to perform a concert for a *coma patient*?

**BILL**  
We peaked at “Welcome to the Jungle” and he missed *all of it*.

**GILLEY** (to the nurse, dramatically)  
When’s he gonna **wake up**, huh?  Like, is this **sedated** like…

(gestures wildly)
*“I’m getting a tooth pulled”* sedation?  Or is this *“don’t wake him or he’ll start vibrating and speak in tongues again”* sedation?

**NURSE** (sipping from her coffee, unfazed)  
It’s hospital-grade sedation.  We wanted to keep his brain quiet until the neuro team gives the green light.

**JEREMY** (quietly to the group)  
He’s missing *the most honest moment we’ve had in years*…

**KATHY** (snorts)  
Yeah. That tracks.

**CREMEANS**  
Don’t worry. I recorded **everything**.  When he wakes up, we’ll make him relive it **in chronological horror.**

**GILLEY** (flat, arms crossed)  
I just wanted him to hear me *rap “Mediate.”*  Is that so much to ask?

**JIM**  
We should’ve brought a speaker and blasted the “Take On Me” falsetto into his IV.

**KATHY**  
That would’ve *killed him*.

They all stare at Jeff again.  Peaceful.  Still.  Totally oblivious to the **greatest acoustic trash tour** in history unfolding in his honor.  

**GILLEY** (staring)  
He better wake up soon.  I brought ribs.  And *regret*.


---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – JEFF’S ROOM – 5:17 P.M.**

The band stands awkwardly around Jeff’s bed.  Monitors beep.  Jeff’s out cold.  Sedated.

Still.  **Too still.**The nurse’s words hang in the air like static: *“The neuro team hasn’t cleared him yet.”*  And that’s when **Jeremy** speaks up.

**JEREMY** (quietly at first)  
Wait—*What was that about the **neurological team?***  What does that mean?

He glances at the nurse. Then at Cremeans. Then back at **Jeff**, unmoving.  His voice gets sharper.  Louder.

**JEREMY (CONT’D)**  
Does that imply something’s **wrong with his brain**?  Because I could’ve told you that.

**GILLEY**  
Jeremy…

**JEREMY**  
No no no, listen—I’ve **lived with him** my whole life.  He showed up one day in **1973** with that face and that voice and that weird thing he does with cereal—And by **1978** I was so **sick of him** I tried to hide his bike in the lake.  But he’s my **older brother**, okay?  So **what the fuck is wrong with him, guys?**

*The room goes quiet.*  **Dead quiet.**  No one has an answer.  Not yet.  Just the hum of the machines.  Just the weight of every lyric they ever wrote **about pain they thought was poetic**… now **hooked up to a monitor**.

**KATHY** (soft, real)  
We don’t know yet.  But we’re gonna find out.  And we’re here now.

**JIM**  
We’re all here.

**GILLEY**  
And we’re not going anywhere.

**JEREMY** (staring at Jeff, barely above a whisper)  
Yeah.  That’s what scares me.  What if he is?

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 5:19 P.M.**

**Jeremy** has just spilled **two decades of brotherhood trauma** into the air, and the silence that follows is **heavy**.  Then—**Bill**, sitting in the corner like a poet who misplaced his synth pad, speaks up.

**BILL**  
I mean—Is he like **out**?  Like…Out out?  Like we need to go pay the **light bill** to get him back on?

**GILLEY** (snorting softly)  
Or do we have to **string a line from the street**, like some kind of illegal brain jumper cables?

**BILL**  
How long’s he **down** for?

**NURSE** (pulling out her chart, calm but hesitant)  
He’s supposed to stay **under** until around **9 p.m.**, give or take.  But—

(beat)
We’re not quite sure how his **metabolism** is responding yet.

**KATHY**  
Because of the migraine?

**NURSE**  
And the **cumulative stress**.  And the fact that he probably hadn’t slept more than two hours at a time in *weeks*.

**JIM** (sighs, folding his arms)  
So we just wait?

**NURSE**  
Yup.  We wait.

**CREMEANS**  
This is gonna be the longest four hours of our tour.

**JEREMY** (softly, eyes locked on Jeff)  
No.  It’s the **first four hours** of the next one.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 5:28 P.M.**

The band has settled into awkward, unsettled positions.  Jeff’s monitors beep softly.  A nurse walks through and leaves again.  The door clicks shut.  No one says anything for a beat.  Then **Kathy**, arms crossed, voice low, says what they’re all thinking.

**KATHY**  
If it ain’t drugs…Then **what the hell is it?**

**JEREMY** (staring at the floor)  
Yeah.  That’s what’s **eating me**.

**GILLEY** (sitting cross-legged on the couch, robe slightly more respectful now)  
So we’re all thinking it, right?

**BILL**  
Yeah.

(quiet)
What if he’s just… **working himself to death**?

**JIM**  
Or what if this is the start of some **neurological thing**?  Some **chronic**, or *degenerative*—

**JEREMY**  
Don’t.

**KATHY**  
He’s been like this for years. Hiding it. Laughing it off.  But what if this isn’t a breakdown?  What if it’s a **diagnosis**?

**CREMEANS**  
We don’t know anything yet.

**GILLEY**  
And that’s what’s worse.  Because our best-case scenario is “Jeff’s tired.”  And our worst-case is… *what?*

**BILL**  
*Early-onset dementia?  Multiple sclerosis?  Brain tumor?*

**JIM**  
Or he’s just… **unraveling**.  Fast.

**JEREMY** (quiet, raw)  
Or maybe he’s been unraveling **this whole time**, and we just thought it was a *bit*.

*The room stills. No one laughs. Not this time.*

**KATHY**  
We keep saying “Jeff’s a weirdo,” like that makes it okay.  But maybe the weird wasn’t harmless.  Maybe it was **louder than we wanted to hear**.

**JEREMY** (small)  
How **broke** is he?  Like—*Not bank account broke.*  *Inside broke.*

**GILLEY** (whispers)  
What if we missed it?

*They sit with it. Every show. Every bus ride. Every time they laughed it off and moved on.*  **Jeff** still lies there.  Still silent.  Still **not okay.**

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 5:38 P.M.**

The band’s standing around, nursing **unfinished coffee**, staring at the **wall**, **shifting weight**, trying not to let the worry claw at their chests.  **Jeremy**, who’s been holding it in for hours, finally **explicitly reiterates** the question that’s been slowly simmering beneath every comment, every sideways glance.

**JEREMY** (firm, steady)  
Kathy.  How **broke** is Jeff?  *You know him. You’ve been—*  

(slight hesitation)  
You’ve been **fucking on and off for the last nine years**.

The words drop like bricks, and **Kathy’s head jerks up** like she wasn’t expecting that bluntness. **Her gaze locks onto Jeremy**. She exhales—heavily.

**KATHY** (stiff, uncomfortable)  
I have no clue.

(beat)
Isn’t he married?  Didn’t he like **get married three years ago**?

**JIM**  
What does that have to do with anything?

**KATHY** (slightly defensive)  
I mean, are we just gonna pretend that his **wife** isn’t involved in any of this?  Do you think so little of her that we haven’t **even contacted her yet**?

She turns to **Cremeans**, and the question hangs in the air. The tension builds.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**  
Cremeans, **you did contact her**, right?

**CREMEANS** (pulling his headset off, sighing)  
Yes, yes.  Did you think I was **stupid**?

(beat)
The flight doesn’t hit the airport for another hour and a half.

**KATHY** (frowning, exasperated)  
Then we wait.

(beat)
But we shouldn’t wait.  She’s his wife. She has **every right** to know.  You’re not telling me **we’ve been sitting here, talking about this, while she’s still in the dark?**

**CREMEANS** (quiet, but with urgency)  
She knows we’ve been in touch.  But… yeah. She’s on her way.

**JEREMY** (cutting through the tension)  
I don’t know what to think anymore. He was just here, **alive**, a few days ago.  What happened?

**KATHY** (calm but insistent)  
What happened was that Jeff's been **suppressing** shit for **so long**.  And now it's **coming out**.

(beat)
This isn’t about **how much he’s making** or **how much he’s spending**.  This is about *how much we’ve been ignoring*.  We all knew something was **off**, but none of us **asked**.

**JIM** (somber)  
I guess we’re all **too used to him being the weird one**. The one who *never* followed the rules.

**KATHY** (looking at Jeff, almost whispering)  
But that’s the problem, Jim.  He followed his own rules.  He just never told us what they were.

The silence **settles**, heavier now.  The clock ticks.  The doors to **Jeff's room** are still closed.

**JEREMY** (gently, to Kathy)  
So you have **no idea** how bad it could be?

**KATHY** (softly)  
No.  But I think we’re about to find out.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – JEFF’S ROOM – 6:02 P.M.**

**Jeff** is still sedated.  The band sits in scattered silence—**Kathy**, **Jeremy**, **Gilley**, **Jim**, **Bill**, and **Cremeans**.  It’s quiet except for the heartbeat monitor, a soft metronome ticking out every second they didn’t use well.

**JIM** (quiet)  
You ever think about how we got here?

**BILL**  
In a literal sense?  Or like… *cosmic band therapy* sense?

**JIM**  
Both.

(beat)
But mostly the part where **we all saw this coming**, and none of us said a goddamn thing.

**KATHY** (sighs, staring at Jeff)  
We let him fall apart.  And we *called it a quirk*.

**GILLEY**  
We called it Jeff being Jeff.

**JEREMY**  
We joked about it.  Every time he flaked out in soundcheck, or forgot a lyric, or lost a full night of sleep and showed up like a fucking ghost.

**CREMEANS**  
You all kept moving like the only thing that mattered was the next city.  The next gig.

**KATHY**  
Because we didn’t know how to stop.  Or how to *ask*.

**JIM**  (quiet)  
Or we just didn’t want to hear the answer.

**BILL**  
You think he would’ve told us?  If we’d asked?

**JEREMY** (soft)  
He’s my brother.  And I think maybe he *tried* to tell me.  In his own way.  I just… didn’t want to hear it.

**GILLEY**  
We all got real good at ignoring the silence.

**KATHY** (slowly)  
That silence cost us.  Trust.  Time.  Maybe the only real chance we had to keep this thing from breaking.

**CREMEANS**  
It’s not just about the show.

**JEREMY**  
It never was.

*A long pause. The monitor beeps. Jeff shifts slightly in bed.*

**KATHY** (small, almost to herself)  
We all built something beautiful.  And we filled it with sound so we wouldn’t have to hear what was cracking underneath.

**JIM**  
You think we still have time to fix it?

**GILLEY**  
Depends.

(beat)
On whether he wakes up.  And what he says when he does.

*They fall into silence again.*  *But this one’s different.*  *This one’s honest.*

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 6:26 P.M. – SAME DAY**

The door opens.  **Jeff’s wife steps in**—sharp-eyed, tightly wound, still carrying the stress of **two flights and thirty hours of emotional freefall**.  She scans the room—Jeff still unconscious, the band loitering awkwardly around him like guilty teenagers at a crime scene.

She doesn't ask.  She *judges silently* for a beat.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
So this is the room.

(sarcastic)
Nice to know you all beat me here.

**JEREMY**  
We left Charlotte as soon as we heard.

**KATHY**  
We didn’t know what else to do.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  (grim smile)  
You could’ve waited.  You could’ve let me walk in *first* for once.

*Everyone stiffens. She walks to the side of the bed, takes Jeff’s hand.*

**JEFF’S WIFE (CONT’D)**  (quiet)  
I haven’t known what to do for months.  Now you’re all here like you’re waiting for him to wake up and tell you he’s sorry.

**JIM**  
We’re here to say *we are.*

*Beat. The room goes still.*

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – BALTIMORE – 6:29 P.M.**

**Jeff’s wife** stands by the bed, one hand on his wrist, eyes narrowed like she's waiting for someone to say the wrong thing.

**Jeremy** lingers just a little too long near the foot of the bed, then clears his throat.

**JEREMY** (low)  
I'm gonna… give you all a minute.

(beat)
Call me if—when—he wakes up.

He walks out fast, **not waiting** for permission or thanks.  Because he knows **what’s coming**.  **Silence.**  **Tension.**  **Then—****Jeff’s wife turns slowly to face Kathy.**

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
So.  Still can’t stay away from him, can you?

**KATHY** (flat, unmoved)  
I’m here because he’s in a hospital bed.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
You’re here because you’ve never known when to *back off.*

**BILL** (half-standing)  
Hey, maybe this isn’t the—

**KATHY** (cutting him off, eyes locked on her)  
Let her go.  She flew here.  She’s pissed.  I can take it.

**JEFF’S WIFE** (smiling bitterly)  
Oh, I know you can.  You’ve been “taking it” for years, right?  Nudging your way in, acting like you were *special*, like you knew the *real* him.

**KATHY**  
I do know the real him.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
Do you?  You lost your key.  The real Jeff married *me*.  The real Jeff picked *this*.  **Us.**  Not the tour bus version.  Not the midnight hotel room version.  Not the **used-to-be magic** that you keep dragging around like it still fits.

*The room is frozen.*  **Jim** shifts but doesn’t speak.  **Gilley** looks like he wants to crawl into the mini-fridge.  **Cremeans** just lowers his head and pretends he’s somewhere else.

**KATHY** (cold now)  
You think you’re winning?  You think you’re the prize?  He’s lying there with a broken brain, and you’re keeping score?

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
I’ve always kept score.  Because *I’m the one who’s still here when he falls apart.*  And I didn't get to *pretend it was all poetry.*

**KATHY**  
And I didn’t get to pretend it was all *marriage counseling and paperwork*.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
You want to be the tragic muse?  Be my guest.  But don’t forget—You’re not the one in the will.

*Boom.*  *Silence.*  Even the monitor seems to beep more slowly.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 6:34 P.M.**

**Jeff’s wife** just dropped the line: *“You’re not the one in the will.”*

The air is thick. **Toxic.**  The band is paralyzed.  **Kathy’s jaw clenches**. Her fingers twitch on the neck of the guitar she forgot she was still holding.  She’s about to say something *that cannot be unsaid*—When **Cremeans steps in. Hard.**

**CREMEANS** (enough)  
*That’s it.*

He strides over, grabs Kathy firmly by the elbow—**not rough, but without room for negotiation**.

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**  
Out.  Now.

**KATHY** (creaking rage under her voice)  
She started it.

**CREMEANS**  
And you're about to finish it—**on top of Jeff's chest**.  We're not doing this here.

*Kathy doesn’t move.*  For a second, it’s like she’s going to fight him, physically or verbally.  But then—**She breaks. Just a little.**She looks at **Jeff**.  Still motionless.  Still unaware.  And she lets herself be **frog-marched out**, biting her tongue like it’s bleeding.

As the door clicks behind them, **Cremeans turns back**, pointing across the room like a field commander.

**CREMEANS (to Gilley)**  
*You take care of your brother.*

**GILLEY** (nods, suddenly very quiet)  
Yes, sir.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  (not looking at anyone)  
That should’ve happened an hour ago.

*The room deflates.*  Gilley moves to Jeff’s side.  Cremeans disappears down the hall with Kathy.  And for the first time in hours—There’s **stillness**.  But not peace.  Just a little **space** for someone to start coming back.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL CAFETERIA – 6:46 P.M.**

The cafeteria is mostly empty—just the glow of vending machines, stale coffee, and old linoleum.  
**Cremeans** and **Kathy** sit across from each other at a corner table, both with untouched drinks.

The silence is finally *comfortable* enough to speak.

**CREMEANS** (quiet, not judging)  
How close were you to committing **assault** in that room?

**KATHY** (sips her coffee, deadpan)  
Within **five seconds**.

(beat)
Three, if she'd *smirked*.

**CREMEANS** (nods, thoughtful)
That’s because you’re still in **love** with him.  Or you still **care** about him.  Or you’re still **having sex** with him.

(leans forward)
Or… *explain yourself.*

**KATHY** (leans back, tired but sharp)  
It’s not any of that.  Or it is, in ways that don’t fit your little tour ledger.

**CREMEANS**  
Try me.

**KATHY**  
He’s the only guy on earth who can make me feel like the **smartest woman alive**—And then an **absolute amateur** the moment we start **writing**.

**CREMEANS** (cocks his head)  
You mean musically?

**KATHY**  
I mean *in every way.*  That guy can lay out a chord progression or a lyric line that makes me want to quit and also record an entire concept album that night.  And I’m **pretty goddamn good** at writing.

**CREMEANS** (sits back)  
I’m quite sure you are.  Because all you guys have **gigantic houses**, **fat bank accounts**, and **gold records** on your walls.  And now your *partner* is sedated in a **fucking hotel room with an IV** in Baltimore.

**KATHY** (smiling slowly, nodding)  
You just used an **F-bomb**.

**CREMEANS** (stares into his coffee)  
That’s my **F-bomb** for the year.

(beat)
Used it wisely.

*Silence again. But this one’s not cold.*
