This is the silence of **two people who understand weight**.  And for once, neither is trying to win.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 8:45 P.M.**

**Jeff blinks awake**. His brain still rebooting. His voice is raspy but **cheerful**—*eerily so, considering the IV in his arm and wires on his chest.*

**JEFF** (grinning)  
…Well that was a hell of a nap.

He turns his head— And there’s **Gilley**, perched in a chair far too close, still in his half-buttoned robe like a human fever dream.

**GILLEY**  
Look who finally decided to join the conscious.

**JEFF** (deep exhale)  
How bad is it?

**GILLEY**  
Define “bad.”  You're in Baltimore.  You missed two days.  Everyone thinks you're dying.  And Kathy almost threw down fists at your wife.

Jeff turns his head.  **And there she is.**  **His wife.**  Tense. Sleep-deprived. Arms crossed.  Still in her travel clothes, makeup worn off, but her posture is **bulletproof**.

**JEFF** (softly)  
Hey.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  (slightly too even)  
Hey yourself.

**JEFF**  
You, uh… get in today?

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
Three hours ago.  No thanks to your tour manager booking me the middle seat between two drunk dentists.

**JEFF** (chuckles weakly)  
So… what’d I miss?

**GILLEY**  
Well, nobody’s dead.  But we’re working on it.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
Your band has been pacing this hospital like ghosts with instruments.  Kathy nearly got kicked out.  Jeremy’s been circling the parking lot like it owes him a free BMW.  Jim looks like he aged ten years.  And Bill’s been trying to compose your eulogy on a napkin.

**JEFF**  
Wow.

(small grin)
I’m flattered.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
Don’t be.  They're not worried because you're you.  They're worried because you're the part of this machine they thought could *never break*.

**JEFF** (quietly)  
Maybe I did.

**GILLEY**  
You're just… rebooting.  We’ll run diagnostics later.

**JEFF’S WIFE** (soft, honest)  
You scared the shit out of me.

**JEFF**  
I scared the shit out of myself.

*Beat. Then, of course—*

**JEFF**  
So no one brought barbecue?

**GILLEY** (lying instantly, confidently)  
There’s some left.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 8:53 P.M.**

**Jeff’s** sitting up slightly now, rubbing his eyes with one hand, IV tube dangling like a lazy spider. His wife sits nearby.  **Gilley** is still hovering, somehow *both guilty and proud*.  Jeff groans and shifts, face scrunching with the **raw logic of post-sedation hunger.**

**JEFF**  
Okay.  Here’s what I remember: I had **one bag of Fritos**.  And a bottle of **Mountain Dew**.  And it cost me…  

(beat)  
**Five hundred bucks.**

**GILLEY**  
Technically, it was a *donation*.

**JEFF** (squinting at him)  
That jockstrap better be *gold-threaded*, my guy.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
He’s talking. That’s either a good sign or a warning.

**JEFF**  
So listen—**for the love of Christ**, can somebody **get me something to eat**?  Like something that doesn’t taste like it’s been filtered through a **hotel lobby carpet**?

**GILLEY**  
I mean… they’ve got pudding.

**JEFF**  
No.  I want **Chinese food**.  Like, **real** food.  Not some six-dollar steamed tragedy.

(beat)
**Beef and broccoli.**  Hot. Salty. Greasy. That’s it.  *Beef and broccoli.*  It’ll be **eight bucks**.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
You want fortune cookies too, or is that a second mortgage?

**JEFF**  
I’ve been **unconscious for days**.  I deserve fortune cookies **and** a goddamn lantern parade.

**GILLEY** (turning to the door)  
Say less.  I’m finding a place that delivers.  Or I’m **liberating** one.

**JEFF**  
Tell ‘em to drown it in sauce.  Tell ‘em it’s for a man who’s seen the other side.

*As Gilley hustles off with purpose, the hospital room feels lighter—not healed, not fixed—but **recognizably alive again.***

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL – CAFETERIA EXIT / PARKING LOT – 9:03 P.M.**

**Kathy** is just tossing her empty coffee cup into the trash when **Gilley appears**, breathless and shining with purpose.  He **grabs her arm gently but with zero time for consent**.

**GILLEY**  
Let’s go.  We’re going on a **road trip**.

**KATHY** (eyebrow cocked)  
Where are we going?

**GILLEY**  
We’re getting **Chinese food**.  At **nine o’clock**.  In a **strange city**.  And it’s going to work out **gloriously well.**

**KATHY** (flat)  
Is this because of that entire *Brotherhood* thing?

**GILLEY** (stops walking, gets weirdly sincere)  
Kathy—This man once helped me when I couldn’t **see**.  Like, literally.  I had this **eye condition**, right?  I was **blind**. Blinded by the light.  They gave me these *brutal* eye drops.  I couldn’t take **any light at all**. Like—not a lamp, not a nightlight, not even the microwave clock.  So I locked myself in a **closet**.

**KATHY**  
…Jesus.

**GILLEY**  
And you know what Jeff did?  He **came over that afternoon**, didn’t even knock.  Just opened the closet door.  Sat **in there** with me. In the dark.  For **three hours**.

**KATHY** (quiet now)  
Just… sat?

**GILLEY**  
Didn’t say much.  Didn’t make it weird.  Just… kept me company.  So yeah—I owe him.  Like, **speedrunning for Chinese food in Baltimore** kind of owe him.

**KATHY** (sighs)  
Okay.  But if this turns into *“Lost in Chinatown with the Synth Messiah,”* I’m calling a cab and leaving you.

**GILLEY**  
That’s fair.   But for the record—You’ll never find a better **egg roll sidekick** than me.

*They step out into the humid Baltimore night, headlights sliding past as they head toward whatever hole-in-the-wall paradise fate delivers.*Because **Jeff asked**, and **Gilley delivers**.

---

## **EXT. CHINESE TAKEOUT WINDOW – JUST DOWN THE STREET – 9:17 P.M.**

The place is **tiny**, neon-lit, and **just barely functioning**, but it’s open.  A faded menu. Bulletproof glass.  One guy at the wok, flipping beef like it is a lifeboat from the Lusitania.  There’s a **sign** taped to the counter that reads:  **“We deliver to Mercy Hospital. Extra duck sauce 25¢.”**

**Kathy** leans against the wall, arms crossed.  **Gilley** is sitting on a cracked plastic bench, tapping his foot with nervous energy.

**GILLEY** (staring through the window)  
You know, thank **God** this place exists.  I don’t think I could emotionally survive **9 p.m. Wendy’s**.

**KATHY** (flat)  
That’s not food.  That’s punishment with ranch dressing.

*They both watch as the cook dumps bright green broccoli into the sizzling wok.*  *The sound is **sharp and alive**, like something **real** is happening.*

**GILLEY** (still watching the cook, then quietly)  
Hey—What does **Jeff** actually mean to you?

*Kathy doesn't answer right away.*

**KATHY**  
You really asking?  Or are you just trying to pass the time until egg rolls?

**GILLEY**  
No, I’m asking.  Like, really asking.  You’ve been half-in, half-out with him for years.  Tour buses. Backstage. Writing sessions. That weird trip to Copenhagen.  So what is it?  Love? Habit? Nostalgia?

*Kathy exhales slowly, her eyes on the steam rising inside the takeout window.*

**KATHY**  
Jeff is the only man I’ve ever met—Who could make me feel like the **smartest woman in the room**—And then **completely annihilate me** with a chord change.

**GILLEY**  
That tracks.

**KATHY**  
He's infuriating.  He’s unreachable.  And sometimes I think he **enjoys** being misunderstood.  But when we write?  When we’re in that moment?  He gets me.  *Fully.*  No filters. No armor.  Just… truth.

**GILLEY**  
Yeah.  That’s what he does.

*The cook yells something unintelligible and slaps a bag on the counter.*  *It steams slightly, filled with **beef, broccoli, white rice, and something still hissing.***

**KATHY** (grabbing the bag)  
Let’s go feed your brother.

**GILLEY**  (smirking)  
Let’s go feed **your heartbreak**.

**KATHY**  
Or I’ll feed you this bag through your **nose**.

*They push out into the warm Baltimore night, quiet now, each holding something heavier than the food.*  Because they’re not just carrying dinner—they’re carrying **years** of silence, love, regret, and the chance—**maybe**—to say it all **before it’s too late.**

---

## **EXT. SIDEWALK – RETURNING TO HOSPITAL – 9:24 P.M.**

The **city hums low** around them.  Plastic takeout bag rustling between them.  Steam rising from the container.  The scent of beef and soy sauce clinging to the night.  **Gilley’s robe is flapping slightly as he walks too fast for comfort.**  **Kathy** is in step, quiet, carrying the rice.  And then—

**GILLEY** (flat, cutting)  
I am *confident*—That that **little fat fuck** enjoys being **misunderstood**. Or **underestimated**.

**KATHY** (glancing at him)  
Jesus, Gilley.

**GILLEY**  
No—**really**. I think he likes it.  I think he **feeds on it**.  Like some sort of mumbling **troll wizard** who *pretends* to be confused by the world just so no one sees the **blade he’s holding under the table**.

**KATHY**  
Yeah.  That sounds… familiar.

**GILLEY**  
It’s a **defense mechanism**.  Let people think you’re off. Or slow. Or burnt out.  Then they can’t see what’s actually going on.

(beat)
And half the time?  I don’t even know if he **likes** people.

**KATHY** (slow, honest)  
You mean like… us?  Or *people* people?

**GILLEY**  
Both.  Because, like—He **performs intimacy**.  He knows *exactly* what to say when it’s lyrics, or when you’re crying, or when someone needs a perfect three-note answer.  But I’ve never seen him hang out at a party longer than it took to grab a drink and disappear.  I've never seen him **open up** unless there was a pen in his hand or a mic in front of his mouth.

**KATHY** (quiet)  
Yeah.  He gives you everything…Except **himself**.

**GILLEY**  
So I’m asking.  Honestly.  Do you think he **even likes people?**

**KATHY** (stops walking, thinks)
I think he loves people.  But I think it **hurts him** to be around them.

**GILLEY**  
Why?

**KATHY**  
Because he feels **everything** too much.  He’s **porous**, Gilley.  Every room he walks into, he’s picking up **signals**, **energy**, **pain**, **bullshit**, and it gets in *him*.  So yeah, he hides.  He cloaks it in weirdness and sarcasm and muttering into a sandwich.  But that doesn’t mean he doesn’t **care**. It means he’s trying not to **drown.**

**GILLEY** (grudgingly, with a nod)  
Okay.  That’s fair.  Still—I’m putting on the record that I *love* the guy. But he’s a **greasy little wizard** who manipulates perception better than a Vegas magician with a coke problem.

**KATHY** (grinning, softly)  
God, I’ve missed talking like this with you.

**GILLEY**  
Me too.  Now shut up before the food gets cold.

*They turn the corner and the hospital glows ahead.*  *Jeff is waiting.*  *So is the rest of the truth.*

---

## **EXT. HOSPITAL PARKING LOT – 9:31 P.M.**

The glow of the ER sign bounces off the concrete.  The city’s slowing down.  Kathy and Gilley walk the last 50 feet back to the entrance, plastic bags of Chinese food steaming in their hands.

They’ve just had one of their **most honest conversations in years**.  So naturally, Gilley can’t help himself.

**GILLEY**  (half-grin, not looking at her)  
So…Just to clarify—Does this mean you want to **jump into bed** with me?  Not **today**, not **tonight**, not **this week**, or even **this year**…But like—**Eventually**?  Do I have a **shot**?

**KATHY** (glancing sideways, not amused)  
Seriously?

**GILLEY**  
I’m just **spot-checking** the vibe.

**KATHY** (stops walking, considers)
No, Gilley.  I left that in our **past**.  And that’s exactly where I like it.  We told way too many lies for way too long and quitting was cathartic.

(beat)
You’re a lot.  I know it’s an **act**, most of the time—But you’re the **best actor** I’ve ever met.  *Seriously.*

**GILLEY** (chuckles, a little too quickly)  
Hey, I *was* almost cast as “Man With Blender” in a shampoo commercial once.

**KATHY**  
And that’s the problem.  I *see you*, but I don’t always want to **fight the performance** to get to the man.

**GILLEY** (grinning through it)  
Well…Ever since I got myself a **crash pad in Hollywood**, life’s been **real good**.  *If you know what I mean.*

**KATHY**  
I don’t.  But I’m gonna assume it involves a hot tub, terrible decisions, and a karaoke mic you don’t deserve.

**GILLEY**  
You know me so well.

**KATHY**  
That’s what terrifies me.

*They step up to the hospital entrance.*  *The sliding doors hiss open.*  *Inside, Jeff waits—hungry, recovering, surrounded by old wounds and people trying to patch them.*

And this?  This was the closest Gilley will get to closure tonight.

---

## **EXT. HOSPITAL ENTRANCE – 9:34 P.M.**

The hospital’s automatic doors are just a few steps ahead.  Gilley and Kathy walk slower now, the Chinese food growing heavier in their hands—**or maybe that’s just the weight of the moment.**  The streetlight buzzes above them.  Quiet hum of a late Baltimore night.  Then Gilley glances sideways, and in that weird vulnerable-wrapped-in-swagger tone of his—

**GILLEY**  
You know—I’m **quite familiar** with how much you **run around**.

**KATHY** (cocks an eyebrow)  
You calling me a floater?

**GILLEY**  
I’m calling you **free-range**.  And look, if I’m ever somewhere else—*On tour*, in Japan, dead, whatever—You could always use my **crash pad**.

**KATHY** (flat)  
In Hollywood?

**GILLEY**  
Yep.  You could, you know—**sample somebody** in town.  No one’s gonna know.

**KATHY** (stares at him, a beat)
You offering me a **fuck-safehouse**, Gilley?

**GILLEY** (pause, then)
More like a **truce zone**.  No expectations.  No strings.  Just a place you don’t have to explain yourself.

*Kathy looks away. She doesn’t laugh. She doesn’t scold.*  She just **sighs**—deep, long, conflicted.

**KATHY**  
That’s the saddest nice thing you’ve ever said to me.

**GILLEY**  
That’s my brand, baby.

*They step into the hospital, Chinese food steaming through the bag, walking back into the reality that **someone else’s life just rebooted** while theirs was still mid-download.*

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 9:52 P.M.**

Jeff sits propped up in bed, **wolfing down beef and broccoli** like a man who’s just returned from a famine.  Chopsticks in hand, IV still taped to his wrist.  Grease on his lips, soy sauce on the napkin.

**JEFF** (mouth full)  
God, I forgot how good **cheap beef** is. Tell me this does not have MSG. Please.

**JEFF’S WIFE** (flat, still seated by the bed)  
Probably the only drug they haven’t tested you for.

**GILLEY** (quiet, edging toward the door)  
Kathy brought it.

**JEFF’S WIFE** (stern, without looking)  
She can go.

*The room shifts. Kathy doesn’t argue. She just nods, tosses a glance at Jeff—who doesn’t meet her eyes—and slips out.*

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL HALLWAY – MOMENTS LATER**

Kathy leans against the cold wall, arms crossed, food bag still in hand.

**Cremeans** approaches, clipboard under arm, tension living permanently in his spine.

**KATHY** (sighs)  
How are we doing?  Do we know anything?

**CREMEANS** (muttering)  
We know… **"it’s probably not that."**  Whatever *that* was.

**KATHY**  
So no answers?

**CREMEANS**  
They’re calling for a **CT scan**.

**KATHY**  
MRI didn’t show anything?

**CREMEANS**  
Nothing specific.  Nothing actionable.  Nothing at all.  They’re using phrases like **“within normal limits”** and **“non-localizing.”**

**KATHY**  
Ugh. The medical version of “it’s not you, it’s me.”

**CREMEANS**  
Right now they’re leaning toward **hypotension**.  Possibly **vasovagal syncope**.

**KATHY**  
Which means?

**CREMEANS**  
Which means…Maybe his **blood pressure crashed**.  And he passed out.  Hard.  He thought it was a **migraine**—Because it felt like one.  Sound sensitivity, light aversion, nausea, the whole thing.

**KATHY**  
And that’s what happened at M&T?

**CREMEANS**  
That’s the leading theory.  Vasovagal episode triggered by… what?  Stress?  Overexertion?  
Standing under lights in front of sixty thousand people and forgetting to breathe?  Take your pick.

**KATHY** (quiet, hands in her jacket pockets)  
You think he’s broken?

**CREMEANS** (shrugs)  
I think he’s **tired**.  And I think we’re all just now realizing how long he’s been *keeping the rest of us running* while **falling apart inside**.

*Kathy stares ahead for a long moment, the hum of distant machines behind them.*

**KATHY**  
How long until the CT?

**CREMEANS**  
They’re prepping now.  He’s not gonna love it.

**KATHY**  
He’s never loved anything that didn’t come with a bridge pickup and a distortion pedal.

**CREMEANS**  
Fair.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL HALLWAY – OUTSIDE CT PREP ROOM – 9:56 P.M.**

**Cremeans** flips through a folder, phone clipped to his belt.  He looks like he’s aged ten years since the Baltimore drive.  **Kathy**, arms crossed, leans against the wall, eyes sharp but tired.  She glances down the hallway where nurses are readying Jeff for his CT.

**KATHY**  
Have you figured it out yet?

**CREMEANS**  
What?

**KATHY**  
Have they told you how long this takes to **treat**?  How long until he’s back on his **feet**, back on a **stage**?

**CREMEANS**  
Kathy—

**KATHY**  
No, I’m serious.  I want to know if the **arena leg** is in **jeopardy**.

**CREMEANS** (sighs)  
We don’t know yet.

**KATHY**  
Because we’re supposed to start **right after Thanksgiving**.  And that’s—

(does the math)
—*eight weeks*.

**CREMEANS**  
I know.

**KATHY** (slowly, like peeling a bandage)  
You’re telling me there’s a chance we might have to **cancel** the entire second leg?

**CREMEANS**  
Not cancel.  But **postpone**?  **Yes.**  If this is something **neurological**, or if his **blood pressure’s still unstable**, or if he needs **ongoing monitoring**—There’s no way we’re putting him on a **six-week, multi-arena, city-a-night schedule** without clearance.

**KATHY** (flat)  
So everything we’ve built up for the last three years is on the line because we didn’t notice the guy holding the bass was *on fire* the whole time.

**CREMEANS** (slow nod)  
That’s about the size of it.

**KATHY**  
Jesus Christ.

*They fall into silence for a beat. Footsteps echo down the hallway. A nurse wheels an empty bed past.*

**KATHY (CONT’D)**  
So what do we do if he can’t play?

**CREMEANS**  
You don’t want the real answer.

**KATHY**  
Try me.

**CREMEANS**  
You either reschedule the tour…Or you put someone else in his spot.

*Kathy stares at him like he just suggested **burning the Declaration of Independence**.*

**KATHY**  
That’s not a spot.  That’s **Jeff.**

**CREMEANS**  
Then we wait.  And we plan nothing until the **scan is read**, the **doctor signs off**, and Jeff himself says, *"Yeah, I can do this again."*

**KATHY** (sighs, looking down the hallway again)  
God, I hope he says yes.

*But what she doesn’t say—what she doesn’t even want to think yet—is:*  **What if he doesn’t?**

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL HALLWAY – OUTSIDE CT SCAN ROOM – 10:02 P.M.**

**Kathy** paces in a small circle, hands in fists.  **Cremeans** leans against the wall, flipping through pages on his clipboard.  The nurses behind the door are prepping **Jeff** for his scan.  Kathy stops pacing.

**KATHY**  
We’re going to have another **band meeting** in a few minutes.

You’re **not invited**.

**CREMEANS**  
I’m not even offended anymore.

**KATHY**  
Good.  Because I’m going to **kill** anyone who votes against my motion.

**CREMEANS**  
Which is?

**KATHY**  
We’re postponing the **arena leg**.

**CREMEANS** (sighs)  
Kathy—
**KATHY**  
Until **2001.**  If he’s okay, we’ll pick up again.  But we’re not pretending this is fine.  We’re not racing into pyrotechnics and blackout dates with a guy who just **blacked out** in front of 60,000 people.

**CREMEANS** (quietly)  
Okay.

**KATHY** (squaring up)  
So you’re going to tell me: What’s the **first date** after New Year’s?  And **where** is it?  Is it in the **South**?

*Cremeans flips through his master sheet, fingers scanning with practiced speed.*

**CREMEANS**  
First confirmed date after the new year—January 4, 2001.

**KATHY**  
Where?

**CREMEANS**  
**Atlanta.**  Phillips Arena.  18,000 seats.

**KATHY**  
Perfect.

**CREMEANS**  
Why?

**KATHY**  
Because if we’re going to come back…We’re coming back **loud**, and we’re coming back **someplace warm**.

*Beat. The scanner door opens behind them. The nurse gives a nod—Jeff’s scan is underway.*

**KATHY (CONT’D)**  
Tell the label.  Tell the venues.  Tell the fans.  We’re not **canceling**.  We’re **deferring**.  
*Because when we come back… we’re not limping.*  We’re going to **burn the South down.**

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL HALLWAY – 10:08 P.M.**

Kathy stands with her arms crossed, watching through the glass as the CT machine whirs to life.  
**Jeff** lies still inside, ghostlike under the pale blue lights.  **Cremeans** is beside her, checking his pager (yes, it’s 2000), scrolling through a paper printout of media tracking and venue correspondence.

Kathy exhales sharply.

**KATHY**  
Okay.  So I’ve been **living in a bubble**, obsessing over **Jeff**, and **barbecue**, and **rehearsal flashbacks**, and **stolen guitars** and *every possible version of emotional damage*…

(beat)
How’s the **rest of the planet** taking this shit?

**CREMEANS** (flat)  
Which part?  The **collapse**?  The **hospitalization**?  The **rumors**?  Or the fact that the band may be **postponing the second leg of the biggest tour of the year**?

**KATHY**  
Any and all.  Give me the oxygen-mask version.

**CREMEANS** (sighs, flips the page)  
Okay—

MTV News ran a **three-minute segment**.  Kurt Loder looks like someone **killed his dog** and told him *69 Reasons* was about to be pulled from shelves. Spin did a **semi-thoughtful** piece—called Jeff’s collapse “a tragic yet inevitable moment for a band built on emotional dissonance and delayed catharsis.”

**KATHY**  
That's so on-brand it makes me want to vomit.

**CREMEANS**  
Rolling Stone hasn’t run a feature yet, but their insider page says we’re in “an unconfirmed medical hold.”  Ticketmaster has frozen all ticket sales past Thanksgiving.

**KATHY**  
And the fans?

**CREMEANS**  
Half are **freaking out**.  Half are already speculating on AOL it’s a **marketing stunt**.  The rest are writing **thinkpieces** about the fragility of art in the shadow of capitalism.  

**KATHY**  
Jesus.

**CREMEANS**  
Your fan forum has a **37-page thread** titled *“Did Kathy Predict This in the Bridge of ‘Sin, West of Eden’?”*

**KATHY** (slow grin)  
That’s honestly amazing.

**CREMEANS**  
One guy mapped out your entire discography and cross-referenced it with Jeff’s **live performance decline curve** like a psychotic economist.

**KATHY**  
Okay. That part’s terrifying.

**CREMEANS**  
The world’s watching.  They’re **speculating**.  They’re **waiting**.  And they want a **narrative**.

**KATHY** (sighs, rubbing her eyes)  
They want a comeback arc.

**CREMEANS**  
Or a **funeral**.

*Kathy looks back toward the scan room, where Jeff lies still inside the glowing cylinder.*

**KATHY**  
Let’s give them something **they’re not ready for**.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL HALLWAY – NEAR MEDIA ROOM / PHONE BANK – 10:14 P.M.**

**Kathy and Cremeans** walk slowly past a few vending machines, the soft hum of soda compressors sounding like a war drum.  Kathy’s on edge. Controlled, but sharp.

**KATHY**  
I’m going to ask the boys to sit down and figure out what we want the **media strategy** to be.

**CREMEANS** (mutters)  
Let me guess.  You’re leaning toward a **total blackout**?

**KATHY** (flat)  
Yes.  No statements.  No rumors confirmed.  No interviews.  Just **nothing**.

**CREMEANS**  
Kendall's gonna tell you that’s probably the **stupidest thing** you could do right now.

**KATHY** (smiling faintly)  
Yep.  I **believe her**.  Which is why…

(beat)
We’re going to **tread cautiously**.

**CREMEANS**  
Kathy, in the absence of a narrative, the world builds one **for you**.  And it’s never the one you want.

**KATHY**  
Which is why we’re not giving them silence.  We’re giving them **controlled static**.

**CREMEANS**  
You're going to leak your own fog machine?

**KATHY**  
Something like that.  Kendall will help me write the *non-answers*.  The *almost-truths*.  We stay in control by **never pretending** to be in control.

**CREMEANS** (slowly nods)  
That I can work with.

**KATHY**  
And when Jeff’s ready?  We let him speak.  But only **then**.

**CREMEANS**  
And if he’s not?

**KATHY**  
Then we do what we’ve always done.  We make something beautiful **out of the wreckage**.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 10:17 P.M.**

Jeff, finished eating, is sitting up, more awake now, energized by MSG and confusion.  A nurse enters, clipboard in hand.

**NURSE**  
Mr. Evans? We’re going to take you down for your CT scan now.

**JEFF** (staring)  
You want to do *what*…to do *what*…and **what**?

**NURSE**  
Just a CT scan. Should only take a few minutes.

**JEFF** (raising a finger)  
Hold on.  How does a **CT scan** work?  Because I just woke up from *chemical napland*, and now you're telling me we're about to play **“Guess That Brain Mass”** with *x-rays*?

**NURSE** (laughing gently)  
It’s basically a 3D x-ray.  The scanner rotates around you.  We get detailed images of your brain.  No pain, no needles, no noise like an MRI.  You just lie still.

**JEFF**  
So you’re saying you spin a camera around my **skull**, slice it into **digital pancakes**, and nobody finds that weird?

**NURSE**  
I mean… it’s *less* weird than some of your album art.

**JEFF** (low, muttering)  
Okay but what if I twitch and you catch the wrong angle and it looks like my brain’s trying to **leave my head**?

**NURSE**  
That’s what the technician’s for.  They catch those things.  You’ll be fine.

**JEFF** (pause)
How long does it take?

**NURSE**  
Ten minutes.  Unless you fall asleep, in which case we gently shake you and hope for the best.

**JEFF**  
Can I hum?

**NURSE**  
No.

**JEFF**  
Can I blink Morse code messages in case I get abducted during the scan?

**NURSE**  
Sir, are you this difficult on stage?

**GILLEY** (from the chair, flipping a magazine)  
Worse.

**JEFF**  
Fine. Let’s go take pictures of my **weird-ass brain**.  But if anything in there is glowing, I want royalties.

*They wheel him out, his voice echoing down the hall with low-volume commentary on conspiracy theories and gamma radiation.*

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – POST-JEFF DEPARTURE – 10:21 P.M.**

**Jeff’s been wheeled off for his CT scan**, still rambling about "radiation patents" and "subdermal bass frequencies."  **His wife**, now seated again, crosses her legs and watches the empty doorway with a small, **genuine smile**.  **Gilley**, lounging in the corner like a half-unwrapped present, glances at her sideways.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  (murmuring)  
God, I love this part.

**GILLEY**  
What part?

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
When he starts **free-associating like a motherfucker**.  It’s like watching his brain try to **improvise jazz without an instrument**.

**GILLEY** (smirking)  
That’s why you two get along so well?

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
Exactly.

**GILLEY**  
Then let me ask you something real, since we’re being *intimate*, **How well do you suck dick?**

*A beat.*

She turns slowly. Doesn't blink.

**JEFF’S WIFE** (icy)  
**Har har. Very funny.**

(beat)
You realize, Gilley—Jeff has been **warning me for more than four years** that you **want in my pants**.

**GILLEY**  
Guilty. Mildly.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
Which is why I’m **not going to talk to you.**

(leans forward slightly)
And if you keep being a **son of a bitch**, I’ll **throw you out**, and you can go deal with **Kathy S. Bitch** instead.

**GILLEY**  (tosses up his hands, mock-surrender)  
Whoa. *Ma’am has range.*

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
I have a very short fuse and a very long memory.  Do not make me use either tonight.

*A tense pause—and then she goes back to her magazine like nothing happened.* Gilley exhales slowly and mutters under his breath:

**GILLEY**  
Jesus. You’re terrifying.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
That’s why he married me.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL – VENDING MACHINE ALCOVE – 10:29 P.M.**

**Kathy** is leaned against the far wall, holding a Sprite, not drinking it.  Her eyes are on nothing.  Just the flicker of fluorescent lights and her own scrambled thoughts.  **Gilley** walks up slowly, rubbing the back of his neck.

**GILLEY**  
Hey.

**KATHY**  
Still in one piece?

**GILLEY**  
Barely.  She verbally castrated me, but it was surgical.

**KATHY** (mild smirk)  
She’s got a gift.

**GILLEY**  
Yeah.  Speaking of which—

(beat)
Do you know what **Mrs. Evans** calls you?

**KATHY** (slow turn, raised eyebrow)  
What, to my **face** or behind my **back**?

**GILLEY**  
Behind.  Definitely behind.

**KATHY**  
No.  But I assume it starts with a “B” and ends with something printable.

**GILLEY** (small laugh)  
Close.  You’re **Kathy S. Bitch**.  Like it’s a full name.  Middle initial and everything.

**KATHY** (flat)  
Wow.  I sound like a Bond villain with a vendetta against romance.

**GILLEY**  
I mean, it’s not… *entirely inaccurate.*

**KATHY**  
Yeah?  Well maybe if I had a husband who’d spent two years emotionally unraveling in headphones, I’d need someone to project my fury onto too.

**GILLEY** (sincere, a little quieter)  
She sees you as the version of Jeff that she **can’t compete with**.

**KATHY**  
That’s not my fault.

**GILLEY**  
Didn’t say it was.  But it’s why she’s never gonna like you.

**KATHY** (sipping the Sprite finally)  
Doesn’t bother me.  I’m not here for **her**.

**GILLEY**  
Who *are* you here for?


**KATHY**  
Mmhm...

(beat)
Jeff.  Same as you.  Even if we show it differently.


*A long pause as the machines hum.*

**GILLEY**  
Can I still call you Kathy S. Bitch when I’m drunk?

**KATHY**  
Only if you want to wake up with a drumstick in your eye.

**GILLEY** (sighs)  
You're so hard to love.

**KATHY**  
That’s why no one ever does it halfway.

*They sit together in the soft glow of vending machines and unresolved history.*

---

## **INT. RADIOLOGY – CT SCAN ROOM – 10:34 P.M.**

The room is dim, quiet, too clean.  The giant **donut-shaped scanner** hums gently in standby.  **Jeff** is wheeled in on a gurney. He’s got a hospital gown on, a lead apron across his hips, and **several lingering questions**.  The radiology tech moves to position his head.

**JEFF**  
Hey, quick one.  Do I have to be, like, **really still** for this?

**TECH**  
Yeah. Super still.  Like “sleeping statue” still.

**JEFF**  
Okay. Because I’m kind of in a weird headspace where my legs want to dance but my soul wants to float.

**TECH** (half-smile)  
Then your **soul** needs to chill.

*Jeff lies back, arms stiff at his sides, staring up into the mechanical halo.*

Then—

**JEFF**  
So…**What’s the difference** between a **CAT scan** and a **CT scan**?  Or is it just that someone **left the A out**?

**TECH** (laughs softly)  
Same thing.  CAT scan = CT scan.  “CAT” stands for **Computed Axial Tomography**.  They just dropped the “A” because apparently **we like things shorter now**.

**JEFF**  
So it’s the same machine?

**TECH**  
Exactly the same. Just a different **acronym mood**.

**JEFF**  
Wow.  Somewhere there’s a guy with a degree who probably *lost his shit* over the **axial betrayal**.

**TECH**  
Probably.

**JEFF** (pause)  
Is it gonna find anything?

**TECH**  
That’s what it’s built for.  Now hold still, Mr. Evans.

**JEFF**  
Right.  Silent jazz mode.

*The scanner begins to rotate, the soft whirring starting as Jeff closes his eyes—his body still, but his mind still asking questions no one’s answered yet.*

---

## **INT. CT SCANNER – 10:38 P.M. – JEFF’S BRAIN, UNFILTERED**

**Stillness.**  

White lights.  Rotating rings.  And the unmistakable sound of **Jeff’s internal thought hurricane**.

**JEFF (INTERNAL)**  
Okay, be still.  Still.  Still like Napoleon’s **alt-card**, the secret one. The imperial reserve.  Destroyed in what—**1815? 1816?**  Anyway, it was France’s last chance to hold the economic flank before the British hammered the franc into oblivion.  And what did that do?  It *directly impacted* **Albanian foreign relations**, obviously.  Because once you lose the anchor currency, Balkan power dynamics—

*The machine hums around him.*

**JEFF (INTERNAL)**  
And now Albania wants in on **NATO**.  So does **Poland**.  They’re sniffing around the edges, waiting for the old Cold War ghosts to die or at least retire to a dacha.  But is **NATO even fit for purpose** anymore?  Twenty-first-century warfare isn’t tanks, it’s **telecom and memes**.  And by God, we’re **three months away** from the actual **twenty-first century**.

*A beep. Shift in table movement. Jeff stays perfectly still. His mind does not.*

**JEFF (INTERNAL)**  
Also, didn’t we all just **live through Y2K**?  Wasn’t that a big thing?  Everyone hoarding water and resetting clocks and predicting **airplanes were going to fall out of the sky**?  And then?  Nothing.  Just… **January 1st.**  No blinking red lights. No servers bursting into flame. Just hangovers and passive-aggressive tech guys claiming they “saved the world.”

*Another beep. Jeff stares into the void of the ceiling plate.*

**JEFF (INTERNAL)**  
Y2K was a metaphor.  Like Napoleon’s alt-card.  Everyone thought it was going to be a **disaster**, but it turns out we’re just all **tired**.  Tired of building things to break.  Tired of pretending **we’re not breaking too**.

*Another beep. Final pass. Silence.*

**JEFF (INTERNAL)**  
Also I still don’t believe Poland’s not already in NATO.

*The scanner powers down.*

**TECH**  
Okay, Mr. Evans. You did great.  Just stay there—we’re bringing the bed out.

**JEFF** (polite, cheery)  
Thanks! By the way, do you know if NATO’s running updates this fiscal quarter?

**TECH** (pause)  
…Sir?

**JEFF**  
Never mind. I’ll write them a letter.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 10:46 P.M.**

**Jeff** is wheeled back into the room post-scan, looking slightly flushed, eyes wide, pupils doing **algebra**.  His wife is waiting in the chair. Calm. Crossed arms.  **Kathy** and **Gilley** are still in the hallway.  **Cremeans** is in the corner, trying to exist quietly.  The nurse parks the bed, adjusts his pillow.  Jeff blinks.  Opens his mouth.

**JEFF**  
I need to talk to **Cremeans** about a **tour of Eastern Europe**.

*His wife stares at him.*

**JEFF (CONT’D)**  
Like—**Poland**, specifically.  **Warsaw. Gdansk.**  Maybe **Lodz** if we can get venue access on a Sunday?  And what's that other one—uh—

(turns his head, blinking)
**Is Kalisz a thing?**

**CREMEANS** (stunned)  
I—uh—yes?  Technically?

**JEFF**  
Great.  I mean, I played **Twilight: 2000** when I was a kid, so I have no idea how much of Poland is **real** versus **burned-out post-apocalyptic hellscape**.

**JEFF’S WIFE** (flat)  
You’ve been unconscious for two days and *that’s* what you lead with?

**JEFF**  
I mean, we’ve done **Norway**, right?  So let’s **open up the map**.

**CREMEANS** (still blinking)  
You have **a tube in your arm**, Jeff.

**JEFF**  
Yeah but I got a **vision**, man.

**JEFF’S WIFE** (sighing)  
Do I even get a *hello?*

**JEFF** (grins)  
Do you want a coupon?  Hi.  

(beat)
**But seriously,** is **Kraków** cool?  Because I feel like it *should be*.

*The nurse adjusts his blanket and walks out with the haunted look of someone who just witnessed a man return from sedation ready to book a six-week Baltic tour.*

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 10:51 P.M.**

**Jeff** is now sitting upright, all IVs considered, buzzing with post-scan clarity.  **His wife** looks halfway between impressed and exasperated.  **Cremeans** leans against the wall, arms folded, already **three moves ahead in the logistical nightmare** Jeff’s trying to manifest.

**JEFF**  
You remember **Twilight: 2000**, right?

**CREMEANS** (laughs under his breath)  
You’re asking me if I remember the **campaign we ran for four straight years**?

**JEFF**  
Yeah, yeah.  You were the **Swedish sniper**.  Gilley was the American tank mechanic.  And Bill kept showing up as that **unplaceable CIA guy** with bad intel and worse hygiene.

**CREMEANS**  
He brought **beef jerky** to the table like it was a prop.

**JEFF**  
Exactly. Anyway, back then, Kalisz felt like the *center of the world*.  So now I’m thinking…Let’s go real-world. **Poland’s on the verge**.

**CREMEANS** (flat)  
You are sitting in a hospital bed with **zero bloodwork clearance**, and you’re trying to pitch me on a **Cold War-era RPG becoming a concert routing strategy.**

**JEFF**  
I’m serious.  You’ve seen the **German industrial push east**, right?  Eurozone stabilizes, German firms start relocating manufacturing to Poland for **cheaper labor**, **looser regs**.  That’s gonna open up **disposable income**, **infrastructure**, and eventually?  **Mid-sized venues.**

**CREMEANS** (sighs)  
Jeff.  Here, in the **year 2000**?  If you’re **lucky**, you can book **Warsaw**.  Maybe **Kraków** in a community center with a folding stage.  Gdansk has a **theater**, but it’s more used to *string quartets and weathered politicians*.

**JEFF**  
Exactly. That’s why we get in **now**.  Build a presence while it’s still **intimate**.  Let the venues grow **with us**.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
Oh, for God’s sake.

**JEFF**  
No, think about it.  What if we were the first arena-sized act to treat Poland like a tier-one market? We’d be **legends**. Cultural diplomats.  Jeff and the Weirdos: **The Warsaw Pact Tour**.

**CREMEANS** (smiling now, despite himself)  
You should stop trying to tour Poland and start **buying it**.

**JEFF** (shrugging)  
I’ve got capital.  Maybe I should.  I could get in early.  A couple properties in Wrocław, maybe…

**CREMEANS** (flat)  
You just woke up from a medical mystery.  You’re talking like you’re building a **real estate empire** in the *shadow of the Iron Curtain.*

**JEFF**  
Yeah, and if I was German, **I’d already be doing it**.

**JEFF’S WIFE** (turning to Cremeans)  
Can you sedate him again?

**CREMEANS**  
If I had a syringe, I’d already be halfway through the plunge.

**JEFF** (jubilant)  
This is **the clearest I’ve felt in months**.  I think we should **strike now**.  Let’s call it **“The Reconstruction Tour.”**

*Jeff leans back, utterly pleased with himself.*  *Cremeans rubs his eyes like someone who knows he’ll now be pricing out Eastern Bloc stagehands for the next three weeks.*

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL HALLWAY – JUST OUTSIDE JEFF’S ROOM – 10:56 P.M.**

**Jeff’s voice echoes faintly from behind the door:**

*“I’m telling you, if we anchor the tour in Vilnius, the Baltic economies will stabilize just from our hotel budget…”*

**Jeff’s wife** stands outside, arms folded, exhausted.  **Jeff’s attending physician**, mid-50s, calm, methodical, steps beside her with a notepad tucked into his coat pocket.

**DOCTOR** (low, careful)  
Is he… normally like that?

**JEFF’S WIFE** (straight-faced)  
Define “like that.”

**DOCTOR**  
I mean—

(gestures vaguely toward the muffled rambling)
That kind of **rapid speech**, **tangents**, **grandiose planning**…He’s talking about buying Poland.  Literally.

**JEFF’S WIFE** (deadpan)  
Yeah.  That’s about **Thursday morning Jeff** before the coffee hits.

**DOCTOR** (still serious)  
So this isn't **new** behavior?  Not… dramatically **worse** than usual?

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
Not worse.  Just…**faster**.  More concentrated.  This is what happens when he’s got **energy, relief**, and **no physical outlet**.

**DOCTOR** (quietly)  
It might be something.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
Like… what?

**DOCTOR**  
We’re still looking.  But post-episode **hypomania** is on the table.  Could be neurological.  Could be metabolic.  Could be the **brain trying to reset** after a collapse.

(beat)
Or this could just be… Jeff.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  (faint smile)  
Doctor, if you figure out how Jeff Evans’ brain works—You might want to write a book.

**DOCTOR**  
If I do, I’ll title it **“Poland and the Pulse.”**

*A loud laugh from inside the room—Jeff again, gleeful.*

*“I’m not saying we invade Belarus, I’m saying we should **monitor** it for venue potential\!”*

**DOCTOR**  
I’m going back in there.  But if he starts trying to **float a new currency**, we’re calling neurology.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL HALLWAY – OUTSIDE JEFF’S ROOM – 10:58 P.M.**

**Jeff’s voice filters out through the door—still mid-monologue about international venue placement and regional economic impact.**

**His wife** leans against the wall, arms crossed, staring at the doctor, who just dropped the word **“hypomania”** like it’s no big deal.  But to her?  It is.

**JEFF’S WIFE** (slowly)  
Excuse me—**Hypomania**?  What does that even mean?  Do I need to get a **book** and **read up**?  
Because I'm just a **bank employee**, not a neurologist.  So if there's something **wrong with his brain**, I’d like you to explain it to me in something **less than a graduate thesis.**

**DOCTOR** (nods, respectfully)  
Fair enough.  It’s not a diagnosis yet—just a possibility we’re considering.  **Hypomania** is a state where someone is extremely **energized**, **talkative**, and full of **big ideas**—but they’re not **delusional** or hallucinating.  It’s **not full mania** like in bipolar disorder.  But it’s **a close cousin**.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
So… like the way he gets when he wants to write an album and a screenplay and rearrange the spice rack all in the same afternoon?

**DOCTOR**  
Exactly.  If someone is *normally like that*, it might just be their personality.  But when it happens **after a collapse**, and it’s a **sudden surge**, we ask: Is this the brain **overcompensating**?  Trying to reboot?  Or…Is there something **underlying**?

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
And what do you do about it?

**DOCTOR**  
First, we observe.  Then we get the **CT results**.  If we’re still concerned, we refer to **neuropsych** or **psychiatry** for evaluation.  We’re not there yet.  But I wanted you to be aware.

**JEFF’S WIFE** (quiet, eyes narrowing)  
So, worst-case?

**DOCTOR**  
Worst-case?  It’s the **first visible flare** of something he’s been **hiding or suppressing for years**.  Best-case?  He’s just… Jeff.

**JEFF’S WIFE** (sighs)  
God help you if that’s your baseline.

*A beat passes. Inside the room, Jeff loudly asks if anyone knows how many power outlets are in the average Warsaw green room.*

**DOCTOR**  
We’ll keep watching.  But if you notice this doesn't slow down—Or if he starts crashing emotionally—Let us know.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
Trust me.  I'll see it before you do.  I always have.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL – WAITING ROOM ALCOVE – 11:05 P.M.**

A bank of vending machines hums softly.  There’s a small glassed-in waiting room next to the nurse station.  Empty except for a few chairs, a dry-erase board, and the kind of table that’s only good for late-night snacks and serious decisions.

**Kathy** stands by the doorway, arms crossed, watching through the narrow window.

She **scans the hallway**:

* **Bill** is half-reading a paperback nearby.
* **Jim** is quietly tying and untying his shoelaces.
* **Jeremy** is leaning against a wall, debating whether to walk back in.

And **Gilley**?  Still in **Jeff’s room**, acting like he’s guarding the Pope of Prog Rock.  So she does what she always does when subtlety is necessary—She goes full **Kathy**.

**She raises her hand**, fingers curled.  **Points downward** in a tight circle.  Then **opens her palm**, then **closes it** into a fist.  It’s not military.  It’s **setlist language**.  **Tour-body-signal language**.

And **Gilley**, mid-sentence inside the room, **stops talking**.  Turns his head.  Tilts it.  And—without finishing his sentence—**walks out.**

**JEFF’S WIFE** (blinking)  
Did she just Jedi him?

**CREMEANS** (sipping from a vending machine coffee)  
She’s been doing that since 1992.

Gilley walks up to Kathy like a man who just followed orders from **his soul**.

**GILLEY**  
You rang?

**KATHY**  
We’re meeting.  Now.

**GILLEY**  
I didn’t even know I had agreed.

**KATHY**  
You did.  With your face.

*One by one, she motions the rest of the gang in—*  *no shouting, no urgency, just **pure stage presence** and **“don’t make me repeat this” energy.***  And it works.  Too well.  **Gilley almost salutes.**

**JIM** (muttering)  
I swear she still runs this like a tour bus with brakes that hate us.

*They gather in the small side room, six seats and a whiteboard, a half-broken marker in the tray.*  **Kathy stands at the head.**

**KATHY**  
This is **off the record**.  This is **not management.**  This is **us.**  I’m about to make a motion.  And if you say no?  Make it a good no.  Because I’m bringing **everything** I’ve got.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL WAITING ROOM ALCOVE – 11:09 P.M.**

Six chairs.  One dry erase board.  The band.  **Kathy stands** at the head of the table like she’s about to read a verdict into record.  **Cremeans is not in the room**, but his **clipboard aura** is very much present.

**Gilley** is already **pacing**—tight, looping movements like he’s trying to generate his own orbit.  
His shoes are squeaking, slapping the linoleum, again and again.  

**Bill**, **Jeremy**, **Jim**, and **Kathy** are seated.  The weight of the moment feels like static electricity.

**KATHY**  
Okay.  I’m calling the **roll**.  But since all you **fuckers are here**, I’m going to dispense with the rest of that **bullshit.**

(slow, deliberate)
We are **not canceling**.  Let me be **clear** on that.  Cremeans would **pinch me** from across the astral plane if I said **cancel.**

**GILLEY** (pacing hard)  
He would.  Like a bureaucratic ghost.

**KATHY**  
So the motion is this: We **postpone** the **December leg** of the tour.

(she breathes, once)
We go **cold** through the end of the year.  And we go **hot again in January**, *if*—and only if—**Jeff makes a swift recovery**.

**JIM** (deadpan)  
So we’re just… done?

**KATHY**  
For the year?  Yes.  We’re just **done**.

**GILLEY** (snap-pacing now)  
We haven’t taken a year-end break since—Jesus, since 1995?  Do you know what I do with downtime?  I start **projects.**

**BILL**  
You tried to start a kombucha label last time.

**GILLEY**  
I **tried**.  You don’t get sued by *both* of the Olsen twins unless you’re trying.

**KATHY**  
Gilley—Stop **digging a hole** in the floor.

**GILLEY**  
I’m just saying—this is a **big pause**.  What if we lose heat?  What if we lose the *fans*? What if—

**KATHY** (sharp)  
What if we lose your brother in arms **Jeff**?

*That shuts the room up. Gilley stops moving.*  The words hang there like a smoke cloud.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**  
I’m not risking another minute of him in a spotlight until we know he’s **safe**.  Not **functional**.  Not **ready**.  Not **brilliant**.  Just **safe**.

**JEREMY** (softly)  
Aye.  I'll second.

**KATHY**  
Good.  The motion’s on the floor.  **All in favor of postponing until January—say Aye.**

**BILL**  
Aye.

**JIM**  
Aye.

**JEREMY**  
Aye.

**KATHY**  
Aye.

*Everyone looks at **Gilley**, who’s still standing. Still twitching.*

**GILLEY** (quiet)  
Aye.

*She nods. Final.*

**KATHY**  
Then we’re dark through December.  Pack it up.  Tell the label.  No press.  No spin.  Just **recovery**.

*Silence. Agreement. And for the first time in a long time, maybe a little **peace**.*

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL WAITING ROOM ALCOVE – 11:17 P.M.**

The vote has been taken.  The tour is **paused**.  The room is quiet—*not defeated*, just **drained**.  **Gilley** breaks the silence with his usual *half-sincere, half-deflective tone*, but this time it’s got **real weight** under it.

**GILLEY** (sighs)  
Cool.  I mean, I’m not **happy**.  Not even close.  But it’s the **right call**.

(beat)
So I guess I’m flying out to **L.A.**  I’ll be back by **New Year’s**.

**KATHY**  
You gonna keep it chill out there?

**GILLEY**  
Only if the city lets me.

*A silence settles again, and then **Bill**, still seated, speaks without looking up.*

**BILL**  
You know what I was doing **New Year’s Y2K**?

*Everyone turns a little, waiting.*

**BILL (CONT’D)**  
I was with **Jeff**.  On a rooftop bar.  Baltimore, weirdly enough.  We had bourbon.  We watched fireworks.  And we both just… sat there, thinking the world might stop.  Computers might crash. Planes might fall. You remember.

**JIM**  
I remember.

**BILL**  
But nothing happened.  Everything just… **kept going**.  Quiet.  Warm.  Like the future was just *waiting for us to catch up.*

(beat)
Maybe we get a shot at that again.  Same place.  Same drink.  Same people.

**JEREMY**  
You think we’ll all be there?

**BILL**  
I think it’s **comforting as hell** to believe we **could be**.  And right now?  That’s enough.

*They all sit with that—not a plan, not a promise, but a hope.*  *The idea that a future moment of peace, bourbon, and brotherhood **still exists on the calendar**.*

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL WAITING ROOM ALCOVE – 11:22 P.M.**

The band is still gathered, coming down off the high-stakes vote.  Kathy clears her throat and **snaps them back to order**.

**KATHY**  
Alright.  **Part B** of this meeting.  So **pay attention**, because this is **important**.

She walks to the whiteboard. It squeaks as she grabs the marker.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**  
What’s the **media strategy**?  Because the press?  Has officially gone **berserk**.  I haven’t even had time to **ask what happened at Giants Stadium**—and I was **on the stage.**

**JEREMY**  
They’re treating it like **JFK meets Spinal Tap.**

**JIM**  
Some of the message boards think Jeff’s **in a coma** and the band’s hiding it.

**KATHY**  
Exactly.  So we need a strategy that’s **not full silence**, but **not wide open either**.

**GILLEY** (interjects, pacing slower now)  
Okay, wait.  Let me throw this in the blender—What about concert video?  From **Baltimore**.  That acoustic set?  It’s the most **raw**, **honest**, **stupidly beautiful** thing we’ve ever done.

**JEREMY**  
We didn’t even have a sound check.

**GILLEY**  
That’s the point.  It was **real**.  And I say we **cut it**, we **clip it**, and we send it to **Jeff**.  Let *him* watch it.  If he puts a **thumbs up on it**, why not sell it?

**BILL**  
You mean like—An acoustic album?

**GILLEY**  
Yes.  Concert video + acoustic CD.  Soft release. Limited run. **Low-pressure.**  Let the world see what we did when everything was on fire and we didn’t panic—we **played.**

**KATHY** (leaning back, thinking)
Do you think maybe—Just maybe—By giving Jeff something **cool** to chew on, something that’s **not demanding**, that’s *about the music*?  That we give him something to feel **proud of** without **putting him back under the lights**?

**GILLEY**  
Exactly.  Let him be **in control**.  Let him **say yes** to something **easy**.  Something that reminds him why he still **matters**.

*Silence for a beat. Then—*

**KATHY**  
Alright.  Cremeans will hate it.  But I’m kind of in love with it.  Let’s get the **audio pulled**, and the **video scrubbed**.  We cut it, clean it, and deliver it to Jeff with **no expectations**.  Just a gift.

**JIM**  
A gift to him.  And maybe to **all of us.**

*They sit in that moment. Hopeful. Quiet.*  *Like they’ve just found something beautiful inside the wreckage.*

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL WAITING ROOM ALCOVE – 11:29 P.M.**

The band is still gathered.  The acoustic album idea is out there.  Hope, for the first time, is on the table.  Then **Jeremy** speaks up, quieter than usual.  Not performing.  Just asking.

**JEREMY**  
Hey…This might be weird, but—We have the **raw feeds**, right?  From **Giants Stadium**?

**KATHY**  
Yeah. Multiple cams.  We were filming for the **archival crew**, remember?

**JEREMY**  
Right.  So…can we pull **Jeff’s feed**?  Like, his **cam track**.  Just him.

**BILL**  
We usually have a **stagewide cam**, plus a couple **isolated rig shots**.  One was on you.  One was definitely on Jeff.

**JEREMY** (quietly)  
Because I can’t stop thinking…That was the last time he was…

(pause)
**Quote-unquote “normal.”**

*He makes air quotes and instantly regrets it, his face twisting in guilt.*

**JEREMY (CONT’D)**  
I hate that I have to do that.  Say **“Jeff”** and **“normal”** like they don’t belong together.  Like his brain is this **thing we tiptoe around**, like it’s **fragile** or **unreliable** or **off-script**.  He’s my **brother**.
And I can’t remember the last time I looked at him and thought, “Yeah, he’s fine.”

**KATHY**  
Jeremy—

**JEREMY**  
No, seriously.  Was he already falling apart at **Giants Stadium**?  Was he—*was he crumbling in front of all of us and none of us saw it?*  Because if he was…I want to **know**.  Not to blame anyone.  Just so I stop telling myself we were too late when we didn’t have to be.

*A long pause. The room’s gone still again. Not silent—just full of **weight.**  Gilley exhales deeply.  Bill won’t make eye contact.  Jim nods slowly, jaw tight.*

**KATHY**  
We can find the feed.  We’ll pull it.  And if you want, we’ll **watch it together.**

**JEREMY**  
Thanks.

(beat)
I need to **see** what I missed.  Because if we get another chance?  I don’t want to miss **anything**.

*They all sit with that—**the footage, the possibility, the accountability.***  *Because art records everything.*  *And sometimes, the worst thing you ever captured is also the **truest**.*

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL MEDIA ROOM – 2:03 A.M.**

A **darkened side room** converted from some forgotten admin office.  Two chairs.  A beat-up **TV monitor**, portable deck, and one of Cremeans’ ancient **field laptops** cabled into a hard drive array.  **Jeremy** leans forward with a Styrofoam coffee cup, staring dead into the glow of the screen.  **Kathy** sits beside him, barefoot now, her boots kicked to the side, hoodie over her hair.

The feed is raw—straight from a **stage-left isolation cam** locked onto **Jeff**.

**JEREMY** (quiet)  
There.  Pause it.  Right… **there**.

**KATHY** (pauses frame)  
Second chorus of *Sin and Death*.

**JEREMY**  
Look at his hand.

Onscreen, **Jeff’s left hand** lingers just a half-second too long over a chord, **slightly late**, like he’s losing time.

**KATHY**  
That’s not playing.  That’s **searching**.

They hit play. Jeff recovers. Keeps going. Mask still on.

**JEREMY**  
Rewind fifteen seconds.

They rewind. Rewatch. Again. Again. Then they jump ahead.  **Third song**.  **Jeff is smiling**, but it’s **wrong**. The eyes don’t match.

**KATHY**  
That's the first time he missed a harmony cue on a bridge since ‘96.  I remember because he **never misses** that cue.

**JEREMY**  
We all thought it was some… *loose night energy.*  But he was **drifting**.

*They sit in silence for a beat, listening to the static hiss under the raw audio.*

**KATHY** (small voice)  
We were **so busy** performing together, we stopped **playing together.**

**JEREMY** (sips coffee)  
Yeah. And now we’re watching a man **disappear** in slow motion. In 480p.

**KATHY** (flat)  
Art is a bitch.

They continue watching—**Jeff lit by stadium lights**, a thousand decibels hiding a private crisis.  At 2:14 A.M., Jeremy pulls a blanket from the corner and tosses it at Kathy.

**JEREMY**  
We’re finishing it.  Start of set to final encore.  You with me?

**KATHY**  
Yeah.  I’m with you.

**And they sit side by side**, watching every frame of their own failure—**not to wallow**, but to **understand**.  Because **next time**?  There’s not going to be a hospital room buffer.  Just **each other**.  And the sound.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL – MONTAGE – THE NIGHT BLEEDS INTO MORNING**

**2:27 A.M. – MEDIA ROOM**

**Kathy and Jeremy** huddled close over a screen.  The hum of the playback deck, frozen frames of Jeff’s hands lagging behind the beat.  Empty coffee cups.  Scribbled notes.  No talking for twenty minutes—just that kind of **silence that only comes from shared purpose and shame.**

### **2:41 A.M. – HOTEL ROOM**

**Bill** lies in a sterile bed.  The comforter twisted around him.  His eyes wide open, staring at the ceiling as his brain replays the whole setlist from Giants Stadium—trying to remember when exactly things went off-key.

### **3:02 A.M. – HOSPITAL COT, FAMILY ROOM**

**Gilley**, half-curled under a blanket, mutters in his sleep: "No pyro… no, the intro's not supposed to be in E minor… Jeff, hit the line…"  He flips, mutters again, shoves the pillow like it owes him money.

### **3:45 A.M. – HOSPITAL ROOM, JEFF'S SIDE**

**Jeff’s wife**, in a chair, arms crossed, eyes fluttering open every twenty minutes to check on him.

She reads two pages of a paperback.  Then stares at him again.  Then sighs.  Then closes the book and leans her head back.  Sleep never sticks.

### **4:22 A.M. – JEFF'S HOSPITAL BED**

**Jeff**?  Dead to the world.  Peaceful. Breathing deep.  Not a twitch.  Not a dream.  Just **complete, unbothered REM** like he’s on a beach somewhere.

### **5:56 A.M. – MEDIA ROOM**

**Kathy and Jeremy**, eyes red, still watching footage.  Jeff’s fourth song.  He stumbles.  
They lean in.

“There. That’s it. He’s fading.”

Jeremy doesn’t even nod.  He just **hits pause**.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL – MEDIA ROOM – SUNRISE – 6:58 A.M.**

The room is glowing in gray-blue pre-dawn.  **Empty cups**, **half-eaten crackers**, and a **timeline full of timestamps** scroll on the laptop screen.  **Kathy** is slumped in the chair. Her eyes are **cracked open**, barely.  **Jeremy** is leaned over the table, head resting on his crossed arms, still **awake**, still **processing**.

**KATHY** (groggy, hoarse)  
Oh God.  That was… **repetitive**.

**JEREMY**  
Yeah.  Like watching a **slow-motion tire blowout**—from seven angles.

*They both blink at the screen. The last freeze-frame of Jeff, slightly hunched at the bridge of a song, still onscreen.*

**KATHY**  
So that was **night three**.  The big finish. Giants Stadium.  Not a trainwreck.  But not… him.

**JEREMY**  
Six hours to confirm one thing: Our **bass player** had a **so-so** night in front of **eighty thousand people**.

**KATHY**  
And we called it “electric.”

**JEREMY**  
Because the house was shaking and the crowd was drunk on nostalgia.  We missed it.  We missed **him fading**.

**KATHY** (quiet, staring at the screen)  
So what about the **rest**?  What about **Philly**? What about **Syracuse**? Do we have to do this for **every night**?

---

*Jeremy rubs his face like he wants to erase it.*

---

**JEREMY**  
We could.

We probably **should**.

---

**KATHY**  
Do you remember if he was **sloppy** when we rehearsed the **Sopranos theme** in Staten Island?

---

**JEREMY**  
(blinks, trying to rewind his memory)

That was… what?  
Three days before the first Jersey show?

---

**KATHY**  
Yeah.

You. Me. Jeff. Gilley on harmonica, pretending to be Clarence Clemons.

---

**JEREMY**  
God, I forgot about the harmonica.

---

**KATHY**  
Was Jeff off then?

---

**JEREMY**  
I don’t know.  
I thought he was just **winging it**.  
We were laughing.  
Gilley was shouting fake Italian at the wall.

It didn’t feel wrong.

---

**KATHY**  
But we weren’t **listening**.

We were performing.

---

*They stare at the paused video again. Kathy leans forward, chin on hand.*

---

**KATHY (CONT’D)**  
So.

Do we dig deeper?

Or do we hand this off to someone else and sleep?

---

**JEREMY**  
If we hand it off, we’ll **never believe their notes**.

---

**KATHY**  
(sighs)  
Yeah.

So let’s go back.

Start at **Charlotte**.

---

*Jeremy sits up, hits the next drive in the chain.*

---

**JEREMY**  
But we’re eating something.

Like… **food**. Real **non-vending-machine** food.

---

**KATHY**  
Agreed.

Also you owe me a back rub.

---

**JEREMY**  
Add it to the rider.

---

*They dive back in.*  
*Because that’s love, too—*  
***going back through the footage, even when you already know what it’s going to say.***  
*Just in case you missed something.*

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL MEDIA ROOM – SUNRISE – 7:12 A.M.**

The sun is now rising full through the blinds—those **slanted hospital blinds** that don’t block light so much as **organize it into guilt beams**.

**Kathy and Jeremy** are sunk in their chairs, eyes red, skin pale from monitor glare.  
Another concert file is halfway loaded.  
Jeremy is chewing on the same empty coffee stir stick from two hours ago.

---

**JEREMY**  
(laughs, half-crazy)  
We’re so fuckin’ **punch drunk** from exhaustion—

---

*He sits up, blinks like he just saw a ghost.*

---

**JEREMY (CONT’D)**  
**Jeff never made it to Charlotte.**

---

*Kathy freezes. Turns slowly, eyebrow raised.*

---

**JEREMY (CONT’D)**  
**He never made it out of Baltimore intact.**

All this dissecting Giants Stadium, and *Baltimore’s the break point.*

Charlotte never **happened**.

He didn’t play.

He **crashed before call time**.

---

**KATHY**  
(sits back, wide-eyed, whispering)

Oh my God.  
We are that **stone drunk stupid**.

---

**JEREMY**  
We’re watching tape like it's a **crime scene**, and the actual **crime** was already reported **and hospitalized**.

---

*They both start to laugh. That kind of **quiet, miserable, joyful laughter** that comes from truth landing hard.*

---

**KATHY**  
(sighs, leaning back)

But…

You can give me that **back rub** now.

---

**JEREMY**  
(deadpan)  
It’ll be the shittiest back rub in recorded music history.

---

**KATHY**  
As long as you don’t fall asleep halfway through it, I’ll take it.

---

\*They sit in the light. Exhausted. Broken open.  
But weirdly **lighter** than they’ve felt in days.

Because they finally said it.  
They finally saw it.

And now?

They can finally stop digging.\*

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL MEDIA ROOM – 7:16 A.M.**

The sun is up.  The video feed is paused.  The silence is thick, and everything smells faintly of warm electronics and vending machine sugar. **Kathy** leans forward, stretching her neck, her spine cracking audibly.

**KATHY**  
Alright.  Back rub time.

**JEREMY** (stretches, rubbing his eyes)  
Okay, but like—This is gonna be a **shoulders only**, **over the hoodie**, **zero chemistry**, **neutral zone** back rub.

**KATHY** (raising an eyebrow)  
Why are you laying out conditions like this is a hostage negotiation?

**JEREMY**  
Because, **Kathy**, if you’ll recall—When I was **freshly divorced** and **deeply stupid**, we **fucked**.

**KATHY** (still calm)  
Oh, that.

**JEREMY**  
Yeah. *That.* And while it was, you know… **decent**, it was also **a massive tactical error**  
involving **tequila**, **tour stress**, and a **hotel air conditioner that wouldn't turn off**.

**KATHY** (grinning now)  
You make it sound like a war crime.

**JEREMY**  
I'm just saying—This is not that.  No **under the shirt** anything.  No **emotional unraveling followed by bad decisions**. Just a back rub. Because we’re **trauma-bonded** and **underslept**,  
not *flirting*.

**KATHY** (smirking)  
Understood.  But if your fingers suck, I *am* going to pretend that was the reason we never did it again.

**JEREMY**  
Deal.

*He moves behind her and presses his thumbs into her shoulders.*  *It’s awkward. Basic. A little too firm.*  *But it’s honest.*  And it’s **nothing like last time.**  Which is the **whole point.**

---

## **INT. JEFF’S HOSPITAL ROOM – 7:28 A.M.**

**Jeff** is sitting up in bed, wearing a hospital gown like a king wears a robe.  He looks **alarmingly fresh**, considering the last 72 hours.  His hair is a mess. His eyes are bright.  **His wife** is sitting nearby, flipping through a magazine, exhausted.  **Cremeans** walks in with a clipboard.

**JEFF**  
Okay.  Listen up.  We have a **situation**.

**CREMEANS**  
…What kind of situation?

**JEFF**  
I require **meat**.  And **potatoes**.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
You just woke up. You had beef and broccoli like twelve hours ago.

**JEFF**  
That was **a snack**.  What I need now is a **foundation.**

**CREMEANS**  
A foundation?

**JEFF**  
Yes. A **grease-based**, **salt-forward**, **no-compromises** foundation of breakfast **brilliance**.

(beat)
And no.  Not **au gratin potatoes**.  Don’t you dare come in here with your little **cheesy layers of sad French disappointment**.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
What *kind* of potatoes?

**JEFF**  
**Potato hacks.**  You know—**hashbrowns.**  Crispy. Golden. Slightly dangerous around the edges.

**CREMEANS**  
Where exactly do you think we’re gonna find that at 7:30 in the morning in Baltimore?

**JEFF**  
*Waffle House*.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
There’s no Waffle House in the city.

**JEFF**  
Then somebody drives.  Somebody gets in a car, **goes to a Waffle House**, and brings me:

* **Waffles** with **chocolate chips**,
* **Sausage**,
* **Bacon**,
* And **hashbrowns smothered, covered, and emotionally available**.

**CREMEANS**  
You’re still hooked up to an IV.

**JEFF**  
Exactly.  Which means **I’m not going anywhere**.  So somebody else has to.

(leans back, hands behind his head)

I’ve been unconscious.  I’ve earned this.

**JEFF’S WIFE** (sighs, pulling out her phone)  
Fine.  I’ll call Kathy.

**JEFF**  
Tell her it’s a **meat-and-potatoes emergency**.  She’ll understand.

---

## **INT. JEFF’S HOSPITAL ROOM – 7:31 A.M.**

**Jeff** is now lying dramatically across the bed, staring at the ceiling like a Roman emperor waiting for grapes.

**JEFF**  
If I don’t get sausage and hashbrowns soon, I’m going to start issuing **decrees**.

**JEFF’S WIFE** (sighs)  
God, you’re worse after sleep.

She stands up, walks to the door, and flags down a **passing nurse** with the sharp, tired authority of a woman who once filed three lawsuits in one fiscal quarter *and won all of them*.

**JEFF’S WIFE (TO NURSE)**  
Can you please find **Kathy Espich**?  She’s somewhere in the building.  Tell her: **“Jeff would like Waffle House, please.”**

**NURSE**  
Just… Waffle House?

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
That’s all she’ll need.

**JEFF (from the bed)**  
And **hashbrowns**.  Say the word **“crispy.”**  Make eye contact when you say it.

**NURSE**  
Okay then.

She walks off, confused but already half-running.

**JEFF’S WIFE** (sits back down)  
If you live through this, we’re revisiting your entire relationship with starch.

**JEFF**  
Only if we do it **over waffles**.

---
## **INT. HOSPITAL MEDIA ROOM – 7:34 A.M.**

The light is **too bright**.  **Jeremy** is behind **Kathy**, giving a sluggish, barely-effective back rub.  Both look like they’ve been living in a **basement archive of regret and caffeine** for a week.

The **door opens**, and a **nurse** leans in with professional confusion and secondhand discomfort.

**NURSE**  
Uh… message from Jeff Evans.  He would like **Waffle House**, please.

**KATHY** (sighs, eyes still closed)  
Of course he would.  I know **exactly** what his order’s gonna be.

**JEREMY** (blinking)  
How do you know that?

*Kathy rolls her head slightly to the side, gives him the kind of **look that predates sleep, guilt, and tact**.*

**KATHY**  
Do you have any idea how many times we **fucked** and then went to **Waffle House** at **4 o’clock in the morning**?

*Jeremy freezes, hand halfway through a shoulder circle.*

**KATHY (CONT’D)**  
I mean, no.  You **probably don’t** know.  So just let that **fester** in your imagination.

**JEREMY** (small voice)  
It’s already festered like Fester. Thanks.  I'll never be the same.

**NURSE** (silently turning, retreating)  
I’m… just gonna go tell the kitchen we’re finding a ride.

*Door closes.*

Kathy snorts.

**KATHY**  
Sausage, bacon, chocolate chip waffles, hashbrowns smothered and covered.  It’s like he’s trying to seduce his arteries.

**JEREMY**  
He’s too happy for a guy with a possible neurological event.

**KATHY**  
It’s the hashbrowns. They override mortality.

---


## **INT. HOSPITAL MEDIA ROOM – 7:39 A.M.**

**Jeremy**, half-dead and rubbing his neck now, squints at Kathy.

**JEREMY**  
Hey Kathy…

What the hell does **"smothered and covered"** even mean?

**KATHY** (sits up slowly, with the gravity of a woman who has explained this before)
Okay.  Let’s get something straight.  Waffle House hashbrowns are like **tattoo choices**—
the more you stack, the more you’re announcing who you *really are inside*.

**JEREMY**  
That’s not comforting.

**KATHY**  
“**Smothered**” means you want them with **grilled onions**.  Like, greasy, translucent, kiss-of-regret onions.  “**Covered**” means **melted American cheese**—the kind that doesn’t belong to a food group but does belong in your bloodstream.

**JEREMY**  
So onions and cheese.  That’s it?

**KATHY**  
That’s just the **entry level**.

You can also get them:

* **Chunked** – with ham.
* **Diced** – with tomatoes.
* **Peppered** – jalapeños.
* **Capped** – mushrooms.
* **Topped** – chili.
* **Country** – drowned in sausage gravy.

**JEREMY**  
That’s not a breakfast. That’s a **breakdown.**

**KATHY**  
Exactly.  That’s why Jeff gets **smothered and covered**—he wants flavor, **but not a full psychotic episode**.

**JEREMY** (sighs)  
And to think I was just gonna ask for toast.

**KATHY**  
You’re not ready for this kind of lifestyle, Evans.

*They sit there, dead-eyed but closer now—bonded by trauma, waffles, and the sacred knowledge of roadside decadence.*

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL MEDIA ROOM – 7:41 A.M.**

Kathy has gone full ragdoll in her chair, hoodie pulled tight around her face like she’s bracing for re-entry.  **Jeremy**, eyes red, hair like a hay bale, squints like a man solving a riddle in a fog bank.

**JEREMY**  
Okay.  Maybe we ought to have… uh…I don’t know.  Who else is even here?  Is **Bill** in the building?

**KATHY** (snorts, without looking)  
Bill went to the hotel hours ago.  Probably dreaming about **compression ratios** and **vintage ribbon mics**.

**JEREMY** (creaking forward in the chair)  
We’re too tired to drive.

**KATHY**  
Yeah.  We’re **liability tired**.  If I sit behind a steering wheel right now, I’m gonna think it’s a **synth module**.

(beat)
Let’s just…I don’t know.  Let’s **make Gilley drive**.

**JEREMY**  
Is Gilley even **here**?

**KATHY** (checks the door, doesn’t see him)  
I don’t know.  If he isn’t, we’ll **summon him**.

**JEREMY**  
Like **Beetlejuice**?

**KATHY**  
Exactly.  Just say **“hashbrowns”** three times and he appears in a bathrobe with keys in his hand.

**JEREMY** (calls out)  
**HASHBROWNS. HASHBROWNS. HASHBROWNS.**

*Nothing happens.*

**KATHY**  
Damn.  He might be **napping in the supply closet** again.

**JEREMY**  
He better not be in my old hoodie.

**KATHY**  
Just find him.  Promise him coffee. Or chaos. Or a dumb girl with a harmonica.  He’ll do it.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL MEDIA ROOM – 7:43 A.M.**

**Kathy** suddenly bolts upright in her chair, eyes wild, hair a mess, hoodie askew, but face **radiant with epiphany**.  **Jeremy**, mid-yawn, freezes at the tone shift.

**KATHY**  
I am the most **goddamn genius woman** on the face of this planet.

**JEREMY** (concerned)  
Okay.  Why do you sound like you're about to build a trebuchet?

**KATHY**  
Because I know **exactly** how we’re going to get to **Waffle House**.  And we are going to do it like **Greek gods descending from Olympus**.

**JEREMY** (scared now)  
Kathy.  You have **too much tone**.  You have a **dangerous amount of tone** right now.  How the hell are we getting to Waffle House?

**KATHY** (pitch perfect, finger in the air)
We’re going to go outside.  We’re going to **find Tom**.  And we’re going to tell him to **take the tour bus**.  And we’re going to **Waffle House**.  That’s how we’re going to do it.

*Jeremy stares at her like she just solved world peace with duct tape.*

**JEREMY**  
You want us to take a **tour bus** to **Waffle House**?

**KATHY**  
You’re damn right I do.  We’re exhausted.  We smell like **regret and bandwidth**.  And Jeff wants **hashbrowns**.  And we are not peasants.

**JEREMY**  
This is either brilliant or unhinged.

**KATHY**  
What’s the difference?

*They both stand. Kathy straightens her hoodie like she’s donning ceremonial robes. Jeremy grabs his jacket like it’s a reluctant flag of allegiance.*

**KATHY (CONT’D)**  
Let’s go **find Tom**.  We ride at **dawn**.

**JEREMY**  
Kathy, it *is* dawn.

**KATHY**  
Then we ride *now*.

---

## **EXT. HOSPITAL BACK PARKING LOT – 7:51 A.M.**

**Tom** stands outside the idling **Commuted tour bus**, coffee in one hand, cigarette in the other, looking like a man who just **wanted a quiet paycheck** and ended up inside a Greek tragedy sponsored by waffle batter.  **Kathy** and **Jeremy** approach—Kathy in a hoodie like a war cloak, Jeremy trailing behind with the half-zombie posture of a man ready to die for potatoes.


**TOM** (eyeing them)  
No.  Absolutely not.  Don’t even say it.

**KATHY**  
Tom—

**TOM**  
Lady, do you have **any idea** how difficult it is to get into one of those **rinky-dink Waffle House parking lots**?  They were built for **Fords**, not **tour fortresses**.

**KATHY** (squints at him)
Are you a **train professional** or **not**?

**TOM** (train-whistle exhale)
Oh, I see.  We’re doing **philosophy** now.


**KATHY**  
You’ve navigated **Vegas after a thunderstorm**, **I-70 through snow**, and that time Bill spilled kombucha on the electrical panel.  This is just **a parking lot** and **destiny**.

**JEREMY**  
We’ll buy you **three waffles** and a **moral exemption** from anything that happens in the next four hours.

**TOM** (beat)  
Do I get coffee?

**KATHY**  
The **good kind**. No hospital shit.

---

**TOM**  (sighs, flicks cigarette)  
Fine.  But if I have to reverse into a **dumpster**, we’re blaming **Jeff**.

**KATHY**  
Obviously.

*Tom climbs aboard. The engine revs. The gods ride to Waffle House.*

---


## **INT. TOUR BUS – ROLLING TOWARD WAFFLE HOUSE – 8:02 A.M.**

The **engine rumbles**, the windows rattle, and the **Commuted tour bus** barrels down a quiet Baltimore road, a **mythic steel vessel bound for hashbrowns**.  **Kathy** is slouched in the front lounge seat, one boot off, one eye open.  **Jeremy** leans toward her, whispering like he’s uncovering a deep secret.

**JEREMY**  
Hey.  I think you meant **trained professional**.  Not **train professional**.

*Kathy doesn’t move. Just lifts one eyebrow.*

**JEREMY (CONT’D)**  
As in…Not the kind of guy that goes: **“Choo-choo. Chugga-chugga-chugga-chugga-chugga-chugga-chugga—”**

**KATHY** (flat)  
If you finish that sound effect, I swear to God I will smother you with a Waffle House napkin.

**JEREMY**  
But it would be a **crispy** death.

**KATHY**  
Sleep-deprived me is still capable of violence.

**JEREMY**  
You mean **train violence**?

**KATHY**  
I hope they get your order wrong and give you **dry toast and lukewarm grits.**

**JEREMY** (quiet, terrified gasp)  
You wouldn’t.

**KATHY**  
Try me, **Conductor Dumbass**.

*They ride on.*  *Not rested. Not sane.*  *But rolling strong toward the **golden light of waffles and emotional coping mechanisms**.*

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – ROLLING THROUGH BALTIMORE SUBURBS – 8:06 A.M.**

The road is **clear**, the bus humming like a war machine with a sugar craving.  **Jeremy** glances up toward the windshield as **Tom** swings a wide, perfect turn through a narrowing merge like it’s nothing.

**JEREMY** (grudging respect)  
Tom’s a **pretty badass driver**.

**KATHY** (smirks)  
He’s almost as good as your **dad**.

*Jeremy freezes just a little. Eyes narrow.*

**KATHY (CONT’D)**  
Remember when we went to the **Dayton Airshow** to get **Def Leppard tickets**?  1990?  **Silver Bullet One**, baby.

**JEREMY**  
Oh my **God**.

**KATHY**  
That van was **not road legal**.  The brakes squeaked like a dying fax machine, and your dad took that **off-ramp like he was late to Normandy**.

**JEREMY**  
I would prefer to **black that memory out** of my **consciousness**.

**KATHY**  
Too late.  He drove like a **drag racer with diplomatic immunity**.

**JEREMY**  
Yeah.  But, I mean… **yeah**.  My dad could drive a **vehicle**.

**KATHY**  
If he were here right now, he'd parallel park this bus **between two Geo Metros and a mail truck**, and we’d still make it to Waffle House by **8:15**.

**JEREMY**  
He would’ve brought his own syrup.

**KATHY**  
And judged the hashbrowns like they were **NASA engineering prototypes**.

*They both chuckle softly, eyes glazing over a little with fatigue and memory.*

**JEREMY**  
We were so young.

**KATHY**  
We were so **desperate** to see Def Leppard.

**JEREMY**  
And my dad had **zero idea** what he was enabling.

*Tom calls back from the driver’s seat.*

**TOM**  
You two done with your nostalgic hallucination? Because I’m about to do a **combat turn** into a Waffle House parking lot the size of a **laundry basket**.

**KATHY & JEREMY (IN UNISON)**  
Do it.

---

## **EXT. WAFFLE HOUSE PARKING LOT – 8:12 A.M.**

The sun is rising golden.  Birds chirp.  Someone’s smoking a cigarette next to a rusty Ford Ranger.  Everything is **fine**.

Until it’s not.

Because then, over the hill, comes the **tour bus**.  **Headlights cut through the fog.**  **Diesel hum in stereo.**  **A rolling monolith of regret and greasy intentions.**

Inside the **Waffle House**, behind the counter, a **griddle cook** glances up.  His name tag reads **WALT**.  He’s seen some shit.  He watches the bus pull into the lot, barely clearing the entrance.

**WALT** (quietly, to no one)  
**Nope.**

The waitress—**Mindy**, mid-40s, seasoned in every kind of road-weary breakfast disaster—leans over, sees the bus, and just **laughs once**.

**MINDY**  
Either a minor league baseball team or somebody’s got a hangover with backup singers.

The **bus turns in**.  Tom is **navigating like a submarine pilot**.  **Kathy and Jeremy** are at the window, watching the lot shrink around them.

**JEREMY**  
There is **no way** we’re getting out of here without knocking over **at least one decorative shrub**.

**KATHY**  
Let them sue us.  They’ll get a merch hoodie and a vinyl test pressing of our shame.

Tom gently brakes.  Reverses.  Pulls forward again.  Gilley appears from the back lounge in a bathrobe, confused and excited.

**GILLEY**  
Are we here?  Are we doing the **Hashbrown Redemption**?

**KATHY**  
You’ve got five minutes to look like a human.

**TOM** (leans back, proud)  
And that, kids, is how you parallel park a tour bus **next to a Waffle House dumpster**.

**MINDY** opens the door.  Doesn’t blink.  Just shouts:

**MINDY**  
If you’re here for the **Jeff Evans Special**, the fryer’s already on.

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – Waffle House Parking Lot – 8:13 A.M.**

The bus is parked. The engine still ticks with heat.  **Gilley**, robe loosely tied, emerges from the rear lounge with a **toothbrush in his mouth** and a **plastic comb in his hair** like a forgotten accessory from a glam rock photoshoot.  **Jeremy** turns, sees him, and just **stares**—eyes wide, mouth slowly breaking into an uncontainable grin.

**JEREMY**  
**Where the fuck did you come from, Gilley?**

**GILLEY** (grinning, muffled by toothbrush)  
Back lounge. Showered. Spiritual reset.

**JEREMY**  
No—no.  Don’t just **say that** like it makes sense.  I had **no idea** you were on the bus.  We’ve been on this thing for **half an hour**, and you just now emerge like some kind of **robe-clad raccoon priest**?

*Kathy’s covering her face, trying not to laugh. Gilley spits into a travel mug and shrugs.*

**JEREMY (CONT’D)**  
Please.  Please tell me you were on the bus **alone**.  Please tell me there’s no one **back there**.  Please, please, **you have to tell me**.

**GILLEY** (smiling, ominous)  
Define “alone.”

**JEREMY**  
**No.**

**GILLEY**  
Look, if you didn’t want surprise guests on a breakfast pilgrimage, maybe don’t bring the **Rolling Temple of Excess** to Waffle House at 8 a.m.

**JEREMY** (totally unhinged, doubled over laughing)  
Kathy. Kathy. If I find someone in the bunk with a **ukulele**, I’m gonna **set the waffle iron to kill.**

**KATHY** (struggling not to break)
