Nobody check the bathroom. Nobody. Not right now.

*Tom opens the door.*

**TOM**  
Y’all getting out, or is this gonna be another episode of **“Band Trauma, but Make It Denny’s”?**

---

## **EXT. WAFFLE HOUSE PARKING LOT – 8:15 A.M.**

The tour bus sits like a monument to bad ideas.  The Waffle House is humming, unaware of the storm that’s about to walk in.  **Jeremy** steps down from the bus, eyes darting with **amateur detective energy**.  **Kathy** stretches, one boot on the pavement, hair a mess, hoodie pulled tight.

**JEREMY**  
Okay. I’ve got a plan.

**KATHY**  
Oh boy.

**JEREMY**  
You go in.  Order the food.  You know exactly what Jeff wants.  Do the whole **sausage symphony**, the **smothered sonata**—whatever.

**KATHY** (squinting)  
Why do I feel like I’m being **dispatched** just because I've slept with him?

**JEREMY**  
Because you are.  While you’re making **hashbrown history**, I’m gonna go check the back of the bus.

**KATHY**  
Why?

**JEREMY**  
Because I have a **suspicion**—There may be **loose women** back there.  Like… jazz-influenced, **sleep-deprived**, post-Gilley **loose women**.  Possibly with **patchouli** and a **cracked zither**.

**KATHY** (flat)
If you find a zither, I’m calling security.

**JEREMY**  
If I find a woman with a **didgeridoo**, we’re starting a side project.

*Kathy shakes her head, walking toward the entrance.*

**KATHY**  
Fine. I’ll get Jeff his order.  But if you find someone back there who plays **autoharp**, I’m not helping with the paperwork.

**JEREMY**  
Deal.

*As she enters Waffle House—bell jingling, ready to drop a legendary breakfast order—Jeremy turns with a dramatic inhale, steeling himself for what he might find inside the mysterious, possibly cursed rear lounge of the tour bus.*

---

## **INT. WAFFLE HOUSE – 8:17 A.M.**

**Kathy** walks in like she owns the place.  Grease fog, fluorescent lighting, a booth with duct tape on the seat—it’s **perfect**.  **Mindy the waitress** spots her, coffee pot in hand.

**MINDY**  
You with the bus?

**KATHY**  
I’m with the **waffles**.  And I need the **Jeff Evans Special**:

* Chocolate chip waffle
* Double sausage
* Extra bacon
* Hashbrowns—**smothered and covered**
* Scrambled eggs he won’t eat, but send ‘em anyway for the aesthetic

**MINDY** (points to a booth)  
Sit. I’ll feed you, too. You look like a haunted librarian.

*Kathy sits. Smirks. She does.*

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – REAR LOUNGE – SAME TIME**

**Jeremy**, armed with curiosity and bravado, tiptoes down the narrow hallway toward the **back curtain**.  Soft light filters in through the emergency exit.  It’s too quiet.  He pulls the curtain back like he’s revealing **a crypt**, and—

**JEREMY**  
(sotto)  
Here we go.

Inside:

* **No groupies**
* **No rogue zither players**
* But there’s…
  * A half-eaten pack of **Red Vines**
  * A **sock** that might belong to no one
  * An open book of Rilke poetry
  * And, disturbingly, a **Gilley-branded scented candle** labeled **“Smoked Confidence”**

Jeremy stares.

**JEREMY** (whispers)  
This is somehow **worse** than a woman with a didgeridoo.

He backs out, curtain swaying, wondering if the candle is flammable in a legal sense.

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – BACK LOUNGE – MOMENTS LATER**

Jeremy squints into the dimness.  He bends down.  Sees it.  A lone, crusty-looking **sock**, balled but somehow menacing.  He stares at it like it's whispering Latin.

**JEREMY** (low, to himself)  
Oh… no.  No, no, no.

He stands up—**too fast**—and **erupts**.

**JEREMY (SHOUTING)**  
**GILLEY!!**  **HAVE YOU BEEN USING THIS THING AS A SPANK SOCK?\!**

*No reply. Just the quiet hum of the idling bus and the smell of synthetic candle wax.*

**JEREMY (LOUDER)**  
**Come on! Jesus H. Christ. JEREMY GILLEY\!\!**

Somewhere in the bus, possibly from a supply cabinet or duct vent:

**GILLEY (faintly)**  
Define “using.”

**JEREMY**  
Define—?!  **NO. ABSOLUTELY NOT.**

There is **DNA evidence** on this thing and I did **not sign up for forensic breakfast.**

*He tosses the sock onto the floor like it’s a cursed object and backs away like it might chase him.*

**JEREMY (CONT’D)**  
This is why we can’t have nice things.  This is why Waffle House bans bands.

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – FRONT LOUNGE – 8:27 A.M.**

**Jeremy** has just re-emerged from the back like he survived an exorcism.  He’s pale, holding his hands like they’re radioactive.  **Gilley** strolls in from somewhere—probably a side compartment or an unused bunk—wearing his bathrobe like it’s a diplomatic sash.

**GILLEY** (holding up both hands like a lawyer in a panic)
Okay.  Okay.  Before you get weird—Let me **explain**.

**JEREMY**  
Explain?

**GILLEY**  
I was trying to think **strategically**.

**JEREMY**  
Oh God.

**GILLEY**  
Because I don’t get **a lot of time** to work with the **nurses**, okay?  They’re always **moving**, they’re **fast**, there’s **activity**, and I’m **in demand**, you know?  And I needed—

**JEREMY**  
Nope. I’m out.

**GILLEY**  
Listen!  I needed to **clear my head**.  And I’m not saying it’s a spank sock, but I’m also not **not** saying that.

**JEREMY**  
This is worse than denial.

**GILLEY**  
I was being **efficient**.  I was being a **time management professional**.  Do you want **Jeff to recover** or not?

**JEREMY**  
What does that have to do with—**Fuckit.  No!** You don’t get to use **Jeff’s recovery** as a **justification** for—For that **polyester war crime** I just found in the back lounge!

**KATHY** (from inside Waffle House, through the window)  
If you two don’t shut up, I’m eating your hashbrowns.

**GILLEY** (to Jeremy)  
We’re brothers in crisis. Let’s just… burn the sock and move on.

**JEREMY**  
It’s a biohazard, Gilley. Not a **therapeutic milestone**.

*They both turn slowly and head toward the Waffle House entrance—Jeremy shaking his head, Gilley already trying to workshop a name for the candle he’s going to make about this moment.*

**CUT TO:**

---

## **INT. WAFFLE HOUSE – 8:28 A.M.**

**Mindy** drops off plates that steam like redemption.

**Kathy**, hands folded, smiles **like she just summoned order out of chaos**.

**MINDY**  
Your guy really that picky?

**KATHY**  
He’s not picky.  He’s **ritualistic**.

*Door jingles. Jeremy reappears, shaken but proud.*

**JEREMY**  
Mission accomplished.  No loose women.  Just a traumatic episode I’m going to talk to my therapist about.  

**KATHY**
Spank sock?

**JEREMY**
Spank sock.

**KATHY**  
Waffles?

**JEREMY**  
God, yes, please.

*And for one shining moment, it’s quiet.*  *Just two weirdos, a booth, and the breakfast of legends.*

---

## **INT. WAFFLE HOUSE – BOOTH – 8:33 A.M.**

The food is on the table.  **Jeff’s order** is perfect.  The air smells like maple syrup and regret. **Kathy** sits across from **Jeremy**, who still looks like he’s seen an exorcism.  **Gilley** is next to him, proudly eating bacon with the smug glow of someone who believes his sins were strategic.  Kathy stares at her coffee cup like it’s going to answer the questions the universe refuses to.

**KATHY** (flat, slow)
You know what’s **ironic**?  The only person here **thinking with his dick** is also the only person who’s **remotely coherent** or **logically functioning**.

**JEREMY**  
Don’t say that out loud.

**KATHY**  
I mean it.  **Gilley**—**this idiot**—is out here giving us **strategic analysis** of sock logistics and **tour bus timing**, and I—

(stops, blinking)
Oh my **God**.  Was I actually **trying to defend** someone who was **jerking off on the bus**?

**GILLEY** (cheerfully)  
Not jerking off.  **Resetting mental focus.**

**KATHY**  
**Don’t rebrand your shame.**

**JEREMY**  
I need to bleach my brain and start over.

**KATHY**  
I want a waffle, a nap, and **divine intervention**.

**GILLEY**  
I want us to remember this forever.

**KATHY**  
Oh, we will.  I’m going to write a song about this, and it will ruin your **future relationships**.

**GILLEY**  
Joke’s on you—I’m emotionally unavailable to begin with.

**WAFFLE HOUSE WAITER (passing by)**  
Y’all need anything else?

**KATHY**  
Just… patience.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 8:45 A.M.**

The door swings open.  **Kathy**, still wearing the hoodie of a woman who’s stared into the void, steps in like she’s bearing the **Ark of the Covenant**.  Behind her, **Jeremy** follows with a paper bag of **utensils, napkins**, and a travel cup of **coffee so dark it might be illegal**.  **Jeff** sits upright, alert, eyes shining with **purpose**.

**KATHY**  
Here you go, **Jeff**.

*She sets the container down like it’s a sacred relic.*

**KATHY (CONT’D)**  
And we made sure they used the **good polystyrene box**.  So your food is going to be quite warm
.
**JEFF** (staring at it)  
Oh my God.  Is this—Is this **hashbrowns**?  **Smothered and covered**?

**JEREMY**  
There was a pilgrimage.  There was **fuel spent**.  There was **shouting**.  There was a **sock incident**.

**JEFF**  
A sock incident?

**KATHY**  
Don’t ask.  Just eat.

**JEFF** (softly, with reverence)  
You even got the **chocolate chip waffle**.

**JEREMY**  
And extra bacon. Because you’re **recovering** and you deserve to feel **dangerous**.

**JEFF**  
You guys are—

(snickers)
You’re still the **weirdest people** I know.

**KATHY**  
And you’re still the only one we’ll drive a **tour bus to Waffle House** for.  So eat it while it’s warm. Before Jeremy starts **cataloguing the food** for emotional metaphors.

**JEFF** (holding up a hashbrown forkful like a blessing)
Then let it be known—On this day,  after surviving sedation, surveillance, and whatever the hell that candle was—I reclaim my **right to sodium**.

*And with that, he digs in.  Eyes closed. Bite deep.  Like a man reborn.*

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 8:49 A.M.**

**Jeff**, mid-bite, has syrup on his thumb.  **Kathy** is lounging in the window seat, sipping coffee like a sleep-deprived oracle.  **Jeremy** is peeling the lid off a second waffle box with delicate reverence.  **Cremeans** bursts in, briefcase in one hand, blazer wrinkled, face pale with **bureaucratic tension**.


**CREMEANS**  
Okay.  So.  Quick update—Island Records currently thinks **Jeff’s been dying**.

*A beat.*

Jeff freezes, hashbrown halfway to his mouth.  Jeremy blinks.  Kathy raises an eyebrow.  And **Gilley**—Wherever Gilley was in the room—leaning in the doorway, fiddling with a sugar packet, humming “Radar Love”—**stops cold**.

He turns.  Slow.  Precise.  Like a **heat seaking missile locking onto narrative opportunity.**  Eyes sharp.  Voice quiet.

**GILLEY**  
Dying?

**CREMEANS**  
Yes.  They’ve already had **three emergency calls**, **two internal memos**, and one **A&R guy crying in a stairwell**.


**GILLEY**  (his voice shifting, lower now)  
So they think he’s—**actively dying.**

**CREMEANS**  
That’s the word they used.  Not “hospitalized.” Not “fatigued.”  **Dying.**

*Gilley straightens. The bathrobe might still be present, but now it looks like the robes of a cult leader ready to execute a pivot in global branding.*

**GILLEY**  
Well then.  We have **leverage**.

**KATHY**  
Oh God.  He’s **activating.**

**JEREMY**  
Hide the press kit. He’s gone **full Predator.**

**GILLEY**  
They thought Jeff was dead?  That means the **public** might think that too.  Which means—We now own the most **dramatic resurrection narrative** since Jesus Christ booked Madison Square Garden.

**JEFF**  
I’m just trying to eat bacon.

**GILLEY**  
Then eat it with **gravitas**, Jeff.  Because we’re about to do the **Comeback of the Century**—And it starts with **smothered hashbrowns** and a **camera crew**.

*Cremeans drops his briefcase on the floor with a sigh like he’s aged 30 years in the last 48 seconds.*

**CREMEANS**  
You’re going to give me a coronary.

**GILLEY**  
I’m going to give you a **billboard campaign**.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL HALLWAY – 8:53 A.M.**

Gilley leans against the wall, coffee in one hand, still in his robe, still barefoot, but suddenly radiating **total internal precision**.  His bandmates are behind the door.  **Cremeans** is mid-heart attack from the Island Records fallout.  **Jeff** is mid-bacon.  But **Gilley**?  Gilley is already **six hours ahead.**

**GILLEY (INTERNAL MONOLOGUE)**  
Alright.  Sarah Malcolm.  Four to six hours.  Press badge, probably disguised as compassion.  First pass? **Subtle.**  Just enough lip gloss and eye contact to pretend it’s about sympathy.  Six to eight hours?
**Second pass**.  Polished, private, maybe she wants to "talk" over hospital vending coffee.  

*He sips his own. Smiles.*

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
By **supper time**, if I time it right, her lips’ll be on my—*Well.*  Let’s call it **an information transaction**.  She’s not new to this.  She’s **been doing it** since before we signed with Island.  And she’s good.  Too good.  She gets the **truth** by making you think you’re **already naked**.

He straightens.  Looks down the hallway like he can already see her heels clicking toward him.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
So what do I trade?  What’s the **price** of the scoop?  Do I give her **the night Jeff almost collapsed in Japan?**  Do I give her **Kathy’s breakdown in ‘96**? Or do I hold those cards? Maybe give her just enough to **lead the narrative**,  but keep the core?

*He finishes his coffee.*

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
She’s a wonderful woman.  But **cold as quartz** when she wants the story.  And maybe it’s time I **make a deposit** into her **account**.  Let her **think** she’s buying access.  But what I’ll sell?
Will just be the **headline.**  The **lead.**  Not the **truth.**

He walks back into the room with a grin.  Because **Gilley’s not flinching**.  He’s **plotting**.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 8:56 A.M.**

**Jeff** is still eating, methodically working through a waffle that might as well be his rebirth ceremony.  **Gilley** stands by the window, pacing, robe open like a cape, eyes shining with wild strategy.
**Kathy** sips coffee.  **Jeremy** pokes at his eggs.  **Cremeans** is slumped in a corner chair, muttering something about budget overruns and insurance clauses.

**GILLEY**  
Okay. So listen.  We just—We just made a pact.  We had a vote.  **Jeff.**  We’re **done touring** this year.  Just—**done**.

*Jeff looks up, syrup on his chin, blinking.*

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
We’re giving you **four weeks** to get better.  Four **full** weeks.

**JEFF** (chewing)  
That’s a pretty decent trade.

**GILLEY**  
But here’s the thing: **January 4th**.  **Atlanta**.  That date—That has to be **insane**.  Like… **plussed up**.   Full-scale **media resurrection**.  That show’s not just a concert—It’s a **message**.

**KATHY**  
It’s the **Reset Button Show**.

**GILLEY**  
Exactly.  We need **cameras**, we need **press**, we need **fanfare**, we need **subtext**.  And most importantly—We need a **kickass opening act**.

He spins toward **Cremeans**, now halfway into a paper folder.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
Jeff Cremeans.  Do we got anyone **booked**?

**CREMEANS** (groggy)  
Booked? For Atlanta?  No.  I had a shortlist, but I pulled it when we thought we’d **cancel**.

**JEREMY**  
Okay, but now we’re back on.  So who’s on that list?

**CREMEANS** (smacking his lips)  
Uh… couple newer acts. Nothing massive.  One alt-rock darling. Some synthpop kids from Austin.  Nobody that makes a **statement**.

**GILLEY**  
No. We need **fire**.  We need **contrast**.  Something that says: **"We're back. And no one else matters."**

**KATHY**  
So what are we thinking?  Iconic?  Up-and-coming?  Genre clash?

**GILLEY**  
Yes. All of that.  Someone **unexpected** but **perfect**.  A **sound clash** that sets the tone for a **comeback no one can ignore**.

---

*Everyone leans back, now thinking—serious. Focused.*  Because Atlanta isn’t just a date.  It’s **the new beginning**.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 8:59 A.M.**

Jeff sets down his fork with the kind of authority normally reserved for gavel slams and rock ballads.

**JEFF**  
If we’re going to **Georgia**, and this is gonna be a **Resurrection Act**—Then **R.E.M.**  Somebody call **Stipe**.

*A silence falls over the room. Not shock—just awe at the audacity.*

**JEFF (CONT’D)**  
Does anybody here know **Michael Stipe**?

*Eyes dart.*

**JEFF (CONT’D)**  
**Kathy.**  Do you know **Michael Stipe**?

**KATHY**  (sips coffee)  
Not biblically. Not legally.  I met him once at a **moody art opening** in 1997.  He gave me a look that said “I appreciate your trauma.”

**JEREMY**  
That’s probably how he says hello.

**CREMEANS**  
Do you want R.E.M. to open?  Or to **co-headline**?  Because if this becomes a **Georgia double-feature**, we’re going to need **insurance** and **divine approval.**

**GILLEY**  (grinning, already pacing)  
I don’t care what we have to do.  If we can get Stipe and the boys on stage?  This show goes from **“welcome back”** to **“holy resurrection.”**

**JEFF**  
That’s what I’m saying.  It’s not a **tour restart**.  It’s a **spiritual reset**.

*The room goes still. Because now?*  They’re **actually considering it**.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 9:03 A.M.**

The room is still half-lit by the sun and the fumes of too much Waffle House.  **Jeff** has just dropped the R.E.M. bomb.  Everyone’s heads are spinning with dreams of Stipe, spotlights, and moody harmonies.  And then—**Bill** speaks.

**BILL**  
**No.**  Rejected.  Return to sender.

*The room turns. Bill rarely says “no” this hard.*

**BILL (CONT’D)**  
That’s not somebody who can **fill an arena**.  And it’s not somebody who can **inspire a goddamn thing** now that their drummer’s retired and their pulse is running on **ambient synth pads** and **mid-tempo reflections on architecture**.

**JEFF** (quietly)  
Okay, harsh.

**BILL**  
We need **arena bands**.  **Arena energy**. Not a **soft-focus art project**.

**GILLEY**  
He’s not wrong.  We need someone who makes people show up and scream **before** we hit the stage.

**JEREMY**  
Okay.   So if not Stipe, then who?

**BILL**  
Think.  **Headliners-in-waiting**.  Somebody loud.  Somebody **current**, but with **weight**.  Somebody who gets **butts in seats**, but doesn’t **outshine us**.

*The room falls silent again—but now it's focused. R.E.M. is out.*  It’s time to dig deeper.  To find the name that will **crack Atlanta wide open**. 

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 9:05 A.M.**

The group is frozen in the aftermath of **Bill's takedown** of R.E.M.  **Jeff**, still chewing his bacon slowly, eyes shifting.  **Gilley** is biting his thumb, thinking.  **Jeremy** is scribbling down names that may or may not exist.  **Cremeans** is checking a binder with all the dead eyes of a man doing math at gunpoint.  And then:

**Kathy**, standing, arms crossed, face locked.

**KATHY**  (slow, sharp)  
Well—**Who the fuck else then?**

*Beat.*

**KATHY (CONT’D)**  
I’m serious.  We want **arena-capable**, **emotionally credible**, **crowd-motivating**, **not-a-fucking-art-installation**—THEN.  WHO.  THE.  FUCK.

*Everyone looks at everyone else.*  No one says anything.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**  
Because right now, this whole resurrection tour has a date, a venue, a band with a coma survivor, and **no act** to warm the crowd that isn’t already **crying in their soda**

**JEFF**  (deep sigh)  
Well, we did try to poach **Garbage** in ‘98.

**GILLEY**  
Shirley Manson would incinerate a crowd.

**JEREMY**  
She’d also **incinerate you**.  That’s a dangerous booking.

**BILL**  
You want dangerous, or you want someone who brings **heat**?  Because we don’t need an “opener.”  We need a **primer charge**.

**CREMEANS**  
I’ve got a list.  But if we want **arena-level**, we’re looking at either: * Someone on the **rise**, who owes us a favor **or** * Someone **resurrected**, like us.

*Silence.*

**KATHY**  
Then find me someone who can **resurrect a goddamn room** in 15 minutes.  That’s your assignment. We’ve got four weeks. Make them count.

*The meeting ends not with applause—but with tension.*  *Because this next move is going to define everything.*

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 9:07 A.M.**

Tension is **thick**.  Kathy’s still pacing like a field commander.  Bill’s flipping through mental rosters like a music industry encyclopedia with trust issues.  Jeff is now halfway through his waffle, staring at the middle distance.  **Cremeans**, in the corner, calmly sipping coffee from a paper cup that says “PROPERTY OF FLOOR 2B.”  And then—**Jeremy** turns to him.

**JEREMY**  (eyes narrowing)  
Okay.  **Where’s your list**, Cremeans?

**CREMEANS**  (sips, unbothered)  
Which list?

**JEREMY**  
The one with the **arena openers**.  The ones we could **actually book** for Atlanta.  Do you have that, like…

(points vaguely at the clipboard)
**Written down**?  Or is it at home?  Or…

(leans in)
Do you even **actually fucking remember**?

**CREMEANS**  (raises an eyebrow)
I remember **everything**.

**JEREMY**  
That’s what they say right before they hand you a napkin with “maybe Coldplay?” written in crayon.

**CREMEANS**  
If you want the list, I have it.  It’s in the **green folder** back at the hotel.  With the **alternate routing proposals** and **our 1099s**.

**JEREMY**  
I swear to God, if you bring me a list with **Semisonic** on it—

**CREMEANS**  
Semisonic is opening for **Matchbox Twenty** in Denver.

**KATHY**  
He’s right. I saw the flyer.

**JEREMY**  
Jesus Christ. We’re living in **Y2K pop purgatory**.

**GILLEY**  
We’re living in a time when **Cremeans** is the only one with **receipts**.  Let the man retrieve the **holy folder**.

**CREMEANS**  
Give me **ninety minutes** and a real espresso.  You’ll have a list of names that can **fill Atlanta** or at least **fake it well enough.**

**KATHY**  
Bring the folder.  Bring the truth.

**JEFF**  
And bring syrup.  We’re out.

*Cremeans exits like a man on a sacred quest.*  *Jeremy watches him go, muttering something about “folder mythology” and “the gospel according to routing sheets.”*

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL HALLWAY – 9:10 A.M.**

**Cremeans** is walking with purpose but the gait of a man who hasn’t slept and knows **he will never catch up** with the data.  His blazer is wrinkled.  His briefcase is three pounds heavier than it should be because it’s full of **stuff he already memorized**.  And he’s mumbling.  To no one. To the universe. To the gods of PalmPilots and broken promises.


**CREMEANS**  (quietly, bitterly)  
One day…One day I’d love to have all this information at my fingertips.  Like a **real digital assistant**.  Not one of those **fake-ass Newtons** with a stylus that thinks “venue logistics” means I’m ordering a sandwich.

*He stops at the elevator, jabs the button like it owes him royalties.*

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**  
We’re talking about what—**eight, maybe nine kilobytes**? Just to store the **top twenty arena-capable acts in Q1**?  Should fit on a flippin' **floppy disk**. ---

*The elevator dings. He steps inside.*

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**  
But no.  No, let’s **print everything**.  Let’s keep our **financial future** in a **green folder with a Velcro flap** like we’re running a lemonade stand.

*Doors close. He exhales hard.*

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**  
Somewhere out there, Steve Jobs is smiling.  And I hope he chokes on a stylus.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL LOBBY – 10:41 A.M.**

The **automatic doors slide open**.  In walks **Jeff Cremeans**.  Shoulders back.  Eyes forward.  And in his hands?  **The green folder.**Not bent.  Not smudged.  **Perfect.**  He walks with the posture of a man who **won a war with bureaucracy**.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 10:45 A.M.**

**Kathy**, **Jeremy**, **Bill**, and **Gilley** are half-lounging, half-napping around **Jeff**, who’s still picking at the last remains of his waffle like it’s sacred.  The door opens.  Cremeans steps in like he’s **presenting the Ten Commandments**.  He lifts the folder **over his head**.

**CREMEANS**  
**List retrieved.**

**JEREMY** (dramatic gasp)  
He **lives**!

**KATHY**  
Did you actually bring names, or just more laminated heartbreak?

**CREMEANS** (straight face)  
Twenty-seven possible openers.  Broken down by:

* **Availability**
* **Draw capacity**
* **Technical compatibility**
* And “**will they explode mid-tour**” risk factor.

*He opens the folder with a satisfying **rip of Velcro**. The room goes quiet.*

**GILLEY**  
That sound is better than a bass drop.

**CREMEANS**  
Now.  Let’s build Atlanta.

*The band leans in. This is the moment.*  *The first real step toward **January 4th, Atlanta, Resurrection Night.***  *And they’re holding it in their hands.*

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 10:46 A.M.**

The green folder is open on Cremeans’ lap, its contents **color-coded**, **tabbed**, and **borderline sacred**.  The band leans forward—sleep-deprived, vaguely greasy, and now suddenly **dead serious**.  **Kathy** locks eyes with him.

**KATHY**  
Okay.  So.  Who’s at the **top of your list**, Cremeans?

**CREMEANS** (slow nod)  
Top of the list.  Most viable.  **Guaranteed draw.**  Big enough to pack seats.  Not so big they eclipse us.

**JEREMY**  
Don’t say Hootie. I swear to God.

**CREMEANS**  
No.

He flips the first page like a magician doing a reveal.

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**  
**The Foo Fighters.**

*Silence.*  Just for a second.  Then:

**JEFF**  
Holy shit.

**GILLEY**  
That’s either **insane** or **perfect**.

**BILL**  
Depends if Dave’s in a **garage band mood** or a **stadium god mood**.

**KATHY**  
He’s got presence.  He’s got chops.  He’s got a **drummer’s brain with a frontman’s charisma**.

**CREMEANS**  
He’s got **availability**.  They’ve got a **gap** between Christmas and mid-January.  No tour booked.

**JEREMY**  
You’ve already called their people, haven’t you?

**CREMEANS**  
I left a message.  Didn’t say what for.  Just said:  “We’re looking for **resurrection-level energy** in Atlanta.”

**KATHY**  
God, that’s actually **sexy**.

**JEFF**  
If he says yes, it won’t be a show.  It’ll be **a goddamn baptism**.

They all look at each other.  It’s not a commitment.  Not yet.But it’s **a direction**

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 10:49 A.M.**

Cremeans still has the **green folder open** like a war map.  Everyone’s riding the emotional high of **"Foo Fighters: Resurrection Night."**  Then **Kathy** cuts through it with a surgeon’s clarity.

**KATHY**  
Okay.  **Foo Fighters** would be epic.  No argument.  But hey, Jeff— What’s **Plan B**?

*Jeff looks up from his now-devoured waffle. Wipes his mouth. Swallows the last sip of coffee.*  He leans back.  Eyes narrow.  The room quiets.

**JEFF**  
Plan B?

*He taps his fingers once on the plastic tray like a metronome. Then:*

**JEFF (CONT’D)**  
**Queens of the Stone Age.**

*The room breathes in.*

**JEREMY**  
God, that’s…  *actually brilliant.*

**GILLEY**  
They’re dark enough to keep the mood real—Loud enough to **blast the dust off the rafters**.

**BILL**  
Plus Josh Homme’s got **that edge**.  Like he’ll either play a perfect set or burn the stage down and call it art.

**KATHY**  
Okay.  That’s **a viable Plan B**.  Are they touring?

**CREMEANS** (tapping notes)  
Limited U.S. dates.  But they’re in **New Orleans** the week before.  Technically a van ride from Atlanta.  If they say yes, we can **stack it** right.

**JEFF** (quietly)  
I want the show to feel like we **almost didn’t make it**—Then we **did**, and **took the whole damn city with us.**

**JEREMY**  
You get Queens for that.  That’s resurrection with a side of **murder ballad guitar tone**.

**KATHY**  
Okay, Cremeans.  Make those calls.  One to the **halo**, one to the **hellfire**.  Let’s see who wants to raise the dead in Georgia.

*They all sit back. Foo Fighters. Queens of the Stone Age.*  
*Either way, the resurrection show just became **unmissable**.*

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL – 11:02 A.M. – CARDIOLOGY FLOOR LOBBY**

The elevator dings open.

**Sarah Malcolm** steps out—**flushed**, slightly **out of breath**, but **gathered** in every other conceivable way.

* Hair twisted up in a way that says "I’m late but still winning."
* Press badge tucked discreetly in her pocket.
* One brow just slightly arched as she scans the hallway.
* And that little **twinkle** in her eyes that means she’s already **calculated who to smile at and who to steamroll.**

She’s got a **clip-on mic** in her bag.  A backup **MiniDisc recorder**.  And about nine years of **quiet leverage** stashed in invisible folders.

**SARAH (to herself, low)**  
Let’s see who panics first.

*She spots the nurse station, flashes a soft, polite smile, not too eager.*

**SARAH**  
Hi— I’m here to see **Jeff Evans**.  I’m with the **press**, but I’m also on the **internal contact list**.

**NURSE**  
Name?

**SARAH**  
**Sarah Malcolm.**

**NURSE** (squinting)  
You’re not the one who said you were his—

**SARAH** (just sweet enough)  
That would be someone else. I’m just the one with **all the questions.**

*She turns. Scans. Sees the door. The band. The moment.  And smiles.  Because she’s just walked into **a goldmine**.  And Gilley?  He can feel her **before** he sees her.*

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 11:04 A.M.**

The door opens.  **Sarah Malcolm steps in**—the air shifts slightly.  She’s flushed from movement, but **collected**.  Her bag is slung casually over her shoulder, lips parted just slightly in **soft urgency**.  The band looks up like a single organism that’s just spotted a **predator in soft cashmere**.

**SARAH** (sweet, efficient)  
Hey.  Sorry to crash the… post-trauma breakfast club.  But I heard rumors and figured I’d rather **hear it from you** than from someone’s **intern at Island**.

**KATHY** (flat)  
Well, Sarah.  You always did know how to knock gently and titty-twist hard.

**SARAH**  
Just here to **check in**.  No mic.  No notes.  Just… eyes and ears.

*She surveys the room, clocking everything:*

* **Jeff’s plate**: cleaned. Good appetite \= decent condition.
* **Kathy’s posture**: tense but alert \= defensive leadership mode.
* **Gilley**: pretending to not care \= very interested.
* **Cremeans**: hovering over a folder \= something big in motion.
* **Jeremy**: leaning back \= exhausted, slightly reactive.

She files it all away.  Then, she smiles.

**SARAH (CONT’D)**  
Jeff, you look… Well, not dead.  So I guess Island can cancel the **panic parade**.

**JEFF**  
Just needed breakfast.  And a **small resurrection**.

**SARAH** (tilting her head, soft)  
So what happened?

**JEFF**  
I passed out.  They ran tests.  I’m still here.  That’s the whole story.

*She doesn’t believe that for a second.*  *But she doesn’t challenge him.*

Instead, she shifts. Walks a little closer. Places her bag down. Loosens her jacket.  Just **enough movement** to suggest **comfort, availability, approachability**.

**SARAH**  
If anyone wants to **fill in the blanks**, I’ll be downstairs in the **coffee pit**.  Or the hallway.  Or wherever the **truth gets bored enough** to talk.

*She makes eye contact with no one for too long—especially not Gilley.*  *Then steps back toward the door.*

**SARAH (CONT’D)**  
I’m around.  And I’m not in a rush.

*She exits smoothly, like someone who knows the story will come to her if she just **waits long enough** and **smiles at the right moment**.  And Gilley?  **He’s already thinking.**

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 11:11 A.M.**

**Sarah’s exit** still hangs in the air like leftover perfume and tension.  The room’s quiet again, the mood tentative.  And then—**Gilley speaks**.  Softly. Deliberately.

**GILLEY**  
I gotta say—I’m pretty firmly in favor of **Plan A**.

*Everyone glances his way.*

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
You know.  **Day Raw.**

**JEREMY**  
You mean **Dave Grohl**?

**GILLEY**  
Whatever.  I call him **Day Raw** when I want to sound cool and mysterious.

**KATHY**  
You sound like a fan trying to buy bootlegs at the wrong merch tent.

**GILLEY**  
Be that as it may…**Foo Fighters.**  That’s the **ticket**.

*He’s standing now, moving slowly—like a stage performer casually crossing into his light.*

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
That’s the kind of band that makes people **pay attention**.  It makes a **press cycle spin**.  It makes the **industry whisper** and the fans **show up two hours early**.

*He lets that hang.*  Then he moves closer to **Kathy**, casual. Drops a hand to her shoulder like he’s just being supportive—but it’s a **tactic**. Proximity equals persuasion.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
I mean, no offense to **Queens**—But **Plan A**?  That’s got legs.  That’s got **legacy**.  And that’s got **drums that announce resurrection**.

**BILL**  
It’s hard to argue with that.

**CREMEANS**  
He’s not wrong.  The **metrics** alone favor Plan A.

**JEFF**  
And I wouldn’t mind watching Grohl from side stage.  He’s still got the **juice**.

*Gilley nods once. Then glances at his watch.*

**GILLEY**  
Cool.  Just wanted to put that out there.  Y’all talk amongst yourselves.

*He backs up. Smooth. Unrushed.*

**He’s baited the room.**  **He’s gotten the lean.**  **And now?**  **He’s almost free.**

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL HALLWAY – 11:14 A.M.**

**Gilley** exits the hospital room, robe still hanging off his frame like he owns every hallway in America.

He doesn’t walk fast.  He **listens**.  To the shift in **air pressure**, to the squeak of **leather soles** on tile, to the subtle hush that follows someone who **knows she’s not supposed to be there**, but walks like she is.

Then—**He smells it**.  The subtle trace of something citrus.  Sharp. Smart. Dry.  **Sarah Malcolm.**  And he smiles.

**GILLEY (under breath)**  
There you are.

*He rounds the corner, slow like a cat in sun.*  *She’s near the vending machines.*  *Pretending to read a hospital brochure she’s already memorized.*

She doesn’t look up.  She doesn’t have to.  She knows he’s there.

**SARAH**  
So.  Is this where we pretend to **run into each other**, or do we admit the timing’s **perfect**?

**GILLEY** (smiling)  
I tracked your **scent**.  You wearing the **one for betrayal and opportunity**?

**SARAH**  
It’s called **"Editor’s Cut."**  It’s discontinued.

**GILLEY**  
Tragic.  But effective.

*They stand there, five feet apart, like two assassins who both left their knives at home on purpose.*

**SARAH**  
So.  How dead is he?

**GILLEY**  
On a scale of 1 to tabloid meltdown?

He’s **resurrected.**  
Breakfast was the turning point.

**SARAH**  
Then I suppose the **real story** is what happens next.

**GILLEY**  
That depends.  How much are you paying for a **sneak peek**?

**SARAH**  
Information isn’t always bought with money.

**GILLEY**  
Believe me.  I remember.

*They lock eyes.*  *There’s a **game** here, and it’s already started.*

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL HALLWAY – NEAR VENDING MACHINES – 11:17 A.M.**

**Sarah** crosses one ankle over the other, calm, posture flawless, brochure folded neatly in her lap.  **Gilley** leans beside the water fountain, arms folded, jaw tight.

**GILLEY**  
So.  What’s on offer?

*Sarah doesn’t blink.*

**SARAH**  
Same as always.

(slow)
**Same as always.**

*Gilley shifts, exhales slowly.*

**SARAH (CONT’D)**  
I’ve got a **hotel room**.  I’m not **staying long**.  But I am, for now, **ready to fuck**.

**GILLEY** (quiet, watching her carefully)  
And in exchange?

**SARAH**  
Just like always—**You talk**.

*She leans in slightly, not seductive—**intimate**. Like she’s speaking at a confession booth.*

**SARAH (CONT’D)**  
But this time, you keep it **extremely careful**, Jeremy.  This is a **high-tension moment** between all of you.  If you overplay, if you say too much, if someone **suspects** something—The comeback dies **before it opens**.

**GILLEY** (smirking, but cold)  
You think I don’t know how to walk a wire?

**SARAH**  
I think you like to jump off it for fun.

*They lock eyes. The game is ancient. But the rules are new.*  **This isn’t casual anymore.  This is about control.  Narrative.  Positioning.**

And Gilley?  He’s in.  But he’ll play it **precisely.**

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL HALLWAY – 11:21 A.M.**

Gilley leans just slightly forward now, voice low, eyes calm.

**GILLEY (INTERNAL)**  
She has something I want.  And I have something **she wants**.  And so I give it to her.  
Not all at once.  Never the good stuff.

*He watches her smile slightly—just a flicker of lip. She knows what’s coming, but **not when**. That’s the magic.*

**GILLEY (INTERNAL)**  
She wants the inside scoop.  The real story.  The fracture line.  But **not yet**.  Not until she’s paid.  Not until I’m **inside her** and she’s too far in to **pull back** clean.

*He studies her.*  *Sarah’s cool, composed, surgical.*  *But there’s always a flicker in her—**want** dressed as control.  That’s the space he plays in.*

**GILLEY (INTERNAL)**  
This thing works because it’s **illicit**.  Because no one knows.  Because it would **destroy reputations** if anyone did.  But she’s got **leverage**, and so do I.  We trade.  We **dance**.
We get away with it.  And we **love getting away with it**.

*Sarah leans her head slightly, waiting.*  The signal.  The unspoken: *your move.*

Gilley straightens.

**GILLEY**  
Tonight?

**SARAH**  
Five o'clock. Suite. Top floor.  Corner room.

**GILLEY**  
Bring your **questions**.

**SARAH**  
Bring your **good lies**.

*They don’t shake hands. They don’t confirm.  But it’s done.  And by the time she gets what she wants?  He’ll already be halfway into her.*

---

## **INT. NURSE’S STATION – 11:24 A.M.**

**Dr. Lang** stands with a chart in one hand and a disposable coffee cup in the other.  He’s not in a hurry, but there’s something relaxed in his posture—like the weight’s finally lifted.  He flips through a few pages, nods to himself.  **Jeff’s nurse**, a sharp-eyed 30-something named **Nina**, waits beside him, arms folded.

**DR. LANG**  
CT scan came back.  Pretty damn normal.

**NINA**  
Define “pretty damn.”

**DR. LANG**  
No signs of hemorrhage.  No tumor.  No swelling.  No anomaly in the ventricles.  No post-concussive flare.  Everything’s **clean**.

**NINA**  
So… this was a **vasovagal dump**, then?

**DR. LANG**  
That’s my working theory.  Massive fatigue.  Poor hydration.  Stress index through the roof.  He collapsed.  His body said *"hell no."*

**NINA**  
And now he’s eating waffles and booking a resurrection tour.

**DR. LANG**  
Modern medicine is a mystery.

*He scribbles a note in the file, then underlines it.*

**DR. LANG (CONT’D)**  
Let the band know.  No cause for alarm on the **CT front**.  Jeff’s **clear**.

*Outside the nurse station, down the hallway, a door creaks open.*  **Jeremy** steps into view, still sipping cold coffee, unaware he’s about to hear the first **truly good news** in days.\*

---

## **INT. NURSE’S STATION – 11:27 A.M.**

**Dr. Lang** is still reviewing Jeff’s chart, his brow furrowed in the satisfied way of a man who doesn’t need to explain another worst-case scenario.  **Nurse Nina** flips through the schedule on a clipboard, then glances up—dry, skeptical, and amused.

**NINA**  
Okay, real question, Doctor—How long do we **keep this guy under observation**?  Because his **wife is here**, and he has already **hit on half the women** on this floor.

**DR. LANG** (pauses)
Half?

**NINA**  
I’m being generous.

**DR. LANG**  
That include admin?

**NINA**  
It includes **volunteers** and **the woman who refills the vending machines**.

*Dr. Lang snorts into his coffee.*

**DR. LANG**  
Alright.  Let’s say…We keep him another **twenty-four hours**, just to be sure.  Cardiac rhythm’s back to baseline.  Vitals are stable.  And if we don’t let him out soon, he’s going to **proposition a radiologist**.

**NINA**  
He already tried.

**DR. LANG**  
Of course he did.

**NINA**  
His wife didn’t blink.

**DR. LANG**  
Then she’s either **very secure**—  Or she’s got someone on **speed dial**.

**NINA**  
I’m not betting either way.

*They nod. Unspoken consensus: keep him one more day, hand him back to the chaos that raised him, and hope the **press release** doesn’t include **Nina’s name.***

---

## **INT. JEFF’S HOSPITAL ROOM – 11:30 A.M.**

**Jeff** is sitting up in bed, tray empty, IV line still in, hair flattened on one side like he fought a pillow and lost.  There’s a small **plastic hospital mug** of lukewarm coffee on the bedside table.  But Jeff?  He has **his eye** on something **better**.  **NURSE TANYA** (mid-30s, no-nonsense, already seen too much) walks in with a vitals tablet.

**JEFF** (smiling like a man who knows exactly what he’s doing)  
Hey, Tanya.

**TANYA**  
Mr. Evans.

**JEFF**  
Do you happen to know if the **coffee gods** are feeling generous today?

**TANYA** (sighs, already tired)  
You already got your one cup.

**JEFF**  
I’m a recovering… artist. I need a **second wind**.  For creativity.  And glucose stability.

**TANYA**  
You had a waffle the size of Delaware.

**JEFF**  
And I spiritually processed it.  I’m ready for **act two**.

**TANYA**  
You trying to flirt your way into another coffee?

**JEFF**  
Not flirt.  **Negotiate**.

*Tanya raises an eyebrow. Crosses her arms.*

**TANYA**  
What’s in it for me?

**JEFF**  
A backstage pass to the greatest **post-near-death-tour** in the Southeast.

**TANYA**  
Where I’d have to **hear you** play?

**JEFF**  
In a private lounge. With air conditioning. And probably a **cheese tray**.

*Tanya eyes him like he’s part golden retriever, part habitual line-stepper.*

**TANYA**  
I’ll see what I can do.  But if I find out you’re caffeinated and climbing the furniture, I’m cutting you off for life.

**JEFF**  
Understood.  One cup.  No climbing.  Maybe **light stretching**.

*Tanya rolls her eyes and exits. Jeff leans back, hands behind his head like he just sold out Madison Square Garden.*

**JEFF (to himself)**  
Still got it.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 11:35 A.M.**

**Jeff** is smugly sipping his second coffee like a man who just talked his way into dessert before lunch.  The door opens.  **His wife** steps in, arms folded, purse strap over her shoulder, expression reading: *“I’ve been watching everything.”*

She surveys the room: Jeff in bed like a royal.  Crumbs on the tray.  Band members drifting in and out like hallucinations.  She raises an eyebrow.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
So.  Question.  Would it be acceptable for **His Majesty** to use the **private shower**, or is that going to trigger an **alarm**, or bring down the **wrath of Nurse Tanya**?

**JEFF** (grinning)  
Do I smell?

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
You smell like **syrup, ego, and recycled air**.

**JEFF**  
That’s just the new cologne. It’s called **“Coma Light.”**

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
That’s not funny.

**JEFF**  
You laughed a little.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
I smirked. That’s different.  So?  **Shower or not?**

**JEFF** (genuinely thoughtful)  
If I can stand, and the floor isn’t made of tile designed by cartoon villains, I’d love a shower.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
I’ll talk to the nurse.  And for the record— I don’t trust you unsupervised near the **waterproof call button.**

**JEFF**  
I make one soap joke and suddenly I’m a liability.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
You make **ten** soap jokes. In **four minutes.**

---

## **INT. NURSE’S STATION – 11:40 A.M.**

**Nina**, the assigned nurse on rotation, is typing vitals into the system when **Jeff’s wife** walks up—calm, cool, purse still over her shoulder like a weapon.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
Hi.  Quick question—Is it a problem for Jeff to use the **private shower**?

*Nina pauses. Looks over the screen, then looks up.*

**NINA**  
Not a problem, assuming he’s **steady on his feet**.  Vitals have been solid.  Dr. Lang didn’t put any mobility restrictions in place.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
Great.  And if it **were** a problem—would it be acceptable if I just **showered with him** to make sure he didn’t slip?

*Nina blinks. Just once. Then nods slowly, professionally.*

**NINA**  
That would be within reason, yes.

You’re listed as his primary contact and spouse.

We just ask that he not stay in longer than **fifteen minutes**, and that you notify us **before** so we don’t mark him as out of room.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
Understood.

(slight pause)
Also…**When is he medically cleared to resume sexual activity?**

*Another pause. A long one.*  Nina sets the keyboard aside. Pulls up the chart. Straightens her back like she’s reading a disclaimer at a pharmaceutical trial.

**NINA**  
No cardiovascular abnormalities.  Normal CT scan.  Stable vitals.  Slept through the night.  Fully alert.

(beat)
He can resume **sexual activity** when he’s **comfortable**— And when his **partner** is confident he’s **not going to fall off a bed or pass out during the act**.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
Great.

(small smile)
I’ll be the judge of that.

*Nina, entirely unphased, nods once and returns to her chart.*

**NINA**  
Just leave the call button nearby.  In case he gets…overambitious.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
Oh, he will.  That’s the problem.

*She turns, calm, decisive, walking back to Jeff’s room like she’s just negotiated a ceasefire.*

---

## **INT. JEFF’S HOSPITAL ROOM – 11:45 A.M.**

**Jeff** is reclined, coffee in hand, looking pleased with himself and clearly plotting something smug and inappropriate.  The door opens.  **His wife** walks in—composed, in control, and carrying a folded towel like it’s a warrant.  She closes the door behind her. Locks it.  Jeff raises an eyebrow.

**JEFF**  
Well, hello there.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
Don’t.  Just—don’t.  Here’s what’s happening.

(she sets the towel down, begins pulling the curtain)

**JEFF’S WIFE (CONT’D)**  
We’re going to the **private shower**.  You are going to **strip**, and you are going to get a **handjob**, and that is **all**.

*Jeff chokes slightly on his coffee.*

**JEFF**  
Wait—what?

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
Because you need the **edge taken off**, and if I let you keep operating at this level of **sexual voltage**, you’re going to end up flirting your way into **a lawsuit**, and the band doesn’t need that right now.

**JEFF**  
That’s… oddly strategic.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
Yes.  Because everything with you is either **a press conference or a crime scene**, and I’m not letting this be **either**.

**JEFF**  
Just a handjob?

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
Correct.  No theatrics.  No ego.  No press pass.  You get exactly one **medical-grade release**, and then you stop looking at nurses like they’re **backup singers**.

*Jeff opens his mouth to reply, then closes it.*  *Thinks better of it.*  *He sets the coffee down.*

**JEFF**  
Well.  When you put it like that… I suppose I’d better get undressed.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
Correct answer.  Strip. Let’s go.

*She pulls the curtain fully closed.*  *This is not romance.*  *This is **recovery with discipline**.*
And Jeff?  For once?  He **shuts up and follows instructions.**

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL – PRIVATE SHOWER ROOM – 11:50 A.M.**

**Steam curls** around the edges of the frosted glass door. The hospital-grade shower is clean, tiled, institutional—nothing sexy about it. Just **sterile white** and **hot water**.

**Jeff** steps under the spray first, groaning softly at the heat on his back.  He leans against the wall with both palms, head down, eyes closed. There’s no music. No laughter. Just water and breathing.

Behind him, his **wife** steps in. Naked. Quiet. Focused.  She doesn’t say anything.  Doesn’t make it sentimental.  She just **reaches around** him, finds him already **half-hard**, and **starts to stroke**.  No ceremony. No kiss.  Just **motion**, timed with breath.  **Jeff shudders once.**

The water keeps running. His hand finds the tile and braces harder.

It’s **intimate**, but it’s **not tender**.  It’s functional. Direct.  She keeps her face neutral. Focused.  
He finishes in less than a minute—quietly, without a word—shoulders twitching once.  She rinses her hand in the water.  He exhales.

They stand there for a moment.  Not lovers. Not enemies.  Just two people **managing the body**. She kisses his **shoulder blade**, once.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
There.  You’re not going to **implode the staff** now.

**JEFF** (low)  
Thank you.

She steps out first. He lingers in the water.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL – PRIVATE SHOWER ROOM – 12:03 P.M.**

**Steam hangs thick** in the room. The walls drip. The drain gurgles.  The silence is heavy, broken only by the sound of running water and **soap lather** being squeezed out of a hospital dispenser.

**Jeff** stands under the water, rinsed, used, not especially glorious.  **His wife** stands outside the spray, arms folded, watching him with the **calculated stillness of a hawk**.  She is not smiling.  She is not joking.  She is not leaving.

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
Start with your **hair**.

**JEFF** (surprised)  
Okay—

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
Lather it. **Real shampoo.**  Don’t just splash and pretend.

*Jeff nods, grabs the small bottle, starts scrubbing.*  She **watches every motion**.  Her eyes follow the foam down his scalp, down his neck.

**JEFF’S WIFE (CONT’D)**  
Now your **pits**.  Both. Get under your arms.  Lift them.  I swear to God, Jeff, I will scrub them myself if I think you’re half-assing this.

**JEFF**  
I’m doing it—

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
Then **do it better**.

*Jeff lathers up again, more thoroughly. She steps forward slightly, inspecting without touching.*

**JEFF’S WIFE (CONT’D)**  
Now your **dick**.  You just came, and I’m not having the nurses walk in here wondering why the hospital smells like **ejaculate and citrus soap**.

**JEFF**  
Jesus, okay—

**JEFF’S WIFE**  
Wash it.  All of it.  Underneath.  Rinse.

*Jeff, now silent, does as he’s told.*  She watches him the way someone watches a **cat near a fishbowl**— paranoia and **protective dread** in equal measure.

**JEFF’S WIFE (CONT’D)**  
Now your **ass**.  You reek.  You’ve been laying in a bed for two days.  Don’t half-rinse.  Don’t use the excuse of bad water pressure.

*Jeff scrubs, rinses. He’s **quiet now**. The energy has shifted. This isn’t play anymore.*  She steps in closer, hands out—not to help, but to **brace** in case he sways.

**JEFF’S WIFE (CONT’D)**  
If you so much as **wobble**, I am calling for a walker and strapping you to it with **band merchandise**.  You are not falling.   **Not on my shift.**

*Jeff finishes, rinses off, shuts the water.*  He leans against the wall, exhausted but clean.  She grabs a towel, tosses it to him.

**JEFF’S WIFE (CONT’D)**  
Dry off.  Put your gown back on.  And we are going to walk out of here like **you didn’t just almost get admitted to the morgue**.

And Jeff, still quiet, still stunned, does exactly what she says.  Because he knows this isn’t just about him smelling like shit.  This is about her holding the line—for both of them.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 12:28 P.M.**

**Jeff** walks back into the room, **hair damp**, wearing a fresh gown.  No swagger. No drama. Just **tired eyes** and a strange lightness in his shoulders.  His wife is at his side, quiet, steady.

**The band looks up**. Gilley raises an eyebrow.  Kathy says nothing but watches.  **Jeff** sits down on the bed slowly, towel still in his hand.  He exhales. Long. Cleansing.

**JEFF**  
I feel…**Enormously better.**

(beat)
Not just clean.  Just…From the **scent alone**.  It’s like my brain finally caught up to my body.

*He looks over at his wife.*

**JEFF (CONT’D)**  
I…I love you.

*She looks at him. Not surprised. But she doesn't rush to respond.*

**JEFF (CONT’D)**  
That was…That was unexpected.  That was the furthest thing from my mind and kind.

(quiet)
But that was **wonderful**.

*He doesn’t mean the handjob.*  *He doesn’t even mean the shower.*  *He means the **whole thing**.*  
*The **grounding**, the **presence**, the **refusal to let him spiral**.*

For the first time, Jeff looks not like a rock star—or a patient.  He looks like a man who just **got pulled back from the edge.**

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL WAITING AREA – 11:32 A.M.**

**Kathy** stands slowly from her seat like a marionette with one cut string.  
Her hoodie is twisted, her boots are loosely tied, and her coffee cup has been empty for forty minutes.

She blinks at the clock on the wall.

**KATHY (muttering to herself)**  
It’s like…Eleven-thirty.   And maybe there’s a bus.  And maybe that bus has a… bus. 
That has a bed. That… maybe I could be in.

*She picks up her jacket, doesn’t put it on, just **drapes it across her arm like a blanket she’s not sure how to use.***  She starts walking.  It’s more of a **stagger**, really—like a person escaping an emotional minefield.  She pushes open the doors into the hallway, eyes half-closed.

**KATHY (to herself)**  
If I get in that bunk now…By supper I’ll be…Like… **functional**.  Like a person.

*She rounds the corner—and there’s **Jeremy**, leaning against a vending machine, crumpled coffee cup in hand, squinting at a nutrition label like it contains a metaphor.*

**JEREMY**  
Oh hey—wait, are you—

**KATHY**  (raising a finger)  
Nope.  Don’t. Don’t “hey.” Don’t narrate. Don’t explain.  Just—**don’t**.

*Jeremy opens his mouth. Thinks better of it. Just nods once.*

**KATHY (CONT’D)**  
I want the **bus**. The one that has the **bed**. And I want to be **in it**. And I want to be **gone**.  If I see **another spreadsheet**, I will **bite someone**. 

**JEREMY**  
Copy that. Godspeed, General.

*Kathy keeps walking.*  *Jeremy salutes with the coffee cup, then drops it in the trash like a spent shell casing.*

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL PARKING LOT – 11:40 A.M.**

**Kathy** is already halfway across the lot, moving with the grace of a **sleep-deprived badger**. **Jeremy** exits the building just in time to catch her. He jogs to catch up, but not fast—just **enough to show he’s in**.

**JEREMY**  
Hey.

**KATHY**  
If you say “mind if I tag along,” I will throw you into traffic.

**JEREMY**  
No speech.  No clever remark. Just—Same.

*They walk side by side now, silent, toward the **dark tour bus** parked near the far end of the lot like a **beached whale full of dreams and soundproofing**.*

The heat from the pavement is rising. The hospital behind them is a memory.  The tension? Still thick. But now?  It’s **their time** to shut down.

---

## **INT. TOUR BUS – FRONT LOUNGE – MOMENTS LATER**

They step inside. The air is **cool**, **dim**, and smells faintly of **leather, sleep, and maybe one of Gilley’s weirder candles**.  Neither of them says a word. They split directions without needing to assign bunks.

---

## **INT. BUS BUNK ROW – CONTINUOUS**

**Jeremy** slides into a top bunk.  **Kathy** into a lower one across the aisle.  The curtain closes. The silence is **perfect**. No voices.  No instruments.  No crises. Just **stillness**. And soon, **breathing**.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL WAITING ROOM – 12:10 P.M.**

**Bill** has the tour binder open on a folding table, eyes flicking across a calendar printout covered in highlighter, arrows, and sticky notes.

**Jim** leans over the back of a chair, arms crossed, reading upside-down but completely locked in.

**BILL**  
Alright.  Three and a half weeks off the schedule.

That’s **six shows**.

**JIM**  
Six shows.

(beat)
Do we really want to **bother**?

**BILL**  
Absolutely.  We’re a **blue-collar band**.  That’s always been the thing.  We show up.  
We play.  Somebody paid for those tickets—we’re gonna **ante up**.

**JIM**  
Yeah, sure.  But then we’re **wedging** those six dates into **January and February**, right?
You realize what that means?

**BILL**  
Four shows a week.

**JIM**  
Four shows a week.  Even though we’ll be in the South— You get **one ice storm** and we’re screwed.

*Bill exhales through his nose, starts doing math without needing a calculator.*

**JIM (CONT’D)**  
Picture this, Bill.  What if **overwork** is what put Jeff down in the first place?

**BILL**  
You think it was?

**JIM**  
I think it **was a note**.

(pause)

How do **you** feel doing four concerts a week? Not Giant Stadium-style—  Not like three **blowout megashows** in New Jersey with all your friends watching and the crowd drunk on your mythology. I’m talking **grind work**.  **Atlanta to Tallahassee**.  **Miami to Orlando**.  **Orlando to New Orleans**. That’s **bus life with camera crews**.

**BILL**  (sitting back)  
Yeah. I see what you mean.

*They sit there in the silence for a minute. The weight of decisions. Of pushing a man—of pushing themselves.*

**JIM**  
So we make a choice. Do we **honor the tickets** and burn out our guy again?   Or do we call those six dates what they are—**Collateral from the hit we already took**?

**BILL**  
Can’t just think about fans. Gotta think about **survival**.

*They look at the calendar again.*  *The days aren’t just numbers—they’re **load-ins, buses, wake-up calls, blisters, missed meals**.* They know what they’re talking about.

This is **real life**.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 12:22 P.M.**

The blinds are partially closed. The light has gone soft.  **Jeff** sits up in bed, damp hair pushed back, hospital gown clean, coffee cup on the tray beside him. There’s a rare stillness in him—like all the static has momentarily cleared.

The door opens—quietly.  **Sarah Malcolm** steps in.  No tape recorder, no camera, no bag slung forward.  Just her.  And **Jeff knows what that means**.

**JEFF**  
Well look who’s back.

**SARAH**  
I was in the building.

**JEFF**  
You're never *just* in the building, Sarah.

*She closes the door gently behind her. Walks in. Not casual—**precise**.*

**SARAH**  
You said you wanted a word?

**JEFF**  
Yeah. One word.  Or maybe two.

**SARAH**  
And do I get to ask the first one?

**JEFF**  
Nope.  Today you’re the **question mark**.  Not the **label**.

*She smiles—very faintly. He sits forward a little, elbows on knees.*

**JEFF (CONT’D)**  
So tell me. Why are you really here?

**SARAH**  
Because you're alive.  Because you're interesting. Because the band is standing on a **ledge**, and you're the one who's either going to **jump** or **pull them back**.

**JEFF**  
And you want to know **which way I’m leaning**?

**SARAH**  
I want to know **what story’s forming in your head**.  Because whatever it is, people are going to hear it.  Whether it’s from me…  or not.

**JEFF**  (sitting back, amused)  
You always did have that knife-behind-the-back compliment thing down cold.

*She walks closer, stopping just out of reach.*

**SARAH**  
You always did get sentimental right after almost dying.

**JEFF**  
That’s because **almost dying** is a great time to make **editing choices**.

(beat)
You want a quote?

**SARAH**  
I want **a truth**.  Just one.

*He considers her. Really looks at her.*  Then:

**JEFF**  
I don’t know what the fuck I’m doing next.

*She exhales, slightly. There’s no victory in her eyes. Just mutual recognition. That’s a truth she can work with.*

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL ROOM – 12:25 P.M.**

**Jeff** is still leaning forward, elbows on knees, coffee cooling beside him.  **Sarah** stands just to the left of his bed, arms loosely crossed, weight on one leg, watching him with **clinical care disguised as charm**.

**SARAH**  
Okay, then, Jeff.  That’s a **bold statement**.

*Jeff shrugs a little, trying not to show how heavy it sits.*

**SARAH (CONT’D)**  
What’s gotten into you lately? Because…From what I’ve heard, you’ve been going **on and on** about the most **ridiculous stuff**.

*She steps a little closer. Lowers her voice.*

**SARAH (CONT’D)**  
And now?  You hit me with that?  That’s a **frank admission of defeat**.

**JEFF**  (smirks, dry)  
It’s not defeat. It’s the **pause** before I roll the dice again.

**SARAH**  
No snappy quote?  No metaphor?  No “music is chaos and I’m the chorus”?

**JEFF**  
Not today.

(beat)
Something changed.

**SARAH**  
In you? Or around you?

**JEFF**  
Both.  I think…I think I finally **stopped performing** when there wasn’t a stage.

*Sarah studies him. Her face softens—not in sympathy, but in respect.*

**SARAH**  
That’s dangerous. People liked the performance. They **paid** for the performance.

**JEFF**  
Then maybe they paid for the **wrong guy**.

*They lock eyes for a long second. It’s not romantic. It’s not flirty. It’s **recognition**.*

**SARAH**  
So what now?

**JEFF**  
I let the **band** figure out how to restart the machine. And I figure out…how to come back as **something else**.

*Sarah nods once. She doesn’t write it down. But she doesn’t forget.*

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL CORRIDOR – 12:40 P.M.**

**Sarah** steps out of Jeff’s room, the door gently closing behind her. She walks slowly at first, then picks up pace—heels clicking softly on hospital tile. She doesn’t look back.
Her face is neutral, but her mind? **On fire.**

**SARAH (INTERNAL MONOLOGUE)**  
That was clean.  Too clean. He was composed.  Measured.  **Self-aware.** Jeff Evans hasn’t been **self-aware** in ten years.

She adjusts her coat, passes the nurse station, barely nods.

**SARAH (CONT’D)**  
He’s lying. Not to me, maybe.  Not out loud. But there’s a **disconnect**. That wasn't reflection.  That was a **script**.

She hits the elevator button. Waits.

**SARAH (CONT’D)**  
And if he’s already lying to himself?  That means he’s **about to do something reckless**.  Maybe not today.  Maybe not tomorrow.  But soon.

*Ding.*  The elevator doors slide open. She steps inside.

**SARAH (CONT’D)**  
Let him feel clean.  Let him feel smart.  I’m just **counting down the hours**.

*She doesn’t press a button. She already knows where she’s going.*

---

## **INT. HOTEL ROOM – SARAH MALCOLM’S SUITE – 1:07 P.M.**

The curtains are drawn.  Laptop open.  Mini tape recorder docked to her mic via a cheap adapter.  A **yellow notepad** full of chicken-scratch, half-doodles, timelines, and initials lies across the bed.  **Sarah** is in her blazer still, shoes off, hair down, pacing with a Diet Coke in one hand and **a steel mind** organizing chaos.

She stops.  Hits **RECORD** on her handheld and begins dictating to her **contact in New York**.

**SARAH (DICTATING)**  
Okay.  Preliminary field notes.  Evans situation.

**(beat)**

> [!note]
> Status: **Awake, speaking, eating.**  Vitals stable.  Released from acute care zone.  Clean CT. No further complications **confirmed**.
> 
> Band status: **Radio silent.**  No press outreach.  No scheduled update.  They’ve closed ranks. **Hard.**

What I’ve learned:

> [!note]
> Evans is **not out of the woods** emotionally.  He’s presenting as **clean**, **reflective**, **centered**—Which is exactly what he wants us to think.
> 
> What’s really happening? **Something’s fractured.** He doesn’t know who he is right now, which means he’s dangerous.
> 
> To his band.  To himself.  To **whatever they’re planning next.**

> [!caution]
> **Kathy** is in charge emotionally—barely.  **Cremeans** is in full damage control mode.  **Jeremy** is fraying.  **Gilley** is circling the spotlight like a tiger who thinks he owns it.

> [!help]
> What I suspect: This tour **will restart**.  But it will not be the same.  Evans is going to **reframe himself** somehow.  That means new tone.  New music, maybe.  And if they don't manage it right? It implodes.  Band is playing it like a **comeback**. But this feels more like a **slow-motion detonation**.

> [!todo]
> 
> 1. Follow up with Island—are they prepping an unofficial narrative?
> 
> 2. Keep ears on Grohl negotiations (if rumor is real).
> 
> 3. Secure early access to first show post-hiatus.

She clicks **STOP**.  Stares at her notes.  Then underlines one sentence three times: **Evans is lying to himself. That means I’m on the clock.**

---

## **INT. HOTEL ROOM – SARAH MALCOLM’S SUITE – 1:11 P.M.**

Sarah sets the recorder aside, flips her laptop shut, and moves to the desk.  Her **legal pad** is now joined by:

> [!example]
> * A half-finished **press contacts sheet**
> * A printed **calendar** of postponed and rescheduled tour dates
> * A running list titled **“Narrative Angles (Viable)”**

She writes as she mutters, pinning the shape of the story with every pass.

**SARAH (quietly, to herself)**  
Alright…If Gilley shows up at five—I have three and a half hours. That’s **enough time to prep the outline**, get notes to editorial, and lock down where the **holes** are.

She draws a box around the name:  **ATLANTA – JAN 4 – Resurrection Night**

**SARAH (CONT’D)**  
Need to prep three versions:

> [!note]
> 1. “Evans reborn” — soft, mythic, high-stakes.
> 2. “The band held its breath” — inside angle.
> 3. “Nothing changed” — skeptical, undercut narrative for alternate outlets.


She circles **#2** twice.  That’s the one she wants.  She picks up her phone, opens her calendar, and checks for flagged messages. Nothing official from the band.  Not yet.  She opens a blank draft email to her compadre:

---

**TO:** *reid.stanwick@islandrecords.com*  
**SUBJECT:** *Preliminary Narrative Tracks – Evans / Commuted*  
**ATTACHMENTS:** *audio\_transcript\_smalcolm\_0128.txt*, *field\_notes.pdf*

---

She stares at the blank body. Types:

> [!warning]
> Reid,
> 
> Not ready to file, but wanted to preview a few tracks. The subject is technically healthy—but not steady. There’s an unraveling coming, and the band is shielding it.
> 
> No press access, no statements. I’m working angles.
> 
> Watch January 4.
> 
> – S

She doesn’t send it yet.  Just saves it to drafts. Then she grabs her phone, sets a **silent countdown timer** for **3 hours, 24 minutes**. And next? She opens her **personal notebook**.

**The Gilley file.**

She flips back six pages to her last full log of encounters—dates, cities, emotional tones, post-interaction behavior.  She writes:

> [!note]
> **Baltimore, 2000.**
> 
> Operating at peak confidence. Controls band dynamics. In possession of early scoop—potentially Foo Fighters opening act.  Will trade information, selectively, post-sex.  My goal: establish *pretext* for deeper questions, using emotional leverage only after physical contact is made.  Must remain neutral in tone.  Must appear available, but **not hungry**. He wants to believe I’m still curious.  I need him to believe I’m not dangerous.

She closes the notebook.  Rises.  Moves to the mirror. No makeup yet.  Just the face of a woman **in control of the tempo**.

**SARAH (to her reflection)**  
Let him talk.  Let him think. You’ll get the real story **between the lines**.

---

## **INT. SARAH’S HOTEL SUITE – 1:17 P.M.**

The suite is quiet, save for the soft hum of the air conditioning and the occasional scratch of a pen across a notepad.  Sarah sits cross-legged on the bed now, in sweats, hair up, shirt rumpled in a way that’s intentional but **deceptively casual**.

She’s got three notebooks open, each tagged with **colored tabs**.

* **Red** is past interviews.
* **Blue** is behavioral patterns.
* **Green** is leverage.

She taps her pen once.  Then begins to write under a heading:

> [!important]
> **GILLEY – 5:00 P.M. STRATEGY**
> 
> Primary Goals: Extract clean, *unguarded insight* into:
> * Jeff’s actual medical state (vs. reported)
> * Band power dynamics (esp. Kathy/Gilley)
> * Resurrection Show (logistics, friction, overreach)
> 
> Secondary Goals: 
> - Confirm Grohl rumor.  
> - Determine if *I'm is ahead or behind*.

She pauses, then writes under a new subheading:

> [!success]
> **Emotional Tone to Maintain:**
> * Low warmth, high availability.
> * Curious but not predatory.
> * Soft sarcasm = invitation.
> * Do **not** challenge Gilley directly; let him circle.
> * Mirror his cynicism in small doses.

Sarah underlines “let him circle” twice.  Because she knows him.  **He’ll come in confident**, cocky, almost amused.  He’ll want to control the tempo. She doesn’t need to win.  She just needs him to **drop something real**,  then she’ll **build the rest herself**.

---

**1:39 P.M.**

Sarah stands. Walks to the mirror.  She studies herself—not vanity, but tone.  She tilts her head. Changes expressions. Tries them on like armor. Then she flips on her **portable cassette recorder** and speaks quietly:

**SARAH (TO RECORDER)**  
Prep log, Malcolm, 1:39 P.M.

Re: Evans – likely post-crisis denial.  
Re: Tour – band scrambling.  
Re: Gilley – volatile asset.  
Most dangerous when performing sincerity.

Expected window of vulnerability:  30 minutes into contact.

*Click. She sets it down.*

She takes a long shower. Not for cleansing— for **clearing her head**.  No perfume yet.  
Just water. Sound. Stillness.

---

**2:22 P.M.**

Dressed in a **clean black tee**, fitted but modest, and **jeans that say comfort, not seduction**.  She eats a protein bar. Drinks water. Sits again at her desk.

---

**2:43 P.M.**

She writes three **speculative headlines**:

> [!question]
> 1. *THE REBIRTH OF JEFF EVANS*
> 2. *TOUR OF RESURRECTION: COMEBACK OR COLLAPSE?*
> 3. *THE SILENCE BEFORE THE SETLIST*

---

**3:10 P.M.**

She reviews past text threads with Gilley.

> [!info]
> * Never affectionate.
> * Always coded.
> * No leaks, no risks.

She scrolls through, stops on one from last year: *“Information is like good sex. If it’s too easy, someone’s faking it.”* She smiles. He sent it after Denver. 

---

**3:41 P.M.**

She lays on the bed. Sets her alarm for 4:10. Closes her eyes. Not to sleep.  Just to rehearse the night.

Her next move? To wake, clean, dress sharp,  and greet Gilley at the door with the kind of smile that says: **“I already know what you’re going to tell me.**  **I’m just letting you think it’s your idea.”**

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S POV – WALKING THROUGH HOTEL HALLWAY – 4:58 P.M.**

Gilley walks slow, clean, steady.  Not overdressed. Slim button-down, sleeves rolled. Jeans.  Nothing overt.  But the man **knows what he looks like**.  He’s got a plan.  And it has **nothing to do with giving up power**.  Quite the opposite.

**GILLEY (INTERNAL)**  
She thinks tonight’s about **information**. It’s not. It’s about **cost**.  She’s gonna get her scoop.  I’ve got the bones of it ready.  But she’s going to **work for it**.  Not through questions.  Not through tape.  Through me.  

He stops at the suite door. Looks once down the hall.  Then knocks.  Once.  Twice. Slow. Like punctuation.

### **INT. HOTEL SUITE – 5:00 P.M.**

The lock clicks.  The door opens.  And **Gilley walks in just like smoke**— slow, unhurried, quiet, **coiled with intent**.  He doesn’t speak first.  He lets the silence settle. Lets the room take him in.

His eyes sweep the space once:
* The untouched wine glass.
* The chair half-turned toward the window.
* Sarah, standing still, notebook closed, face unreadable.

**GILLEY**  (smiling just slightly)  
This the part where you offer me a drink? Or just ask how far I’m willing to go?

He walks past her, not waiting for an answer, brushing close enough to **shift the air**.  He doesn’t look back.  He sets his phone on the table. Keys beside it.  Turns.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
Because I’ve got something you want.  And you know how this works. You want it?  **You pay.**

He closes the distance again, just enough to stand in her space. Not touching. Not threatening.  Just **there**. Like pressure.  Like heat.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
And I’m not selling anything easy tonight, Sarah. Not cheap.  Not quick. You want **truth**?  You’re going to **feel it**.

### **INT. HOTEL SUITE – SARAH’S POV – 5:01 P.M.**

**Gilley** is in the room now.  The door clicked shut.  He didn’t raise his voice.  He didn’t pose.  He just **entered**, and the **dynamic shifted** like gravity found a new center.  Sarah hasn’t moved.  She doesn’t need to.  She’s watching him set down his keys, turn to her, stand in her space like he owns it.

And inside?  **Her mind is running.**

**SARAH (INTERNAL MONOLOGUE)**  
He really didn’t…beat around the bush.  He never does.  Not with me. Not when it’s this kind of night.

*She watches him scan the room like it’s a chessboard and he already knows where her king is hiding.*

**SARAH (CONT’D)**  
He didn’t ask how I’m doing.  Didn’t pretend to be tired.  Didn’t ease in with compliments or charm or the usual smoke and mirrors. He just said it. **You want it? You pay.**

*She exhales slowly through her nose. Not nervous—just pacing herself.*

**SARAH (CONT’D)**  
And the worst part is— He’s not bluffing. He has something.  I can feel it.  Under the surface, tucked into the folds of whatever he’s not saying.  Which means I need to be sharp.  And I need to let him think I’m…**movable.**

*She lets her face soften, just slightly. Enough to suggest openness. Not surrender.*

**SARAH (CONT’D)**  
This isn’t about sex.  It never is.  This is about **narrative**.  Power.  **Who gives first.**
And right now?  He’s made his demand. So I have to decide how much I want what’s behind it.  And how much I’m willing to let him think I’ll give.

*She steps closer. Not much. Just enough.*

**SARAH (TO HERSELF)**  
Let’s begin.

---

## **INT. HOTEL SUITE – 5:03 P.M.**

**Gilley** stands still, hands casually in his pockets, watching her like he already owns the room.  And maybe, for now, he does.  **Sarah** has taken a step closer.  Just one.  She looks up at him, jaw relaxed, expression unreadable.  Then—**slowly, methodically**—she reaches for the top button of her blouse.  And undoes it.

Just one. That’s all.

**SARAH**  
I’m not here for easy.

**GILLEY**  
Neither am I.

**SARAH**  
But before you **sell**, I want to know—Why now?

*She unbuttons the second button. Smooth. No flair.*

**SARAH (CONT’D)**  
You’ve had things before.  You’ve dangled stories like they were toys, breadcrumbs, riddles in bars.  But this time? You walked in **direct**.  So tell me—What’s changed?

**GILLEY**  (smiling)  
You want the answer before the payment?

**SARAH**  
No.  I want to know if **you** know the answer.

*Button three. Still slow. Still deliberate. Her blouse is open just enough to change the air in the room, but not enough to give him anything.*  Not yet.

**SARAH (CONT’D)**  
Because I think you’re playing harder this time.  And when you play harder—That usually means **you’re hiding something bigger**.

*Gilley tilts his head. He's amused. Interested. But not rattled.*  Not yet.

**SARAH (CONT’D)**  
So go ahead.  Talk about cost.  But I’m watching **value**.

---

## **INT. HOTEL SUITE – 5:06 P.M.**

Three buttons undone.  Sarah standing still, measured, poised.  She’s mid-trap, halfway into the emotional scaffolding of a setup.  But Gilley sees it.  **Feels it.**  And decides to turn the air **electric**.

**GILLEY**  
You think this is a question?  This—What you’re doing?

*He steps forward, **suddenly too close**.*  *The space between them disappears—**heat**, **breath**, and **intent** all in one line.*

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
You want to know what changed? **You did.** You think you can dangle questions and silk and control the tempo. But here’s the thing, Sarah—This isn’t your interview.

*He lifts a hand—**not touching**, just hovering near her jaw, thumb grazing **air**, not skin.*

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
You came here to play.  But I’m the one who decides how long the game runs.  And if you want **information**? If you want what’s **under the waterline**? You’re going to have to **work** for it.  Not with charm.  Not with questions.  Not with three polite buttons undone like it’s a calculated reveal.

*He finally touches her.*  *Just a single finger at her collarbone—**down**, slow, past the line of the third button.*

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  
I don’t want your angles.  I want **submission**. And then—Maybe. **Maybe** you get a taste of what I’m hiding.

*He pulls back, just enough to breathe.*  Not backing down.  **Applying pressure.** Testing her. Challenging her to keep the game going under **his rules**.

After all, she's the one that's gonna fall .

---

# **FIN**
